1201 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jeanmarie v. Butler


NO. 2005-CA-1439


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1439 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/11/06); 942 So. 2d 578; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2622



October 11, 2006, Judgment Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Jeanmarie v. Butler, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2660 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Civil District Court, Orleans Parish. NO. 2005-2220, Division "M". HONORABLE PAULETTE R. IRONS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, maintained defendant's wife exception of prescription to plaintiff daughter's filiation action. The daughter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The daughter argued that the case should be remanded to allow the parties to specially plead the unconstitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209 and 197, that art. 209 was unconstitutional, and whether art. 197 governed the time limitations for filiation actions that were pending on the effective date of 2005 La. Acts 192. The appellate court noted that the daughter, by failing to amend her pleadings, lost the ability to challenge the constitutionality of the articles. The unconstitutionality of a statute could not be raised in a memorandum, opposition, or brief as those documents did not constitute pleadings. The new law of 2005 La. Acts 192 could not be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1202 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Cooper


NO. 2005 CA 2360


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2360 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/06/06); 945 So. 2d 48; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2232



October 6, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 515,321. Honorable William A. Morvant, Judge Presiding.
State v. Williams, 541 So. 2d 401, 1989 La. App. LEXIS 530 (La.App. 4 Cir., 1989)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant inmate was resentenced for his armed robbery and attempted armed robbery convictions, he petitioned for credit for time served on both sentences. Appellee Department of Public Safety and Corrections denied his petition, and the inmate sought judicial review. The 19th Judicial District Court of East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, denied the inmate relief based on the commissioner's recommendation. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate argued that the trial court's ruling was erroneous because it was based upon an incorrect interpretation by the commissioner of whether the trial court intended to grant him credit for time served on both of his sentences. The inmate maintained that it was the sentencing judge's intent, not that of the Department, which governed the conditions upon which his sentences had to be served. The appellate court agreed, finding that although it was unclear why the trial court resentenced the inmate on the armed robbery count, and no argument was made with respect to the armed robbery count, the minute entry from the original resentencing indicated that the trial court imposed both sentences with credit for time served. Furthermore, the minute entry did not contradict the sentencing transcript.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling was reversed and the Department was ordered to compute the inmate's armed robbery and attempted armed robbery sentence with credit for time served.

 

1203 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spears


NO. 39,302-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,302 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/27/06); 940 So. 2d 135; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2111



September 27, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Spears, 940 So. 2d 135, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2576 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 26, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Spears, 962 So. 2d 424, 2007 La. LEXIS 1846 (La., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Spears v. La., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3124 (U.S., Apr. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court. Originally appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 46498. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.
State v. Spears, 929 So. 2d 1219, 2006 La. LEXIS 1095 (La., Apr. 4, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, convicted defendant of misapplication of construction contract payments, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:202. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and entered a judgment of acquittal. The supreme court remanded the matter for consideration of defendant's remaining assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash the bill of information and motion in arrest of judgment, in which he argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:202 was unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that the activity proscribed by the statute was sufficiently narrow and gave adequate notice to those who would engage in such conduct, i.e., fail to apply monies received pursuant to a construction contract as necessary to settle claims for material and labor, that the conduct was proscribed. Defendant was provided ample time to conduct any further discovery. The trial court did not err in granting a recess where it was satisfied by the State's allegations that defendant had played a role in a witness's failure to appear. Defendant did not show how testimony with regard to his failure to complete the project and the consequences was irrelevant in determining if funds were misapplied. The trial judge did not err in refusing to give defendant's requested jury instructions. The allegations in the information were sufficient to determine the grade of the offense charged. The jury was not required to determine a specific amount of funds misapplied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1204 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Arrington v. ER Physicians Group


NO. 04-1235


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1235 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/27/06); 940 So. 2d 777; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2164



September 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 28, 2006.
Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Arrington v. Galen-Med, Inc., 947 So. 2d 719, 2007 La. LEXIS 322 (La., Feb. 2, 2007)
Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Arrington v. Galen-Med, Inc., 947 So. 2d 727, 2007 La. LEXIS 821 (La., Feb. 2, 2007)
Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Arrington v. Galen-Med, Inc., 947 So. 2d 724, 2007 La. LEXIS 824 (La., Feb. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 97-4329, HONORABLE J. DAVID PAINTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Arrington v. ER Physicians Group, APMC, 897 So. 2d 911, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 593 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, deceased patient's family, challenged a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) that denied their motion for summary judgment, granted summary judgment for defendant hospital, and upheld the constitutionally of the limitation on recovery or "cap" provisions of the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The case was previously before the court, along with another case, in which plaintiffs sought to have the "the cap" or limitations on recovery for damages under the MMA declared unconstitutional. The Louisiana Supreme Court denied the court's request for certification and remanded the cases for the court to consider the appeals. The court held that the current $ 500,000.00 cap failed to provide an adequate remedy and, thus, was unconstitutional under the provisions of La. Const. art. I, § 22, which assured Louisiana citizens of an adequate remedy under the law for injury to their persons. The court found that competent evidence was presented to show that after considering the devaluation of the dollar in the 30 years since the passage of the MMA, the $ 500,000.00 limit imposed in 1975 was worth only $ 160,000.00 and thus did not provide an adequate remedy to today's severely injured plaintiffs. The court found that in order to grant today's plaintiff the same relief the legislature granted to plaintiffs in 1975, the cap would have to be raised to $ 1,562,500.00. Because the court found merit in plaintiffs' "adequate remedy" argument, it did not discuss plaintiffs' other arguments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, based on its finding that the $ 500,000.00 cap on medical malpractice damages were unconstitutional. The court remanded the case to the trial court for the consideration of what constituted adequate damages and assessed all costs of the appeal against defendant.

 

1205 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clements


NO. 04-1069


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1069 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/27/06); 940 So. 2d 796; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2171



September 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Taylor v. Clement, 947 So. 2d 721, 2007 La. LEXIS 323 (La., Feb. 2, 2007)
Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Taylor v. Clement, 947 So. 2d 730, 2007 La. LEXIS 822 (La., 2007)
Writ granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Taylor v. Clement, 947 So. 2d 732, 2007 La. LEXIS 823 (La., Feb. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 99-191, HONORABLE J. DAVID PAINTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Taylor v. Clement, 897 So. 2d 909, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 583 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which denied their motion for summary judgment seeking to have the limitations on recovery for damages imposed by the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq., declared unconstitutional and granting the motion for summary judgment filed by defendant, the Louisiana Patient's Compensation Fund.


OVERVIEW: The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the limitation on recovery or "cap" provisions of the act. On appeal, the court found the $ 500,000 cap on medical malpractice damages, La. Rev. Stat. § 40:1299.42(B), unconstitutional as failing to provide plaintiffs an "adequate remedy" as guaranteed under the provisions of La. Const. art. 1, § 22. The court did not discuss the matter further.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and set aside the judgment and entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs. The court remanded the case to the trial court for the consideration of what constituted adequate damages in plaintiffs' case. The court assessed all costs of the appeal against the Louisiana Patient's Compensation Fund.

 

1206 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dossman


06-449 consolidated with 06-450


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-449 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/27/06); 940 So. 2d 876; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2192



September 27, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Dossman, 2007 La. LEXIS 1355 (La., June 1, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana) of unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. During the trial, the victims both testified that they were inside the structure, which they both called an apartment, at the time of the incident. Defendant admitted in his own testimony that he went to the apartment and pushed the air conditioner through the wall in order to see inside because he wanted to see if one victim was entertaining a boyfriend there. There was no testimony offered at trial to suggest that defendant went to the main house prior to approaching the apartment. Consequently, defendant's actions demonstrated that he went there because he was aware, at least, that the victim spent sufficient time in the apartment and that she would be likely to be found there if she was entertaining. In addition, the victims were actually in the apartment when the episode occurred. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for the offense of unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling was affirmed. However, his sentence of six years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence was amended to delete the denial of parole eligibility, and the trial court was instructed to make an entry in the minutes to reflect that change.

 

1207 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gauthier


NO. 2005-KA-1365


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1365 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/27/06); 941 So. 2d 642; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2634



September 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 1, 2006.
Subsequent appeal at State v. Gauthier, 978 So. 2d 1161, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 361 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 439-741, SECTION "H". HONORABLE CAMILLE BURAS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED AND SENTENCE, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), convicting him of intimidating a witness in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:129.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of intimidating the victim by threatening her verbally and by letter after he was arrested for beating her. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by allowing defendant to represent himself, even though it did not specifically inquire about defendant's educational level and experience or explain the nature of the charges against him or the range of penalties, because the record showed that defendant was sufficiently articulate and intelligent to knowingly and voluntarily waive his right to counsel. From pretrial observations, the trial court could determine that defendant was articulate, that he generally asked relevant questions, that he was respectful in court, and that he was intelligent. Defendant stated in a pretrial hearing that he needed to use the law library at the prison, indicating that he was aware of the procedures followed in the criminal justice system. Defendant's questioning of one of the members of the sanity committee at a pretrial hearing clearly showed that he was well aware of the nature of his plea of not guilty by reason of insanity. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1208 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hughes v. Connick


NO. 06-CA-152


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-152 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/26/06); 942 So. 2d 1076; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2109



September 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 623-077, DIVISION ''O''. HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State ex rel. Hughes v. State, 793 So. 2d 1238, 2001 La. LEXIS 1977 (La., June 15, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-fourth Judicial District, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, granted appellee district attorney's exception of no right of action and res judicata, dismissing appellant inmate's civil petition for declaratory judgment, which alleged the criminal statute under which he had been convicted was unconstitutional. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the trial court granted the district attorney's exceptions without reason when no jurisprudence or statutory authority was cited by the district attorney. The appellate court did not find that the inmate had a right of action, and the claim was barred by res judicata. The inmate had no real or actual interest in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.2B(3) being declared unconstitutional. He was not currently threatened with prosecution under the statute. He had already been convicted of the crime and his conviction and sentence were final. He had no actual, justiciable controversy that would provide him a right of action in the declaratory action. During the criminal proceeding against the inmate, including the post-conviction relief application, writs, and appeals, he did not question the constitutionality of the statute under which he had been charged and pled guilty. His conviction and sentence were now final. Therefore, he was now barred from relitigating this matter by claiming the criminal statute was unconstitutional through this civil action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1209 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruffins


No. 41,033-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,033 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/20/06); 940 So. 2d 45; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2023



September 20, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Ruffins, 940 So. 2d 45, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2577 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 26, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Ruffins, 959 So. 2d 494, 2007 La. LEXIS 1534 (La., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which convicted him of illegal use of a weapon during a crime of violence and illegal possession of a weapon while in possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot his wife as she was attempting to leave him. When police arrived and searched defendant's residence, marijuana was found inside. Defendant was convicted of two charges, and he sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:94 was not unconstitutional as applied. Section 14:94(A) was distinguished from § 14:94(F) because the latter subsection required proof of the additional element of the intentional use of force or violence being used on a victim. That defendant shot the victim while he was intentionally chasing her distinguished his actions from those in § 14:94(A). Moreover, the district attorney had broad discretion in deciding what charges to initiate; therefore, the decision to charge defendant was a crime with a higher penalty did not render the statute unconstitutional. The statute was not vague because there was adequate notice of what conduct was proscribed and the penalty for a violation thereof. Next, the State was not required to prove that a nexus existed between the firearm and drug offense because defendant was in actual possession of the firearm, and proof of actual possession of the drugs was not required.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1210 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 41,449-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,449 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/20/06); 940 So. 2d 61; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2028



September 20, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35-032. Honorable Glenn Fallin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence in the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana for distribution of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant purchased crack cocaine from defendant. The bill of information was filed in December 2000 and defendant made her first appearance in court without counsel in January 2001. After continuances filed by defendant and the State with defendant switching attorneys twice, defendant filed a motion to quash the prosecution in May 2003. The court affirmed, and held that defendant showed no prejudice from the case being transferred to another judge within the same district when the first judge recused himself. The court also held that defendant's filing of a discovery motion triggered the one-year period provided by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. Art. 580, and thus the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to quash in that it gave the state one year from filing on July 9, 2002 to bring the matter to trial. Also, while the trial court did not comply with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, the trial court had not authority to reconsider the sentence because defendant did not file a timely motion to reconsider. Further, defendant's less-than-midrange sentence without a fine was not constitutionally excessive even for a first offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1211 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Staten v. Brown


No. 41,288-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,288 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/20/06); 940 So. 2d 105; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2085



September 20, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Staten v. Brown, 2007 La. LEXIS 1339 (La., June 1, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological father appealed the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, which found that his paternity claim was barred by peremption.


OVERVIEW: Appellant first met the mother in 2000 while she was living with her husband. Two children were conceived during an adulterous affair. The mother told him she was pregnant in July 2002; appellant was positive the child was his because the mother was not having sexual relations with her husband. She lived with her husband until the second pregnancy; then appellant and the mother lived together, and she later moved in with her grandmother. The mother died on December 4, 2004. Appellant knew he was the father of both children, but waited to file a paternity claim until April 20, 2005. The trial court specifically found that he knew of his paternity and was not deceived. His paternity claim was barred by the two-year limitation period set forth in La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 191. Article 191 was not unconstitutional as applied in this case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1212 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chandler


No. 41,063-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,063 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/08/06); 939 So. 2d 574; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1950



September 8, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Chandler, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2574 (La.App. 2 Cir., Sept. 21, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Chandler, 2007 La. LEXIS 1187 (La., May 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 221,852. Honorable John D. Mosely, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 and sentenced him to a mandatory life sentence without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for aggravated rape, but the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's arguments that the closeness of the definitions of the two crimes, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42(A)(2) and 14:42.1(A)(1) tainted the jury's verdict. The jury's prime function of determining the sufficiency of the evidence for a charged crime was fully and correctly exercised. The court further found no error in the trial court's refusal to give a special jury charge regarding the "virtually identical" crime definitions for aggravated and forcible rape. The trial court's charge read the definitions of both crimes and the applicable sentences to the jury and that was sufficient to advise them of the elements of the crimes and, by implication, to inform them of their power to give a responsive verdict of forcible rape. Under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 702, the court found no error in the trial court's acceptance of a sexual assault nurse examiner as an expert based primarily on her actual experience with rape victims. Additionally, defendant's life sentence was not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1213 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Orillion v. Crawford


NO. 2005 CA 0559


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0559 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/1/06); 964 So. 2d 950; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1933



September 1, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, in part, Amended by Orillion v. Crawford, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2462 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 465,864. Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.
Orillion v. Carter, 639 So. 2d 461, 1994 La. App. LEXIS 2040 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 24, 1994)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which affirmed a judgment from the Louisiana Board of Tax Appeals in favor of appellee department of revenue in a dispute over the payment of taxes on interest earned on a personal injury award.


OVERVIEW: A decedent was awarded damages in a personal injury case. The taxpayer, the decedent's wife, paid an Internal Revenue Service assessment on the interest on the award after the decedent's death. When the department assessed the taxpayer for the same, she contended that she owed no taxes on prejudgment interest under Louisiana law. The Board and the trial court disagreed with her position, and she sought review. In reversing, the appellate court held that the district court had authority to review the decision of the Board under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1435, and it was error to sustain an objection of no right of action as to the taxpayer's constitutional issue. However, it was not necessary to determine the constitutional issue raised. The appellate court found that prejudgment interest was excluded from gross income under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:46. It was noted that Louisiana conformed its laws with federal tax law. Under 26 U.S.C.S. § 104(a)(2), prejudgment interest was not excluded as gross income. However, civil law recognized prejudgment interest as an element of damages, pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2000. Therefore, it was treated differently under Louisiana law.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court and the Board were reversed. The case was remanded to the Board with instructions to determine what portion of the interest was prejudgment interest, which was exempt from taxation under Louisiana law.

 

1214 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomas


No. 41,095-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,095 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/23/06); 938 So. 2d 1178; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1831



August 23, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Thomas v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 132533 (W.D. La., Oct. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 214,193. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of two counts of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and imposed concurrent sentences of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The victims were shot and killed during an armed robbery while they worked at a liquor store and defendant was subsequently convicted of two counts of second-degree murder. On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that his role as a principal in the armed robbery was supported by the evidence, in particular, his own statements to police. Those statements established his participation with another individual in planning the armed robbery, including their use of a pistol. Defendant's subsequent statements to his girlfriend and another friend that defendant was involved in the robbery at the liquor store and the testimony of two other individuals clearly established defendant's culpability. The court further stated that the record supported the trial court's finding that defendant clearly and unequivocally initiated, through his family, his desire to talk with officers and validly reversed his earlier hesitancy to speak without counsel. His sentence was appropriate because he was a willing participant in an armed robbery that resulted in the senseless and brutal killing of two men.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1215 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Entrada Co., L.L.C. v. Moore


No. 41,414-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,414 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/09/06); 938 So. 2d 1055; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1645



August 9, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Entrada Co., L.L.C. v. Moore, 2007 La. LEXIS 13 (La., Jan. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35,580. Honorable Jimmy C. Teat, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners challenged a decision from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne (Louisiana), which granted appellee buyer's request for a partition by licitation.


OVERVIEW: The buyer purchased an interest in certain property and sought a partition without allegedly naming several of the owners. They responded to the partition, but the trial court granted a partition by licitation. Thereafter, the owners filed a devolutive appeal. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the trial court properly denied the owners' peremptory exception of non-joinder of an indispensable party under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 641, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 642. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4985 was meant to outline the precise situation which occurred in this case. The fact that one or more co-owners to property was not named in litigation surrounding the case did not affect the validity of a partition to those who were involved in the same litigation. Moreover, the constitution challenges under La. Const. art. 1, §§ 2, 4 and the Fourteenth Amendment were also rejected. The appellate court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4985 was not void for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.


 

1216 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fontenot


NUMBER 06-226


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-226 (La. App. 3 Cir. 07/12/06); 934 So. 2d 935; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1573



July 12, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 15, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 69196-FA. HONORABLE J. LARRY VIDRINE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to molestation of a juvenile, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, and was sentenced to serve eight years at hard labor, two years suspended, and upon release be placed on active supervised probation for three years. The 13th Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana) also found the offense was a crime of violence as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13). Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: First, defendant argued that the court erred in sentencing him as having committed a crime of violence. Molestation of a juvenile, was not listed as a crime of violence in § 14:2(13). However, at least one court had held the list was illustrative, rather than exclusive. Defendant argued there was no evidence that his crime was violent, because no serious bodily injury occurred. At issue was not whether the instant offense was executed in a violent manner, but whether molestation of a juvenile generally, as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, was a "crime of violence," as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13). Molestation was inherently a crime of violence. Such crimes were of a genera that was violent in nature. The trial court did not err by finding defendant committed a crime of violence. Further, defendant did not point to any consequences the designation produced in his sentence. Diminution of the sentence was not affected by the designation, since molestation of a juvenile was clearly a sex offense, and thus was precluded from such diminution, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:537. Also, suspension of sentence was not precluded for a first-offense violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The case was remanded for the trial court to impose the mandatory conditions of probation and a probation supervision fee in accordance. The trial court was also instructed to deny defendant eligibility for diminution of sentence. Lastly, the trial court was instructed to advise defendant of the prescriptive period for filing post-conviction relief.

 

1217 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. King


No. 41,083-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,083 (La. App. 2 Cir. 06/28/06); 935 So. 2d 354; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1437



June 28, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. King, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1890 (La.App. 2 Cir., Aug. 4, 2006)
Writ granted by State v. King, 955 So. 2d 670, 2007 La. LEXIS 1121 (La., Apr. 27, 2007)
Vacated by, in part State v. King, 969 So. 2d 1228, 2007 La. LEXIS 2329 (La., 2007)
Writ denied by State ex rel. King v. State, 2012 La. LEXIS 1860 (La., June 22, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 235,808. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED AND SENTENCE AMENDED; AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which entered judgment on a jury verdict and convicted defendant of armed robbery using a firearm, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. §§ 14:64 and 14:64.3, and which sentenced him, as an adjudicated habitual offender, to 203 years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted for his part in a bank robbery. On appeal, defendant argued, among other things, that the State failed to prove that the 10-year maximum period between offenses, set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, had not expired. In affirming the conviction but amending the sentence, the court first found that the trial court did not err in calculating that the 10-year period between convictions had not elapsed. Next, even though the State failed to provide fingerprint evidence identifying defendant as the person who committed both crimes, the court noted that identity was proved by defendant's own admissions at the armed robbery trial and by the certified bill of information and court minutes from the previous conviction. Finally, the court determined that, although the sentence was not constitutionally excessive, it was illegal in that the trial court improperly applied the five-year enhancement set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.3 because the applicable sentence under the habitual offender law effectively replaced the sentence for the underlying crime under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64 and 14:64.3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, amended the sentence by reducing it by five years, without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence, and affirmed the judgment of sentence as amended.

 

1218 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


NO. 05-KA-951


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


05-951 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/28/06); 934 So. 2d 269; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1470



June 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 2006.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 2007 La. LEXIS 2125 (La., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-304, DIVISION ''C''. HONORABLE J. STERLING SNOWDY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 40th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist, State of Louisiana, convicting him of distribution of cocaine and distribution of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for directing an undercover detective to a drug dealer, from whom the detective purchased cocaine and marijuana. On appeal, the court held that the State proved that defendant was a principal to the sale of drugs to the detective because the jury could have reasonably inferred from a videotape of the transaction and the detective's testimony that defendant had arranged with the drug dealer to assist him in selling narcotics by taking potential buyers to him. Defendant's argument that the trial court erred in denying his challenges for cause as to three prospective jurors and prejudicing him by forcing him to use peremptory challenges to excuse them was rejected because the record showed that defendant had six peremptory challenges remaining when jury selection was completed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's motion in limine, seeking suppression of evidence concerning the drug dealer based on defendant's allegation that the State failed to inform defendant prior to trial that the drug dealer was an alleged co-perpetrator, because it was evident from the State's discovery response attachments that he was the co-perpetrator.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1219 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lande


NO. 06-KA-24


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06 24 (La. App. 5 Cir. 06/28/06); 934 So. 2d 280; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1542



June 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 11, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Lande, 954 So. 2d 154, 2007 La. LEXIS 952 (La., Apr. 20, 2007)
Related proceeding at In re La. v. Lande, 2009 La. LEXIS 1651 (La., June 4, 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Lande v. Cooper, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 52111 (E.D. La., Mar. 20, 2012)
Related proceeding at Lande v. Cooper, 2012 La. LEXIS 754 (La., Mar. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-4759, DIVISION ''L''. HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, II, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, convicting him of two counts of aggravated incest in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1 and indecent behavior with a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, and sentencing him as a multiple offender to 15 years in prison on each count without the benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for sexually assaulting his stepdaughter. On appeal, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1 was not unconstitutionally vague because the offenses of incest and aggravated incest were self-contained, and § 14:78.1 specifically listed the prohibited acts and clearly defined those persons to whom the proscription applied. The court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence was insufficient on the ground that the State failed to prove his status as the victim's stepfather at the time of the acts because the victim consistently testified that she was around eight or nine when the incidents occurred and that they occurred after defendant married her mother in July 2001. The evidence was also sufficient to support defendant's conviction of indecent behavior with a juvenile because lewd and lascivious behavior was established. Defendant showed the victim sexually explicit shows immediately prior to making her "rub his private part until white stuff came out." The victim's description of what she saw on television, "naked people having sex," effectively conveyed material that sufficiently qualified as an indecent sexual display.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The trial court was ordered to inform defendant of the sex offender registration requirements by sending written notice to him within 10 days.

 

1220 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Pelts & Skins, L.L.C. v. La. Dep't of Wildlife & Fisheries


2005 CA 0952


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0952 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/21/06); 938 So. 2d 1047; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1394



June 21, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Pelts & Skins L.L.C. v. 939 So. 2d 1281, 2006 La. LEXIS 3024 (La., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 523,294. Honorable Wilson Fields, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alligator farm alleged that appellee department of wildlife collected tag fees on alligators and alligator skins shipped out of state, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 56:253C(2)(a), and 56:256, and that the statutes were unconstitutional. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) found the statutes constitutional and granted the department's exception of no cause of action. The farm appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the Commerce Clause/Complete Auto analysis, the failure to tax all raw hides, if proven, could have been found to have been an unfair apportionment of the tax and a discriminatory burden on interstate commerce. Similarly, under the Michelin analysis, a discriminatory tax could have been found to have violated the Export-Import Clause by singling out exportation and discouraging it in a manner inconsistent with federal policy. Thus, the farm sufficiently stated at least one basis for its cause of action asserting constitutional challenges. If the farm proved that fees and taxes were levied or collected on the skins themselves while "in transit," the exaction might initially qualify as a per se violation of the Import-Export Clause, whether or not the Michelin analysis applied. Under the "stream of export" doctrine, or as a discriminatory burden on interstate commerce, a levy on any goods themselves while in transit could likely have violated the Commerce Clause as well. Thus there were instances where, based solely on the factual allegations taken as true, analyzed under the wording of the statutes and applicable law, the company had sufficiently stated a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded. The costs of the appeal, $ 480, were assessed to the department.

 

1221 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jim Walter Homes, Inc. v. Guilbeau


NUMBER 05-1473


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1473 (La. App. 3 Cir. 06/21/06); 934 So. 2d 239; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1403



June 21, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 15, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION - # 4. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 03-03427. SHARON MORROW, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A workers' compensation judge (WCJ) in the Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC), No. 4, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana) found that appellant claimant had made a willfully false statement for the purpose of obtaining and continuing workers' compensation benefits in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 and that appellee employer unreasonably paid the first week of benefits in a late and untimely manner. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The WCJ found that when the claimant directly stated, under oath, that he could not get up on roofs and could not perform roofing duties, he willfully made a false statement. Given the videotape of his performing roofing duties on a roof, in direct contradiction to his sworn statement, the judgment that the claimant was in violation of § 23:1208(A) as of the date of that statement, and that he should suffer the forfeiture of any benefits accruing under the workers' compensation statute from that point forward as required by § 23:1208(E), was not in error. It was against the purpose of the statute to penalize a claimant retroactively to the date when benefits accrued. Violations yielding forfeiture had to be proven by the one alleging fraud. Unless the one alleging fraud could prove that false, willful statements or representations made to obtain benefits were made when benefits first accrued, forfeiture occurred prospectively from the date of proven violations. Given that the employer could not prove the claimant violated § 23:1208 at the time his benefits first accrued, the WCJ's assessment of a penalty and attorney fees against the employer for late payment was correct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1222 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Caples


2005 KA 2517


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2517 (La. App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 147; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1369



June 9, 2006, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Caples, 2007 La. LEXIS 1163 (La., Apr. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 392189 "A"), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE RAYMOND S. CHILDRESS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Disposition: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress his identification by the victim, his statement, and the evidence. A jury found him guilty of first degree robbery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1. Defendant's motions for a new trial and for a post verdict judgment of acquittal were denied. He moved for reconsideration of his sentence, but the motion was also denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told the victim that he had a knife and to give him his money. Defendant's right hand was underneath his sweater. The victim surrendered his two twenty-dollar bills to defendant because he felt threatened by him. The victim indicated he did not fight back because he was afraid defendant had a knife. The victim believed that defendant had a knife because of the threat defendant had made and due to a hand motion defendant had made underneath his sweater. The evidence thus viewed established that defendant induced a subjective belief in the victim that defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon and that the victim's belief was objectively reasonable under the circumstances. Therefore, any rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of first degree robbery of the victim under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16:64.1(A). Also, nothing in the caselaw suggested that the jury's verdict had to be unanimous for defendant's sentence to be increased. Thus, La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A) were not unconstitutional and not violative of defendant's Sixth Amendment right to trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1223 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mizell


2005 KA 2516


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2516 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 712; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1364



June 9, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 367199, Division "I". Honorable Reginald T. Badeaux, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana that convicted him of aggravated rape, a violation of the aggravated rape statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42; sentenced him to life in prison without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence; and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court erred in denying his motion for new trial because the verdict was not by a unanimous jury as required by La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) in capital cases. The State argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 was not unconstitutional, as it specifically provided for prosecution of the aggravated rape of a victim under 12 years as "either" a capital offense or a non-capital life imprisonment offense. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 was amended in 1997 and allowed a non-unanimous verdict in non-capital prosecutions only. The court held that there was no conflict between § 14:42 and La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) because once the district attorney opted to prosecute the offense as a non-capital life imprisonment offense, capital punishment was no longer a possibility; therefore the unanimity requirement of Artcle I, § 17(A) was no longer applicable. The court noted that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A), which governed cases involving confinement at hard labor, was triggered. Therefore the court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to require a unanimous verdict and denying defendant's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1224 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Lamz v. Wells


NO. 2005 CA 1497


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1497 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 792; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1348



June 9, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 2004-15096. Honorable Raymond S. Childress, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judicial candidate sought injunctive relief alleging that defendant opponent caused false allegations about the candidate to be distributed in campaign literature. The 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana found the motion to be moot, and allowed the candidate to amend his petition to allege defamation. The trial court then granted the opponent's motion to strike pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971.


OVERVIEW: The opponent had filed the special motion to strike pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971, arguing that the candidate had maliciously sued him in an attempt to curtail protected political speech in direct violation of the First Amendment. The trial court granted the motion, and the candidate appealed. The court held that the opponent's special motion to strike was properly granted because the opponent met his burden to show that the case involved protected free speech with a connection to a public issue, as provided in Article 971, which then shifted the burden to the candidate to establish a probability of success on his defamation claim. The court found that there was nothing in the record to suggest that the candidate would be able to satisfy the elements of his defamation action, namely, that the publications were false, that the opponent acted with actual malice, or that the candidate sustained any injury as a result of the publications. The court also noted that the candidate had not properly raised a constitutional challenge to Article 971, and that the opponent's claim for attorney fees was not addressed in the trial court, and thus not considered in the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that granted the opponent's special motion to strike and dismissed the judicial candidate's action with prejudice. The court assessed all costs associated with the appeal against the candidate, but found that the opponent represented himself and thus did not incur any attorney fees.

 

1225 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hano


2005 KA 2090


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2090 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 181; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1360



June 9, 2006, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Hano, 948 So. 2d 164, 2007 La. LEXIS 276 (La., Jan. 26, 2007)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Hano v. State, 25 So. 3d 796, 2009 La. LEXIS 3269 (La., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hano v. Warden, La. Corr. Inst., 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 84705 (E.D. La., July 6, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Hano, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 1160 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 369912 "F"), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE MARTIN E. COADY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of second degree murder, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1. The trial court denied her motions for post verdict judgment of acquittal and a new trial and sentenced her to life imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Her motion to reconsider her sentence was also denied. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's girlfriend testified that she witnessed defendant deliver to the victim two pills. That testimony established that defendant distributed methadone to the victim. The witness also testified that she and the victim each took one of the two pills, thereby establishing that the victim ingested the methadone. Thus, the evidence supported beyond a reasonable doubt the jury's conclusions that defendant distributed methadone to the victim and that he ingested the illicit drugs. Also, the evidence was sufficient to convince a rational trier of fact that the methadone was the direct cause of the victim's death because all three medical experts agreed that whether the victim died as a result of respiratory suppression from ingesting a combination of methadone and benzodiazepine or from vomiting, it was the presence of both drugs that gave rise to the hypoxic brain injury that ultimately caused the victim's death. But for the ingestion of the methadone that defendant distributed to the victim he would not have died. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt all of the elements of second degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1A(3).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1226 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Southeast Wireless Network, Inc. v. U.S. Telemetry Corp.


NO. 2005-CA-1536


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005-1536 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 127; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1366



June 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Southeast Wireless Network, Inc. v. U.S. Telemetry Corp., 943 So. 2d 1056, 2006 La. LEXIS 3381 (La., Nov. 28, 2006)
Affirmed by Southeast Wireless Network, Inc. v. U.S. Telemetry Corp., 954 So. 2d 120, 2007 La. LEXIS 890 (La., Apr. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 505430, DIVISION "E23". HONORABLE WILLIAM A. MORVANT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff stockholders challenged a decision from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which sustained an exception of lack of personal jurisdiction over appellee directors in a case arising under the Louisiana Blue Sky Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:701 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The stockholders contended that financial information was not revealed to them in violation of the Blue Sky Law. The directors were sued on the ground that they knew or should have known of the alleged fraudulent inducements and activities. The directors' exception based on lack of personal jurisdiction was sustained, and the stockholders sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that long-arm jurisdiction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3201B was coextensive with the federal constitutional due process requirements. The corporation in this case directed its activities toward the residents of Louisiana. As to the individual directors, they manifestly availed themselves of the privilege of conducting business in the forum and being protected by its laws; therefore, it was not unreasonable to require them to submit to litigation in Louisiana as well. The directors failed to show that jurisdiction would have been unreasonable in light of traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice. Finally, the appellate court rejected the argument that the "fiduciary shield" doctrine precluded the exercise of personal jurisdiction over the directors.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Thomas


NO. 2005 KA 2210


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2210 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/9/06); 938 So. 2d 168; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1353



June 9, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Thomas, 955 So. 2d 683, 2007 La. LEXIS 1153 (La., Apr. 27, 2007)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Thomas v. State, 986 So. 2d 258, 2008 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 767 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Thomas v. State, 61 So. 3d 654, 2011 La. LEXIS 726 (La., 2011)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Thomas, 2011 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 470 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 10, 2011)
Writ denied by State v. Thomas, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2838 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 20, 2013)
Writ denied by, Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Thomas v. State, 149 So. 3d 790, 2014 La. LEXIS 2195 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Thomas v. Smith, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 158690 (E.D. La., June 4, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 17th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 401111. Honorable Ashly Bruce Simpson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION FOR VEHICLE HOMICIDE AFFIRMED; HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION REVERSED; HABITUAL OFFENDER SENTENCE VACATED; ORIGINAL SENTENCE FOR VEHICLE HOMICIDE REINSTATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the 17th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana) found defendant guilty of vehicular homicide, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1. He was sentenced to 20 years' imprisonment at hard labor. He was then adjudicated a fourth felony habitual offender. The trial court vacated the previous sentence and sentenced him to 40 years' imprisonment at hard labor. It then denied his motion to reconsider. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that there was sufficient evidence of a causal relationship between defendant's blood-alcohol concentration and the victim's death to support his vehicular homicide conviction. The evidence showed that defendant was highly intoxicated at the time of the accident. Also, a doctor testified that defendant's blood-alcohol concentration of .24 grams percent would have impaired defendant's judgment and vision and slowed his reaction ability. Further, it was reasonable for the jury to infer that defendant's blood-alcohol concentration contributed to his lack of judgment. In addition, the jury could have reasonably disregarded the hypothesis that, even sober, defendant could not have avoided the accident. Thus, defendant's intoxication combined with his operation of his automobile was the cause of the victim's death. However, for purposes of his adjudication as a fourth felony habitual offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1C, the State failed to prove that the 10-year cleansing period between the 1979 conviction and the 1995 predicate offense had not lapsed; thus, the appellate court found that defendant's habitual offender adjudication was improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for vehicular homicide, reversed the habitual offender adjudication, vacated the habitual offender sentence, reinstated the sentence on vehicular homicide, and remanded for further proceedings on the habitual offender bill.

 

1228 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Prest v. Parish of Caddo


NO. 41,039-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,039 (La. App. 2 Cir. 06/02/06); 930 So. 2d 1207; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1303



June 2, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 486,874. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner sought a special exception use pursuant to Caddo Parish, La., Ordinance 51-1126, so that he could sell his land to developer who wanted to build a truck stop/casino. The zoning board granted the exception. Appellee parish commission reversed that grant. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) reversed the decision of the commission. Intervenor area resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner argued that the testimony presented at trial to refute the concerns raised at the public hearing was a sufficient basis for the trial court to reverse the decision of the commission. However, the appellate court held that the landowner's burden was not simply to rebut the concerns expressed by residents and commissioners, but to demonstrate that the commission's decision to deny the special exception did not have any substantial relationship to the public health, safety and welfare. The appellate court held that the commission acted after considering the costs and benefits to the public that would result from approval of the special exception use, including the safety and health implications of increased gambling and alcohol consumption. In addition, the comments of commissioners who voted to deny the exception reflected a decision that gambling and alcohol sales were not compatible with the expected need for future residential development in the area surrounding the proposed facility. That was a reasonable consideration since a new residential subdivision was being built in close proximity to the site. Thus, the landowner failed to satisfy his burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the parish commission's decision denying the special exception use was reinstated. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the landowner.

Therefore, the court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to consider the factors in Article 894.1, if it had not done so; 2001 La. Acts 403, which reduced penalties for drug offenses for non-violent offenders; and review Dorthey factors in its resentencing determination.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case for resentencing with instructions for the trial court to .

 

1230 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruiz


KA 06-30 consolidated with KH 05-1098 & KH 05-1261


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-30 (La. App. 3 Cir. 05/24/06); 931 So. 2d 472; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1248



May 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Ruiz, 944 So. 2d 1274, 2006 La. LEXIS 3538 (La., Dec. 15, 2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Ruiz, 2007 La. LEXIS 891 (La., Apr. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 02-1010. HONORABLE PAUL JOSEPH DEMAHY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sixteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana) of possession of cocaine, second offense, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967 and 40:982, and distribution of cocaine, second offense, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967 and 40:982. Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: The bill of information contained allegations that defendant had prior drug-related convictions. While defendant was awaiting sentencing, the state supreme court ruled that allegations of prior offenses could not be placed in the charging instrument of a subsequent offense for purposes of sentence enhancement under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:982. On appeal, the court held that it was error for the State to charge the prior offenses in the bill of information because the applicable ruling of the state supreme court applied retroactively. The second-offense convictions under § 40:982 had to be reversed as convictions for non-crimes, but the portion of the offenses based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967 was severable from the non-crimes of second-offense possession and second-offense distribution. Although it was error to expose the jury to the fact of defendant's prior convictions, the court determined that the error was harmless as to the § 40:967 violations because of the strong evidence regarding defendant's sale of cocaine to an undercover officer. The court concluded that defendant's motion to suppress was waived when he proceeded to trial without obtaining a ruling.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the second-offense portions of defendant's convictions, vacated defendant's sentences, ordered the entry of convictions for the lesser offenses of possession of cocaine and distribution of cocaine, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Wright


No. 40,945-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,945 (La. App. 2 Cir. 05/19/06); 931 So. 2d 432; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1164



May 19, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Wright, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1946 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 23, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Wright, 952 So. 2d 694, 2007 La. LEXIS 656 (La., Mar. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 69,945. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster (Louisiana) convicted defendant of two counts of video voyeurism involving a child under 17 and one count of video voyeurism, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:283(B)(4) and (3). He was sentenced to serve five years' imprisonment at hard labor on count one, 10 years on count two, and 10 years on count three without benefits, with the sentences to be served concurrently. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: At trial, two victims testified that they both tried on clothes, including bathing suits, in the dressing room while defendant was at the store counter. When defendant later left the store for a short time, the girls discovered a monitor hidden behind the counter. They flipped through the channels and saw that one view was of the inside of the dressing room. Upon close inspection of the dressing room, they slid a mirror to the side and discovered a hole in the wall with a camera inside. The victims identified themselves in a dressing room videotape, one of the many discovered in defendant's car, and stated that they were unaware that they were being videotaped by defendant and denied ever giving him permission to videotape them. A third victim identified herself in a dressing room videotape and stated that she was unaware that she was being videotaped by defendant and denied ever giving him permission to videotape her. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's three convictions for video voyeurism. But, the sentence imposed for count three was illegal because it was five years more than the maximum possible sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:283(B)(3).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions but vacated his sentences and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1232 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


NO. 40,972-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,972 (La. App. 2 Cir. 05/17/06); 930 So. 2d 1122; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1145



May 17, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Allen v. State, 2008 La. LEXIS 2720 (La., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 83493 & 83493A. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.
State v. Allen, 871 So. 2d 1097, 2004 La. LEXIS 1332 (La., Apr. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana) convicted defendant of attempted armed robbery and two counts of aggravated battery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:64, and 14:34. He was sentenced to serve 35 years at hard labor for the attempted armed robbery conviction and 10 years at hard labor for each of the aggravated battery convictions. The sentences were ordered to be served concurrently. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The record was sufficient to show that defendant was the person who attempted to rob a grocery store, and that he fired a shot that injured the store's owner. Therefore, the convictions for attempted armed robbery and aggravated battery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:64, and 14:34, of the store's owner were supported by the record. Also, although defendant stated that he did not intend to kill the store's owner or one of its employees during the attempted robbery, both women testified that defendant threatened to kill them prior to firing the shots. The store's owner testified that she thought that he had killed the employee (her sister) and that he was going to kill her as well. Defendant's action in firing a sequence of gunshots into the confined space where the store's owner and the employee were standing implied that defendant either intended to kill both women, or he intended to inflict great bodily harm. For those reasons, the evidence was sufficient to support the elements of the greater offense of attempted first degree murder. Accordingly, the responsive verdict for attempted first degree murder, aggravated battery, was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Washington


NO. 2005-KA-1006


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1006 (La. App. 4 Cir. 05/10/06); 931 So. 2d 1120; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1202



May 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 13, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Washington, 944 So. 2d 1272, 2006 La. LEXIS 3586 (La., Dec. 15, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wash. v. La., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 4473 (U.S., Apr. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 451-662, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence imposed by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), after a jury found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C)(2). The district court found defendant to be a third felony offender and sentenced him to eight and one-half years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged statements made by the State regarding sentencing and claimed that his sentence was excessive. On review, the court found no error. The State's comments related to defendant's most recent conviction, and the choice to permit an argument about the penalty was within the discretion of the district court judge. Considering the factors enunciated by the district court at the sentencing hearing, the court found that defendant's sentence was not excessive pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 20. The district court noted defendant's long history of drug related arrests, and the maximum sentence he could have received as a third offender was 10 years. Thus, defendant failed to show that the district court abused the liberal discretion allowed in sentencing. Further, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 was not unconstitutionally applied to defendant because he was not punished for being a drug addict but for possessing cocaine and for two prior convictions for possession of crack. Finally, the habitual offender sentence did not violate the Due Process Clause or the right to a jury because the enhancement was for prior convictions, which did not require fact finding by a jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Williams

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williams v. Louisiana, 550 U.S. 971, 127 S. Ct. 2880, 167 L. Ed. 2d 1156, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 6141 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Williams v. Cain, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 67082 (E.D. La., Sept. 11, 2007)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 6 So. 3d 810, 2009 La. LEXIS 357 (La., 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 131 So. 3d 41, 2014 La. LEXIS 198 (La., 2014)
Writ dismissed by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 2016 La. LEXIS 1002 (La., Apr. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Criminal District Court Orleans Parish. NO. 411-522, Section "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.
State v. Williams, 793 So. 2d 572, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1306 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 11, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced him to life imprisonment under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and to 30 years in prison after he was convicted of distribution of cocaine and possession with the intent to distribute cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine and possession with the intent to distribute cocaine. On the first count, he was sentenced to life imprisonment under the Habitual Offender Law. He was sentenced to 30 years in prison on the second count. The sentences were to be served concurrently. On appeal, defendant claimed that the life sentence was excessive under La. Const. art. 1, § 20. The court found that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in sentencing defendant under the Habitual Offender Law. The trial judge noted at the sentencing hearing that defendant had a lengthy and extensive criminal history that dated back to him reaching the age of majority. The presentence report showed that defendant had violated both his probation and his parole when they had been granted to him. Thus, defendant had not taken advantage of the opportunities made available to him. The trial judge had considered the mitigating factors that were presented at the sentencing hearing, including the fact that defendant was addicted to drugs when he committed the crimes for which he was convicted. Defendant's reliance on Apprendi was misplaced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1235 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Long v. Hutchins


No. 40,548-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,548 (La. App. 2 Cir. 04/26/06); 926 So. 2d 556; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 969



April 26, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Originally appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 486935. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.
Long v. Hutchins, 926 So. 2d 556, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2550 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was subject to punishment under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4611(1)(b) for violating a restraining order prohibiting him from contacting respondent. He was given a determinate sentence in the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of 120 days, 100 of which were suspended. Inter alia, he was not allowed to put on a defense and he was not advised of the right to a jury trial. Appellant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The matter was before the appellate court to again consider the scope of rights to be afforded a party in a civil proceeding subject to contempt punishable under § 13:4611(1)(b) and whether appellant was deprived of such rights. His sentence of 120 days with 100 days suspended was a definite sentence imposed without conditions or a purge clause. Because the sentence was a determinate one, the punishment was criminal in nature, and it could not be imposed unless federal constitutional protections were applied in the contempt proceeding. Defendant's determinate sentence was clearly criminal in nature. Moreover, he was exposed to a maximum penalty of 12 months imprisonment thereby meeting the threshold for jury trial eligibility as a constitutional right. The sentence was imposed without appellant having been advised of, or provided with, the constitutional safeguards.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded.

Roudakis v. City of Ruston


No. 40,952-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,952 (La. App. 2 Cir. 04/19/06); 927 So. 2d 1231; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 905



April 19, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 48,991. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents challenged a decision from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln (Louisiana), which dismissed their action against appellees, a city and an applicant, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief in a zoning dispute.


OVERVIEW: The city's board of aldermen granted variances to Ruston, La., Mun. Code § 29-43(5) (1998) to allow the applicant to construct two cellular phone towers. The residents contended that the city's action in granting the variances was invalid because the ordinance contained no objective standards for allowing a variance. The trial court dismissed the action for failing to follow the procedures in La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1880. It also found that the city's decision was not arbitrary and unreasonable. The residents then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that article 1880 required service on the state attorney general if an ordinance was alleged to be unconstitutional. Even though the petition did not assert such a claim specifically, the trial court properly found that the claim was based on an assertion of unconstitutionality. Further, the city's board considered the facts and circumstances of the case and exercised their authority honestly and upon due consideration. The considerations were related to the public health, safety, and general welfare. Moreover, a prima facie presumption of validity attached to the zoning body's actions.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.
