CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court, Caddo Parish, Louisiana, that, on remand, sentenced him for public intimidation in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:122 as a third-felony habitual offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and imposed a life sentence without the benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant had threatened a police officer who responded to a domestic disturbance call.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's decision granting defendant a judgment of acquittal was reversed and the defendant was sentenced on remand as a second felony habitual offender. However, the trial court erred in failing to consider whether the mandatory sentence was constitutional as applied to this defendant using the Johnson factors, such as the use or lack of violence in the current and prior offenses, the more lenient punishment under the amended habitual offender statute, and the burden on taxpayers of housing defendant for life.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's the habitual offender adjudication and remanded the case to the trial court for reconsideration of the life sentence imposed in light of the Johnson guidelines.

State v. Roberson


No. 40,809-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,809 (La. App. 2 Cir. 04/19/06); 929 So. 2d 789; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 907



April 19, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 123,224. Honorable John M. Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 26th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, convicting him of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and obstruction of justice in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:130.1, and sentencing him to life in prison at hard labor without benefits and 40 years at hard labor, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for beating the victim to death and then disposing of her body. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's second-degree murder conviction because the circumstantial evidence against him was overwhelming. The evidence showed that: (1) defendant rented the motel room where the murder took place; (2) a housekeeper and motel resident saw defendant the day of the murder; (3) connections were made between the brands of cigarettes and condoms found in the motel room and defendant's home; and (4) DNA evidence linked defendant to the victim, including defendant's DNA evidence found in the motel room, the victim's DNA found on defendant's clothing, and the victim's DNA found in the motel room and in defendant's vehicle. The evidence was also sufficient to support defendant's obstruction of justice conviction because the victim's DNA was found on multiple surfaces in the trunk of defendant's vehicle, which matched descriptions of the vehicle at the motel. A detective's testimony that liquid dripped from defendant's trunk clearly suggested that he attempted to clean out the trunk of his vehicle.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1239 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ceasar v. Hebert


05-1195 c/w 05-1196


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1195 (La. App. 3 Cir. 04/05/06); 926 So. 2d 139; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 733



April 5, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Sub nomine at Corsey v. Iberia Parish Gov't, 926 So. 2d 144, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 731 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 5, 2006)
Motion denied by Ceasar v. Hebert, 932 So. 2d 758, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1413 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 100030. HONORABLE GERARD W. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former prisoner brought a negligence action against defendants, the sheriff and a deputy, for injuries sustained when he was injured in an automobile accident while riding in a truck the deputy was driving. The Sixteenth Judicial District Court of Iberia Parish, Louisiana, granted summary judgment in favor of the sheriff and the deputy on grounds that they were immune from liability. The former prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the former prisoner contended the trial court erred in granting summary judgment on grounds that the deputy and the sheriff were immune from ordinary negligence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:708; he asserted that the trial court erred in applying § 15:708 to him because he was not a prisoner at the time the suit was filed. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the former prisoner's injury occurred while he was a prisoner. The injury arose out of participation in the litter abatement program, and the fact that the former prisoner had since been released did not affect the immunity afforded by § 15:708 for injuries arising out of a prisoner's participation in a litter abatement program. Nothing in § 15:708 extended the correctional facility's obligation to provide medical treatment beyond the period of incarceration. And the fact that the accident occurred after the truck's engine died as the deputy drove out into the intersection showed that the accident did not result from gross negligence or an intentional act. As such, no issue of material fact remained as to any negligence, and summary judgment was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Allen


NO. 2005 KA 1622


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1622 (La.App. 1 Cir. 3/29/06); 934 So. 2d 146; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 673



March 29, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 17th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Lafourche, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 409,850. Honorable Ashly Bruce Simpson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by amended bill of information with one count of second degree robbery, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.4, and pleaded not guilty. He waived his right to a jury trial, and following a bench trial in the 17th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), was found guilty as charged. He was sentenced to twenty-five years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that he was denied due process when the evidence introduced by the State was legally insufficient to support the verdict rendered by the trial court. He argued there was no testimony that he beat the victim. The appellate court held that the evidence proved beyond a reasonable doubt, and to the exclusion of every reasonable hypothesis of innocence, all of the elements of second degree robbery and defendant's identity as a perpetrator. The direct evidence and those reasonably inferred from the circumstantial evidence were sufficient for a rational juror to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had the specific intent to inflict serious bodily injury on the victim. Defendant was not merely present at the scene. He knowingly participated in the execution of the offense and played an integral part in the completion of the offense. Defendant drove the vehicle while the victim was beaten by his accomplices. Furthermore, defendant dragged the victim out of the vehicle, demanded the victim's property, and forcefully removed the property from the victim while defendant's accomplices viciously beat the victim to prevent his resistance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Babin v. McDaniel


NUMBER 2005 CU 2455


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2455 (La. App. 1 Cir. 3/24/06); 934 So. 2d 69; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 614



March 24, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Barry v. McDaniel, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3136 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Family Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 141,203. Honorable Toni M. Higginbotham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the parents, sought review of the decision of the Family Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiffs, the grandparents, and declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 constitutional, granted visitation to the grandparents, and found the parents in contempt of court.


OVERVIEW: The parents, who were the biological father and the adoptive mother, sought review of a judgment against them and in favor of the maternal grandparents; the court affirmed in all respects except as to the finding of contempt. Because the trial court failed to render an order reciting the facts constituting the contempt, as was required by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 225(B), the court reversed the judgment insofar as it held the parents in contempt of court and ordered them to pay a $ 1,000.00 fine, plus costs and attorney fees, and granted the grandparents seven make-up visitation days with the child. The court further held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 could be interpreted in a constitutional manner; thus, there was no error in the trial court's determination that § 9:344 was constitutional on its face. The specificity of the trial court's judgment demonstrated its awareness of the parents' constitutionally protected fundamental right to raise the child as they saw fit and that the grandparents' rights as grandparents were ancillary to the parents' rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the issue of contempt and affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

Brown v. Jones


NO. 2006-CA-0260 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2006-CA-0261


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-0260 (La. App. 4 Cir. 03/21/06); 929 So. 2d 169; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1171



March 21, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 2006.
Writ denied by Brown v. Jones, 925 So. 2d 1241, 2006 La. LEXIS 1102 (La., Mar. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 2006-2025, DIVISION "I," HONORABLE PIPER GRIFFIN, JUDGE AND NO. 2006-1975, DIVISION "A," HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidates challenged orders of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division "I" and Division "A" (Louisiana), which granted appellee electors' petitions challenging the candidates' qualifications for office under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:463.


OVERVIEW: The candidates qualified as candidates for assessors in municipal elections. Each candidate included the initials "I.Q.," which stood for "I quit," in their names. The trial courts ruled in both cases that "I.Q." was not a permissible "nickname" but was an impermissible "designation" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:463. The candidates argued that the trial court erred in finding that "I.Q." was not a permissible nickname and impermissibly construed § 18.463 as prohibiting political speech in a candidate's name on the ballot in violation of the candidates' First Amendment rights. The candidates admitted that they only started using the "I.Q." moniker several weeks before qualifying for their respective races and that "I.Q." was to inform voters that they would take no salary and work for the contraction of the number of assessors from seven to one. The court found that "I.Q." pointed out to voters what the candidates would have done if they were elected. Thus there was nothing manifestly erroneous or clearly wrong with the trial court's rulings. The constitutional claims were not reviewable because they were not raised before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1243 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Stalder


NO. 2006 CW 0051


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0051 (La.App. 1 Cir. 3/17/06); 934 So. 2d 722; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 595



March 17, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM THE 20TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EAST FELICIANA. NO. 36,831. HONORABLE WILLIAM G. CARMICHAEL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED AND MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, the Department of Public Safety and Corrections (Department), filed a writ application seeking review of the decision of the 20th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Feliciana (Louisiana), which denied an exception of prescription in respondent inmate's action for damages that he allegedly sustained as a result of being struck by another inmate.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed an action for damages and the Department filed a peremptory exception of prescription, seeking dismissal of the suit with prejudice. Therein, the Department argued that the inmate failed to timely file an administrative claim for relief pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1172. The district court denied the exception and the Department filed a timely writ application. The court granted the writ, stating that the district court used the term "interruption" in regard to prescription, whereas the relevant statute, § 15:1172(E), used the term "suspension" in regard to liberative prescription. Further, in briefs, the inmate argued that he had one year subsequent to delivery of the final agency decision on May 7, 2004, to file suit. In that sense, he appeared to argue that prescription was interrupted until May 7, 2004. The district court erred in finding that the statute provided for the interruption, rather than suspension, of the prescriptive period for delictual actions. Since the court believed that constituted legal error, it granted the writ and vacated the judgment of the trial court dated September 16, 2005.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ and remanded the matter to the district court for proper application of the law to the facts at hand.

State v. Lawrence

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana for armed robbery. Defendant was originally sentenced to 25 years, then he was adjudicated a habitual offender and sentenced to serve 40 1/2 years.


OVERVIEW: Masked perpetrators robbed a convenience store. After a 911 call was received, an officer stopped a car being driven by defendant which contained occupants that matched the description of the robbers. State v. Cuccia


NO. 2005-KA-0807


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0807 (La.App. 4 Cir. 3/15/06); 933 So. 2d 134; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 935



March 15, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 7, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Cuccia, 939 So. 2d 1273, 2006 La. LEXIS 2996 (La., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 440-982, SECTION "J". HONORABLE DARRYL A. DERBIGNY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans parish (Louisiana) that convicted him of manslaughter under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31; sentenced him as a third-felony habitual offender to 30 years at hard labor under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1; and denied his motions for new trial, for arrest of judgment, for release of juror information, and to reconsider sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that brain scans of the victim did not show serious injury on the day he struck her during an altercation over drugs and items she allegedly stole while in his house; thus the evidence did not show that his blow caused her death. The court held that defendant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence, which included the testimony of pathologist that indicated that defendant struck the victim on head with a flashlight, causing bleeding in her brain that resulted in a coma and her death 2 days later. The court rejected defendant's justification defenses because the justified force provision, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:19, did not apply where the force resulted in a homicide. The court rejected defendant's claim regarding the limited cross-examination of police officers because defendant failed to object and the responses involved speculation, hearsay, matters not within the officer's personal knowledge, or opinion. The court found that defendant's sentence was only slightly longer than the minimum statutory sentence under the Habitual Offender Law, and that his two prior drug offenses could serve as the basis for his sentence as a third-felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Stanton


NO. 2005-KA-0812


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Stanton v. Cain, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29292 (E.D. La., Feb. 25, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Stanton v. State, 140 So. 3d 1185, 2014 La. LEXIS 1495 (La., 2014)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM Criminal District Court Orleans Parish. NO. 436-978, Section "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted armed robbery and attempted manslaughter, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27. Defendant challenged the sentences imposed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant attempted to rob a tire repairman of $25.00. He fired a gun at the victim, but it luckily misfired and no one was injured. After he was convicted of two crimes, the trial court considered his extensive juvenile record and other factors when it imposed concurrent forty-five and twenty-year sentences. Defendant then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the sentences were not excessive under U.S. Const. amend. VIII or La. Const. art. Further, Apprendi did not prohibit the trial court from considering the juvenile adjudications. In addition, Apprendi did not apply to defendant's situation because he did not receive a penalty that exceeded the statutory maximum. Finally, the ineffective assistance of counsel claim should have been pursued in an action seeking postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

W.R.M. v. H.C.V.


05-425


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-425 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/01/06); 923 So. 2d 911; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 398



March 1, 2006, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Companion case at W.R.M. v. H.C.V., 923 So. 2d 916, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 375 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 1, 2006)
Vacated by, Set aside by, Petition dismissed by W.R.M. v. H.C.V., 2007 La. LEXIS 522 (La., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2003-3614. HONORABLE GUY BRADBERRY, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Viator v. Miller, 136 Fed. Appx. 615, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 11103 (5th Cir. La., 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Several years after defendant mother gave birth, plaintiff ex-boyfriend filed a petition to establish filiation, alleging he was the biological father of the child. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court of Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana, denied his plea challenging the constitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 191 and granted the mother's exceptions of no cause of action, no right of action, and prescription. The ex-boyfriend appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the ex-boyfriend again challenged the unconstitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 191, asserting that the retroactive application of the peremptive period set out in art. 191 unconstitutionally deprived him of a vested right. The appellate court agreed, finding that prior to the passage of 2004 La. Acts 530 (which created La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 191), Louisiana courts traditionally recognized a biological father's right to his illegitimate child by means of an avowal action. Therefore, at the time the ex-boyfriend filed his suit, he had a vested right to sue to avow paternity. Accordingly, retroactive application of art. 191 was an unconstitutional abridgement of a right to due process. And as an action for avowal was not subject to a prescriptive period under the law in effect at the time the petition was filed, the trial court could not grant judgment on the mother's exceptions based on the timeliness of the ex-boyfriend's petition. Therefore, the trial court erred in granting the mother's exceptions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying the plea of unconstitutionality was reversed. The trial court's judgment granting the mother's exceptions was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Stracener v. Joubert


05-1121


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1121 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/01/06); 924 So. 2d 430; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 400



March 1, 2006, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. C-2005-0052 "A". HONORABLE STUART S. KAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The child's father died in a car accident the day before the final judgment of his divorce from appellant mother. Appellee paternal grandparents subsequently filed a petition for visitation rights with the child. The Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court of Beauregard Parish, Louisiana, rendered judgment granting visitation to the grandparents. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the mother contended the trial court abused its discretion in the amount of visitation awarded the grandparents and in failing to place special weight on the mother's visitation preference who was not proven to be or challenged as an unfit parent. She also argued that the trial court erred in applying La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 and in failing to apply and address the provisions of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136. The appellate court agreed that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 was inapplicable as the father's death did not occur while he was married; the fact that the judgment of divorce was not signed by the trial court until the day following his death was of no consequence. The trial court should have applied La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136. The appellate court also agreed with the mother that the trial court's visitation award was excessive, especially considering the fact that they were awarded more time with the child than the father was.


OUTCOME: The grandparent's visitation award was reduced and the visitation schedule was amended; as amended, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Williams


05-1338


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1338 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/01/06); 924 So. 2d 1159; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 412



March 1, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Williams, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 938 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 12, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 944 So. 2d 1284, 2006 La. LEXIS 3584 (La., Dec. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 273,837. HONORABLE JOHN C. DAVIDSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Ninth Judicial District Court of Rapides Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of aggravated rape, aggravated burglary, and first degree robbery. He was sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for the rape, to 40 years without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for the robbery, and to 30 years at hard labor for the burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the verdicts of guilty of aggravated rape and aggravated burglary were unconstitutional because they imposed multiple punishments for a single act. He also contended the aggravated rape conviction was not sustainable because there was no evidence of a weapon or use of a weapon during the commission of the crime. The appellate court disagreed, holding first that the State did not need to present evidence that defendant used a weapon to be convicted of aggravated rape; the fact that the victim was 77-years-old at the time of the rape was sufficient to support this conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. And based on the Blockburger test, double jeopardy did not exist as the crimes of aggravated rape and aggravated burglary each required proof of an additional element different from the other. Defendant could have been convicted of aggravated rape without proof that an aggravated burglary occurred; he could also have been convicted of aggravated burglary without proof that a rape occurred, considering the fact that he committed a battery upon the victim when he struck her in the arm and armed himself with a club.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed but the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to amend the sentencing minutes to reflect that the trial court sentenced defendant to 30 years at hard labor for aggravated burglary and to order the sentence imposed for first degree robbery to be served without benefit of parole.

Coleman v. Thompson


05-857


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-0857 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/01/06); 923 So. 2d 889; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 433



March 1, 2006 Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 218,987. HONORABLE HARRY FRED RANDOW, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sued defendant warden for compensatory and punitive damages for the warden's delay in releasing him to a work release program. The Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, Louisiana, dismissed the inmate's complaint for failing to exhaust his administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that his due process and equal protection rights were violated by not being granted a timely work release. Accordingly, despite titling his action as a tort action, the court held that the inmate's suit was in substance a challenge to the rules and conditions of his confinement. For such complaints, the inmate was required to exhaust the administrative remedy procedure which governed those complaints before filing suit in district court. The inmate was approved for work release in August 2004. The first correspondence from the inmate was dated October 18, 2004 asking for assistance in getting a work release. The inmate wrote the warden or assistant warden four more times asking for assistance of some sort though December 1, 2004. Of note, none of the letters contained the phrase "This is a Request for Administrative Remedy," pursuant to La. Admin. Code tit. 22, § XI.325(F)(2)(a) and (b) (2005). The inmate filed suit on November 15, 2004. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's complaint because it was clear that he did not exhaust his administrative remedies before filing suit as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the inmate's complaint was affirmed.

State v. Poche


05-1042


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1042 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/01/06); 924 So. 2d 1225; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 435



March 1, 2006, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ALLEN, NO. CR-2004-3752, HONORABLE PATRICIA C. COLE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen (Louisiana) of battery of a correctional facility employee and obscenity. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he did not validly waive his right to counsel. The court of appeals disagreed. Based on the trial transcript alone, the trial court's actions were inadequate; however, based on the entire record, the trial court's determination was not error. Throughout the prosecution of his case, defendant filed numerous pretrial pro se briefs with the trial court. The trial court granted defendant hearings on several of his pretrial pro se motions, and upon his request, allowed defendant to personally argue his motions. At defendant's arraignment, the State read the bill of information. The bill of information included the elements that the State intended to prove at trial. After being advised of the elements of the offenses, defendant stated that he understood both of the charges. At the sentencing hearing, the trial court discussed defendant's prior extensive experience with the judicial process. Defendant was a fifth felony offender with a record dating back to 1983. Based on his prior extensive experience with the criminal justice system, defendant was aware of the dangers and disadvantages of self-representation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kujawa


NO. 2005 KA 0470


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0470 (La. App. 1 Cir. 2/22/06); 929 So. 2d 99; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 303



February 22, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Kujawa, 2006 La. LEXIS 2777 (La., Oct. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court Parish of St. Mary, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 154,238. The Honorable Keith J. Comeaux, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a Catholic priest, sought review of the decision of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), which convicted him of 15 counts of possession of pornography involving juveniles in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1, after his plea of guilty. He was sentenced to 10 years at hard labor for each of the counts, to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to quash and sentenced him to 10 years at hard labor for each of the 15 counts of child pornography. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences, stating that at issue in the case was the legality of imposing separate sentences on defendant for convictions of 15 counts that were charged separately in a single bill of information. The court stated that a careful reading of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1 revealed that the legislative intent was to proscribe possession of any single image. The use of the plural form was clearly a matter of grammatical style and not suggestive of an intent to establish a unit of prosecution based upon a broad course of conduct involving multiple contraband images. Thus, defendant's emphasis upon the plural form of the contraband items was misplaced. The court further concluded that the sentences imposed were not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense. Because defendant made no objection when the trial court imposed fines, the issue was barred on appeal pursuant to La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 103(A)(1) and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 841.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gray v. State


05-617


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-617 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/15/06); 923 So. 2d 812; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 277



February 15, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CATAHOULA, NO. 23-375. HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of an order from the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Catahoula (Louisiana), which granted exceptions and motions filed by defendants, a correction center, a warden, a captain, and an officer, and struck his habeas corpus petition without prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court granted defendants' exceptions and struck the inmate's pleadings without prejudice. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in dismissing the petition as premature because there was no showing that an adequate administrative remedy was available. A review of the inmate's pleadings indicated that he never had the opportunity to adjudicate the merits of his claim for the return of his personal effects, including his law books. The trial court dismissed his complaint for failure to pursue administrative remedies, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1184(A)(2), without reaching the question of whether prison officials prevented him from pursuing those remedies. Further, the trial court erred in dismissing the petition pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 891 because the pro se petition was sufficient to alert defendants of the causes of action alleged. Finally, the trial court erred in dismissing the petition pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1184(B) because the allegations were not frivolous, did not fail to state a cause of action, and did not meet any other criteria for dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting defendants' exceptions. The court reversed the order granting defendants' motion to strike, except as to any monetary references in the petition. The court remanded the case for a hearing and ruling on the issue of the inmate's right to pursue mental anguish damages and punitive damages. The court ordered that the inmate be afforded access to the law library or be provided legal assistance.

State v. Doussan


NO. 05-KA-586


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


05-586 (La. App. 5 Cir. 02/14/06); 924 So. 2d 333; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 270



February 14, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-2277, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him, by a guilty plea, of possession of more than 60 pounds of marijuana in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(F)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his guilty plea and sentence, but the court affirmed. The court stated that the officers had probable cause sufficient to justify a warrantless arrest when they entered the recording studio. By that time, the confidential informant had purchased marijuana from defendant inside the studio and told the officers that he had seen additional marijuana there. The officers also arrested a man immediately after he left defendant's studio who had marijuana in his possession. The officers were concerned that defendant had been alerted to their surveillance activity. Due to defendant's nervous behavior, the officers believed that he was aware of their presence and was destroying evidence. Based on that, the court found that there were exigent circumstances sufficient to support a valid entry. When officers approached defendant outside of his business, they had probable cause to arrest him for distribution of marijuana. When defendant attempted to elude the officers by fleeing into his studio and locking the door, the officers were within their authority to enter the building pursuant to the Fourth Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 5 to complete the arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded with instructions to the trial judge to send written notice to defendant within 10 days of the rendition of the opinion of the correct statement of the law regarding the prescriptive period for postconviction relief, and to file written proof in the record that defendant received the notice.

 

1255 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wooley v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Ins. Co.


NO. 2005 CA 1490


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1490 (La. App. 1 Cir. 02/10/06); 928 So. 2d 618; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 292



February 10, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 502,311. The Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.
Wooley v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Ins. Co., 893 So. 2d 746, 2005 La. LEXIS 142 (La., Jan. 19, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commissioner of Insurance sought declaratory relief seeking a determination that 1995 La. Acts 739 and 1999 La. Acts 1332 were unconstitutional; the trial court held the Acts unconstitutional. Defendant insurance company appealed directly to the Supreme Court of Louisiana, which remanded the matter to determine if the Commissioner had the right to declaratory relief on the issue of whether a form complied with applicable laws.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company had sought approval of a form. The Commissioner had disapproved of the form, but an administrative law judge (ALJ) approved the form over the Commissioner's objection, and the Commissioner sought judicial review. A trial court ruled that the Commissioner had no right to judicial review, based upon La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 49:964(A)(2) and 49:992(B)(3). The Commissioner then filed the present action. The appellate court determined that the Commissioner had no right to seek declaratory relief in a situation where the insurance company had only sought administrative approval of the form and a challenge to the form had not arisen out of a concrete factual situation because the legislature's enactment of §§ 49:964(A)(2) and 49:992(B)(2) and (B)(3) unequivocally restricted the Commissioner's authority to seek judicial review of the ALJ's adverse adjudication of the issue presented to him. As the administrative approval of insurance forms were not civil matters within La. Const. art. 5, § 16(A), the issue was not within the original jurisdiction of the court. Thus, there was no justiciable controversy that allowed the Commissioner to seek declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated.

Succession of McKay


CA 05-603


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-603 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/01/06); 921 So. 2d 1219; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 167



February 1, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication March 24, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Succession of McKay, 929 So. 2d 1252, 2006 La. LEXIS 1834 (La., June 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 33,700. HONORABLE F. RAE DONALDSON SWENT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two men, claimed to be the illegitimate children of the deceased and filed petitions to intervene in his succession. Appellee representative filed exceptions of prescription and no cause/no right of action. The Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), found former La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209, regarding proof of filiation, applicable and sustained the exceptions and dismissed the petitions. The men appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the appeals were pending, the Louisiana Legislature enacted La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 197 which was effective in 2005, and which changed the law regarding the time period for bringing a paternity action. Formerly, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209C provided for the time limits for proving filiation. At the time the instant petitions were filed, one of the men was 54 years old and the other was 36 years old. Obviously, they were well beyond 19 years old and their claims for filiation had long prescribed under former art. 209, which had required that any proceeding had to have been brought within 19 years of their birth. Although the men claimed that the trial court erred in finding that former art. 209 was constitutional, its constitutionality was clearly upheld by the Louisiana Supreme Court in Succession of Grice. Based on Grice, the appellate court agreed with the trial court's ruling that former art. 209 was constitutional and therefore, that finding foreclosed the constitutional attacks of the men. Nor had the appellate court found any "clear and unequivocal" expression by the legislature that new La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 197 revived filiation claims that had already prescribed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were to be shared equally between the two children.

 

1257 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hitchcock v. Heritage Manor Nursing Home


05-1010


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1010 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/01/06); 922 So. 2d 764; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 178



February 1, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 4, NO. 97-04797. HONORABLE SHARON MORROW, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.
Hitchcock v. State, 901 So. 2d 613, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1083 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 27, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant appealed the decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 4 (Louisiana), to dismiss her disputed claim for compensation pursuant to appellee employer's motion for summary judgment. The court found that no question of fact remained but that the claimant violated the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 by misrepresenting her condition to obtain workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employer alleged that the claimant made numerous misrepresentations as to previous injuries and her pre-accident physical condition in depositions and that surveillance videos showed that she was able to perform tasks she previously denied being able to do. The appellate court noted that while the video surveillance tapes showed the claimant doing tasks which she stated she was unable to do, they also showed occasions on which she appeared to be in pain and unable to function normally. The WCJ stated in her oral reasons for judgment that the claimant made deliberate misrepresentations about her injuries in order to bolster her compensation claim. The WCJ also stated that there were some cases where she felt that she needed to see the witness to judge the credibility. But that it was sufficiently documented in the instant case that the claims were "more than puffery or exaggeration." In light of the contradictory evidence and the WCJ's credibility evaluation with regard to the claimant's motive or intent, the appellate court found that summary judgment was not appropriate. A material issue of fact remained as to whether willful misrepresentations were made to obtain benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the employer.

 

1258 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Schoeffler v. Drake Hunting Club


05-499


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-499 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/04/06); 919 So. 2d 822; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1



January 4, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, NO. 01-63941. HONORABLE KEITH RAYNE JULES COMEAUX, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed a decision of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which granted defendant property owners' exceptions of no cause and no right of action to survey and fix boundaries at the high water mark along privately-owned lands. Plaintiffs added the State as a defendant and sought mandamus compelling the State to bring a boundary action against the owners.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were individuals who navigated the waters of a basin for commercial and recreational purposes. They claimed that the owners impeded plaintiffs' servitude and right of public access to waters and banks subject to public use under La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 456 and 784, et seq., and La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3691. The court held that on the face of the petition, there was not a cause of action for the kind of "boundary" that plaintiffs sought to fix in that it was not a traditional boundary between contiguous lands. Plaintiffs did not have a right of action to fix such boundaries because plaintiffs were not owners, lessors, lessees, legal or conventional usufructuaries, or adverse possessors of the properties at issue. As to mandamus, there was no indication of even a discretionary basis for the State to fix such boundaries. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 41:1701.1B(4) did not impose the burden of suing numerous landowners to fix boundaries not required by law. Further, the request for declaratory judgment essentially sought to compel the State to declare rights not adjudicated. Plaintiffs had no standing to compel the State to make such broad declarations on their behalf.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Pulliam


KA 05-534


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-534 (La. App. 3 Cir. 12/30/05); 920 So. 2d 900; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2656



December 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 6, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Pulliam, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 427 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF GRANT, NO. 03-563. HONORABLE ALLEN A. KRAKE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Thirty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Grant (Louisiana), which denied his motion to suppress. He had pled guilty to a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(D).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, third offense, which was a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(D). He pled guilty to the offense as charged, while preserving his rights to appeal. He was sentenced to pay a fine and to serve two years at hard labor and he appealed, seeking review of the denial of his motion to suppress. The court affirmed however, stating that he failed to show that the evidence of his intoxication was obtained as a result of a checkpoint that was improperly established or administered under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:295.4. The only motorists who were detained were those who, like defendant, were observed to have been in violation of a traffic statute. His sentence, however, was vacated as illegal, and the case was remanded for resentencing pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.4. The penalty provision in effect at the time of the offense was the applicable sentencing provision. The trial court was instructed to resentence defendant to a legal sentence under the sentencing provision in effect when the offense was committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed but the sentence was illegal. Thus, the court remanded for resentencing.

 

1260 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Knowles


Nos. 40,324-KW & No. 40,325-KW Consolidated Cases


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,324 (La. App. 2 Cir. 12/30/05); 917 So. 2d 1262; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2690



December 30, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana Trial Court Nos. 129,306 & No. 129,308. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES VACATED AND SET ASIDE; JUDGMENT REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress alleging that the evidence was obtained as a result of an unconstitutional stop. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana) denied defendant's motion. Defendant was subsequently convicted of possession of marijuana and resisting an officer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Louisiana Wildlife and Fisheries Enforcement agent stopped a vehicle driving through a wildlife management area (WMA) to determine if the occupants had obtained a permit to conduct activities in the WMA. The stop led to further investigation in which the agent learned that marijuana was in the vehicle. The agent told a sleeping passenger, defendant, to get out of the vehicle. He then attempted to flee the scene. The agent chased and apprehended him. The agent testified that the reason he stopped the vehicle was that he did not see a self-clearing permit on the dashboard, but the regulations did not require such a permit if the vehicle was simply passing through the WMA. The stop appeared to be arbitrary or discretionary on the part of the agent and constituted an invasion of privacy. Thus, the stop violated the Fourth Amendment prohibition against warrantless searches and seizures, and violated the La. Const. art. 1, § 5 right against invasions of privacy. Therefore, the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress. Finally, because defendant was not under arrest, he could not be convicted of resisting an officer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:108A.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated and set aside defendant's convictions and sentences, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The judgment denying the motion to suppress was reversed.

 

1261 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moreau


05-544


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-544 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/30/05); 918 So. 2d 598; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2696



December 30, 2005, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, NO. 03-227269. HONORABLE KEITH RAYNE JULES COMEAUX, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which convicted him of dogfighting. He was sentenced to one year at hard labor, with a $ 1,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was pulled over by a police officer for impeding the flow of traffic. After the driver and defendant were arrested, the officer saw a bleeding dog on the backseat of the vehicle. The officer searched the car, also finding a video camera and a videotape. Upon questioning the driver, the officer learned that he and defendant had engaged in dogfighting. Defendant was charged with dogfighting. The trial court denied his motion to suppress. He pled guilty to the charge. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in notifying defendant verbally, rather than in a written waiver of rights, of the prescriptive period for filing postconviction relief. The notice did not meet the requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8. The record supported a determination that the officer was reasonable in stopping defendant's car where it was stopped at a traffic light next to another vehicle and the occupants of both vehicles were talking. The officer had probable cause to believe that the dog was injured as a result of some criminal activity because the vehicle was stopped in the early morning, defendant seemed intoxicated, and the driver had blood on his pants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court remanded the case with instructions to the trial court to send defendant appropriate written notice of the prescriptive period for filing postconviction relief within 10 days and to file written proof that defendant received notice in the record of the proceedings.

 

1262 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Duhon v. Lafayette Consol. Gov't


05-657


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-657 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/30/05); 918 So. 2d 1114; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2647



December 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NUMBER 2004-3599. HONORABLE PATRICK MICHOT, PRESIDING.
Duhon v. Lafayette, 31 Fed. Appx. 838, 2002 U.S. App. LEXIS 3220 (5th Cir. La., 2002)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, several individuals, sued defendants, a parish government (the parish), and the State Land Office. The underlying issue was the boundary between two parishes and the residency of a candidate. Plaintiffs alleged, in part, that defendants relied on inaccurate surveys when determining the boundary. The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana, held suit was barred by res judicata. Plaintiffs sought review.


OVERVIEW: The underlying issue, which went back to 1999, had involved a dispute about whether a candidate for the parish government resided within said parish. The first state court lawsuit litigated the eligibility of said candidate. The instant court had held that his home was located in an adjacent parish. The issues in the present suit, as to the validity of an ordinance establishing the boundary, were not raised or litigated in the previous state court action. Moreover, the parish and the State Land Office were not parties to that suit. Plaintiffs had then brought suit in federal court alleging violations of their constitutional rights. However, the issues raised in the instant suit were not litigated in that action. Later, with respect to the ordinance, the trial court rescinded a temporary restraining order and denied a permanent injunction. The judgment was silent with regard to plaintiffs' request for a declaratory judgment as to whether said ordinance was constitutional. Ultimately, plaintiffs filed the instant suit, claiming fraud or mistake on the part of the government officials. Thus, the appellate court found the instant suit was not barred by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

NO. 2004 CA 1448


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1448 (La. App. 1 Cir. 12/29/05); 923 So. 2d 166; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2641



December 29, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by City of Baton Rouge v. Douglas, 929 So. 2d 1254, 2006 La. LEXIS 1839 (La., June 2, 2006)
Later proceeding at City of Baton Rouge v. Douglas, 984 So. 2d 746, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1294 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)
Writ of mandamus denied City of Baton Rouge v. Douglas, 60 So. 3d 1255, 2011 La. LEXIS 845 (La., 2011)
Motion denied by City of Baton Rouge v. Douglas, 75 So. 3d 912, 2011 La. LEXIS 2685 (La., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 466,636. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.
City of Baton Rouge v. Douglas, 800 So. 2d 448, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2248 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 28, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, ordered defendant city to reinstate plaintiff employee to his position at the Department of Public Works (DPW). The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated from his employment with DPW; however, he appealed his termination to the personnel board. After a hearing, the Board members could not agree on an appropriate punishment. Because there were not enough votes to impose either penalty considered, the Board ruled that the employee would be reinstated to his DPW position. Approximately 18 months after the appellate court rendered its original unpublished decision, another panel considered and decided another case. In that appeal, the appellate court decided that city had, by its own charter, limited its recourse as a juridical entity from adverse decisions of its own personnel board. Therefore, neither the district court nor the appellate court had subject matter jurisdiction. To resolve the conflict, the appellate court overruled its decision in the earlier appeal of this case.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Manuel v. Stalder


NO. 2004 CA 1920


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1920 (La. App. 1 Cir. 12/22/05); 928 So. 2d 24; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2597



December 22, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 489,482. The Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a petition for judicial review of the administrative decision recalculating his sentence after his parole was revoked after he was found guilty of a crime committed after he had been released on parole. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) dismissed the inmate's suit for judicial review, assigned a strike, and assessed costs against him. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was originally convicted and sentenced to a total of 15 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. At the time he was sentenced, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.14 was in effect. As a result of the revocation, he was required to serve the remainder of his original sentence due at the time of his release; i.e., approximately seven and a half years in addition to the new five-year sentence. The inmate claimed that the court erred in not restoring his earned good-time credits, in retroactively applying newer, more onerous and burdensome versions of §§ 15:571.14 and 15:571.4, and in assessing costs to him and assigning a strike against him. Inter alia, the appellate court held that an inmate whose conditional release was revoked upon his conviction for another felony was not entitled to credit against his sentence for time spent free under parole conditions. However, the district court erred in assigning a strike because the Prison Litigation Reform Act's (PLRA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1181-91, strike provisions did not apply because the inmate was challenging the duration of his custody and not a condition of his confinement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court dismissing the petition for judicial review without prejudice and assessing costs was affirmed. The portion of the judgment assigning a strike against the inmate was vacated. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the inmate.

Walker v. State through the Louisiana Legislature


No. 40,402-CW


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,402 (La. App. 2 Cir. 12/21/05); 917 So. 2d 1229; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2586



December 21, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Walker v. State, 917 So. 2d 1229, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 54 (La.App. 2 Cir., Jan. 19, 2006)
Writ denied by Walker v. State, 927 So. 2d 296, 2006 La. LEXIS 1476 (La., Apr. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Application for Writs from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 481701. Honorable John R. Harrison, Ad Hoc, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee attorney and former indigent defender board (IDB) member brought an action to judicially declare the statutes and procedures governing selection of IDB members unconstitutional or otherwise illegal. Appellant State, through judges, filed various exceptions including the exception of no right of action. The First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) denied the exception. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney alleged that the judges, empowered by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:144(B), involved themselves in the functioning of the IDB to the extent that by 2003 the judges effectively supervised and controlled the IDB's operations. The attorney claimed that such control violated the separation of powers between different branches of government in violation of La. Const. art. II, § 2. From that he argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:144 et seq., were facially unconstitutional. The appellate court held that it was difficult to imagine what class of plaintiff would have been appropriate to challenge the constitutionality of the statutes setting up a board to represent indigent defendants if the judges' argument was accepted. The attorney was a citizen and certainly could challenge the process. The trial court accurately interpreted La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1872 to require only a minimal threshold for standing for declaratory judgment relief and found that the attorney met the "person interested" requirement for standing under art. 1872. Under his allegation, the attorney had more than an expectation. Thus, the trial court correctly found that the attorney had a right of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Jefferson


NO. 2004-KA-1960


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1960 (La. App. 4 Cir. 12/21/05); 922 So. 2d 577; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2877



December 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 10, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Jefferson, 2006 La. LEXIS 3006 (La., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 441-813, SECTION "C". Honorable Benedict J. Willard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED, SENTENCES VACATED, AND REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) for attempted first degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27 and 14:30 and felon in possession of a firearm under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. Defendant was sentenced to 50 years at hard labor on count one and 15 years at hard labor on count two; the sentences were to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: An officer testified that he approached defendant as a suspicious person, and after some confrontation, defendant shot the officer four times. The court held that while defendant and the officer told dramatically different versions of the events, the State's witness could have viewed defendant on his knees as a struggle, and she also testified that others "rooted" defendant on to shoot the fallen officer. The evidence was sufficient to support a finding that the officer was acting as a peace officer at the time of the shooting because he was returning from court when he encountered defendant and he was attempting to handcuff defendant when he was shot. Given defendant's testimony that he shot at the officer's head because he was not sure the officer was wearing body armor, this supported a finding that he intended to kill the officer. The trial court properly excluded evidence of a misdemeanor charge against the officer as it happened two years after the shooting, and any possible relevance was substantially outweighed by the potential prejudice. The court remanded for resentencing because the trial court failed to set forth particular reasons for the consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the sentences and remanded.

State v. Persley


No. 40,271-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,271 (La. App. 2 Cir. 12/16/05); 918 So. 2d 491; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2580



December 16, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 208,524. Honorable Leon Emanuel, III, Judge.
State v. Mitchell, 894 So. 2d 1240, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 278 (La.App. 2 Cir., Feb. 17, 2005)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31 and sentenced him to 35 years imprisonment at heard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his manslaughter conviction, but the court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. There was a combination of physical evidence, both circumstantial and direct, and eyewitness testimony that was sufficient to carry the required burden. Defendant failed to identify specifically what evidence the State failed to provide that would have exculpated him and the record also evidenced that he was afforded time, when requested, to review the witnesses' statement. Thus, a mistrial was not warranted under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 729.5. Testimony based upon a witness's experience as an employee of a retail gun store who had to be generally familiar with firearms laws in order to operate the business was appropriate pursuant to La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 702. Although a witness's alleged confession to a new witness was partially corroborated by the evidence, the overwhelming weight of the evidence showed that defendant, in fact, fired the fatal shot in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and modified the sentence to delete the prohibition of parole.

State v. Price


NO. 40408-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40408 (La. App. 2 Cir. 12/16/05); 917 So. 2d 1201; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2582



December 16, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Price, 929 So. 2d 1284, 2006 La. LEXIS 1985 (La., June 16, 2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Price v. Cain, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23474 (W.D. La., Mar. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 02F2236. Honorable Carl Van Sharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana that convicted him of aggravated rape, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, and that sentenced him to serve the mandatory term of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his offense involved minimal force which did not justify punishment in the greater degree as an aggravated rape. The court held that defendant's conviction for aggravated rape was supported by sufficient evidence that showed he forced the victim to perform oral sex on him, she was prevented from resisting the act by threats of great and immediate bodily harm, and that the victim testified that when she attempted to escape, he picked her up and slammed her to the floor. Also La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:41, 42, and 42.1 had been amended to add oral sexual intercourse to the crimes of forcible rape and aggravated rape. The court noted that the difference between aggravated rape and forcible rape was the degree of force employed and the extent to which the victim resisted, and that the determination of the grade of rape was for the jury to decide. The court rejected defendant's Batson challenge where there was nothing in the record that established defendant had made out a prima facie case of discriminatory purpose. The court also held that the mandatory life sentence was not excessive and that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for mistrial.


OUTCOME: . The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Ralph v. City of New Orleans


NO. 2004-CA-1270


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1270 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/14/05); 921 So. 2d 988; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2847



December 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2006.
Reversed by, Remanded by Ralph v. City of New Orleans, 928 So. 2d 537, 2006 La. LEXIS 1431 (La., May 5, 2006)
Writ granted by Ralph v. City of New Orleans, 2006 La. LEXIS 1440 (La., May 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Civil District Court, Orleans Parish. NO. 2003-9871, Division "J". Honorable Louis A. DiRosa, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged defendant city's ordinance. The taxpayers sought to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional, and to also to enjoin the city from extending health care benefits to the registered partners of city employees. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted the city's peremptory exceptions of no right of action, no interest, and no cause of action. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers' factual allegations included the following: (1) the city's chief administrative officer announced that same sex domestic partnership coverage was now available and announced the utilization of a domestic partnership registry; (2) the city council adopted and codified the domestic partner benefits provision by enacting New Orleans, Louisiana, Code of Ordinances, ch. 87, § 87-1 et seq. As to the exception of no right of action/want of interest pursuant La. Code Civ. Pro. Ann. 681, the appellate court agreed with the trial court that the taxpayers were required to make a showing that there was an effect upon the public fisc by the government action in question; then and only then would the taxpayers demonstrate an interest sufficient to afford a right of action. The taxpayers failed to establish the minimal requisite interest.

1270 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Caldwell Wholesale Co. v. Smith


NO. 40,369-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,369 (La. App. 2 Cir. 12/14/05); 916 So. 2d 1255; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2573



December 14, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Caldwell Wholesale Co. v. Smith, 2006 La. LEXIS 1215 (La., Apr. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 458060. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former employee appealed a judgment from the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, that dismissed his reconventional demand seeking medical expenses, permanent and total disability (PTD) benefits, penalties and attorney fees based on its finding that the employee's medical problems of stroke and ischemic colitis, and his PTD were unrelated to his 1980 work-related heart attack.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed the insurer should have paid his medical expenses for a stroke and colitis and PTD benefits because those conditions were secondary to the same disease process that caused his work-related heart attack in 1980. The trial court did not err in concluding that the employee was not entitled to workers' compensation for medical expenses for his stroke and colitis, and disability benefits where medical experts testified that his medical problems and disability resulted from the progression of his atherosclerotic disease, accelerated by his failure to reduce his risk factors, and were not the result of his heart attack as provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(8)(a). However, the trial court did err in failing to make findings of fact regarding the employee's claim for reimbursement of the amount the insurer reduced his weekly workers' compensation payments as an offset against his Social Security old-age benefits because the statutory authority for such an offset, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1225(C), had been held unconstitutional. Also, reimbursement of the offset should have been retroactive to when the offset commenced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the trial court judgment that denied the employee's claim for reimbursement of the offset against his Social Security old-age benefits, and amended the judgment to order reimbursement to the employee. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects and assessed the costs of the appeal to the employer and insurer.

 

1271 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Casby


NO. 2005-K-1181, NO. 2005-K-1222 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2005-K-1223 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2005-K-1237


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1181 (La. App. 4 Cir. 12/14/05); 921 So. 2d 181; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2855



December 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Casby, 927 So. 2d 309, 2006 La. LEXIS 1602 (La., May 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATIONS FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-972, SECTION "D". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE AND NOS. 428-498, 413-173 AND 266-560, SECTION "C". HONORABLE BENEDICT J. WILLARD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Writ of applications is granted


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In four consolidated actions, appellant State of Louisiana filed writ applications directed to the Criminal District Court of the Orleans Parish No. 3, Louisiana, challenging the order that the State file a petition to have appellee criminal defendants civilly committed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue raised by the State in the writ applications was whether the trial court erred when it directed the State to file a petition to have defendants civilly committed. The State argued that defendants' commitment pursuant to the Louisiana Code of Criminal Procedure was legal, and that the trial court should continue to conduct periodic reviews of defendants' condition pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 648 et seq., without the need for the filing of a new petition. The appellate court ruled that the trial court erred. There was nothing in the Louisiana Code of Criminal Procedure, in Title 28 of the Louisiana Revised Statutes, or in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:211(A) which required the State to file a formal petition for a civil commitment once the trial court had determined under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 648(B)(3) that a criminal defendant was unlikely in the foreseeable future to regain his capacity to proceed. The statutes had not been amended to impose such a requirement in the years since the trial court first found that the criminal defendants were unrestorably incompetent and dangerous, as required to designate continued commitment as "civil."


OUTCOME: The State's writ applications were granted, and the trial court's orders were vacated.

State v. Jarreau


NO. 2005-KA-0355


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0355 (La. App. 4 Cir. 12/14/05); 921 So. 2d 155; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2859



December 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2006.
Writ denied by State v. Jarreau, 929 So. 2d 1267, 2006 La. LEXIS 1920 (La., June 14, 2006)
Appeal after remand at State v. Jarreau, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 458 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 403-391, SECTION "H". HONORABLE CAMILLE BURAS, JUDGE.
State v. Jarreau, 810 So. 2d 585, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3408 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 27, 2001)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of the possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, and sentenced him to life under a former version of the Habitual Offender Law (Law), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's case involved an appeal regarding the length of the sentence received by him under the Law as it was in effect on November 25, 1998, the date that defendant committed a third offense under the statute. Defendant was sentenced to life in prison without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, and he appealed that sentence as excessive. The court vacated and remanded for resentencing, stating that it found that the imposed sentence at the age of 50 made no measurable contribution to acceptable goals of punishment. It appeared from the face of the record that the life sentence was grossly out of proportion to the severity of the crime and the harm to society that it caused. Additionally, defendant would have faced a maximum of 10 years in prison under the current Law, and the court found that on the face of the record, the sentence that he received could have been shocking to the conscience when that fact was considered.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. Defendant was to be resentenced after a presentence investigation had been obtained and after the trial court made a determination of whether the minimum sentence in effect at the time defendant committed the crime of possession was constitutionally excessive.

 

1273 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


NO. 2005-KA-0431


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0431 (La. App. 4 Cir. 12/07/05); 921 So. 2d 139; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2857



December 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 443-943, SECTION "B". HONORABLE LYNDA VAN DAVIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED, SENTENCES VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, (Louisiana) that convicted him of second-degree battery and attempted false imprisonment while armed with a dangerous weapon; and that imposed concurrent 5 year sentences at hard labor on each count with the battery sentence to be served without benefit of parole, pursuant to the firearm enhancement statute, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his enhanced sentence without parole eligibility pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.3 for the battery conviction violated his Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial under the Apprendi rule. The court noted that the statutory maximum for second-degree battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1, was 5 years at hard labor with no limit on parole eligibility, and that the firearm enhancement statute, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.3, merely provided for the imposition of a mandatory minimum sentence when a firearm was used. The court held that Article 893.3 did not provide for a separate sentence in addition to the sentence imposed for the battery; therefore defendant's enhanced sentence presented an Apprendi rule violation because it was a more severe sentence than the five-year sentence with no restriction on parole eligibility allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1. The court held that the trial court, not the jury, found defendant used a firearm in the commission of the battery that resulted in a more severe sentence than the jury's findings alone would have permitted. The court vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated his sentence on the second-degree battery count and remanded the case for re-sentencing on that count consistent with the opinion. The court affirmed defendant's sentence on the attempted false imprisonment count but directed the trial court to issue a new commitment order consistent with the transcript that reflected parole was not restricted.
