State v. Chestnut


NO. 05-KA-220


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


05-220 (La. App. 5 Cir. 11/29/05); 917 So. 2d 573; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2496



November 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-4465, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish (Louisiana), convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated, third offense, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98, upon defendant's guilty plea. When defendant pled guilty he specifically reserved his rights to appeal the trial court's denial of his motion to quash, asserting the invalidity of one of the predicate offenses used to enhance his offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that a predicate offense was invalid because the ad hoc judge who took his plea in that case was not an elected judge and, hence, did not have authority to accept his plea; and the ad hoc judge in that case failed to properly advise him of his constitutional rights before accepting the guilty plea. Defendant failed to cite any ruling that denied the authority of a duly-appointed ad hoc or pro tempore judge to accept a guilty plea. Defendant argued that the Waiver of Rights form submitted by the State as proof of the predicate conviction revealed that the form failed to include an advisement of defendant's presumption of innocence and/or the fact that the state carried the burden of proving his guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant contended the fact that such an advisement was not contained in the form showed that the ad hoc judge neglected to advise him of that right. Any failure of the court to advise defendant of the presumption of innocence did not invalidate his plea for enhancement purposes. The trial court properly denied his motion to quash. The court was not required to inform defendant that he was presumed innocent until proven guilty.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1275 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scott


2005 KA 0325


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0325 (La. App. 1 Cir. 11/04/05); 927 So. 2d 441; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2342



November 4, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. Docket No. 3-97-219. Honorable William A. Morvant, Judge Presiding.
State v. Scott, 769 So. 2d 1286, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2917 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 3, 2000)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which sentenced him to life imprisonment as a third felony habitual offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 following his conviction of possession of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C). Defendant asserted that the statutorily mandated life sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not file a motion to reconsider the sentence with the trial court. The court noted that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 881.1(E) and 881.2(A)(1), the failure to make such a motion precluded defendant from raising an objection to the sentence on appeal. The court determined that it would nonetheless examine the sentence for excessiveness because it was necessary to do so as part of the analysis of defendant's allegation of ineffective of counsel in failing to file the motion. The court rejected defendant's argument that changes in the Habitual Offender Law required a reduction of his sentence. Without proof that defendant's history was an exceptional one, the prospective change in that law was not enough to justify any downward departure in sentencing. Defendant did not prove by clear and convincing evidence that he was exceptional to the extent that a mandatory life sentence was not meaningfully tailored to his culpability, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the case. Thus, defendant did not meet his burden of showing that the sentence would have reasonably been different absent defense counsel's failure to file a motion to reconsider sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence.

State v. Joseph


05-186


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-186 (La. App. 3 Cir. 11/02/05); 916 So. 2d 378; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2294



November 2, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. LANDRY, NO. 03K4336A. HONORABLE JAMES T. GENOVESE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION FOR ONE COUNT OF ARMED ROBBERY REVERSED AND JUDGMENT OF ACQUITTAL ORDERED; SENTENCES VACATED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which convicted him, following a guilty plea, of two counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and one count of aggravated burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60 and which ordered him to pay restitution as required by law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with a co-defendant, kicked down the front door and entered a woman's home. Once inside, defendant took a gun from the woman, while the co-defendant struck another occupant of the home with a bottle of bleach before taking money from her possession. On appeal, the court first noted that the trial court's failure to state the amount of restitution rendered defendant's sentence indeterminate and thus illegal. The court next addressed defendant's argument that the factual basis established at the guilty plea hearing was sufficient to support only one count of armed robbery, rather than two counts as charged. Defendant contended that the only item taken from the woman was a handgun, and that subsequent to his taking of that weapon, no item of value was taken from her. The "taking" upon which the charge of armed robbery was based was the gun taken from the woman. The court first stated that the facts clearly supported the plea of guilty to the charge of aggravated burglary. The court next determined, however, that charging defendant with both aggravated burglary and armed robbery, based upon the same set of facts, clearly violated the "same evidence" test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for one count of armed robbery and ordered a judgment of acquittal entered on the record. The court vacated defendant's sentences for the convictions of the remaining count of armed robbery and aggravated burglary and remanded the case with instructions for resentencing.

State v. Runyon


05-36 consolidated with 05-104


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-36 (La. App. 3 Cir. 11/02/05); 916 So. 2d 407; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2320



November 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Reported at State v. McDonald, 916 So. 2d 431, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2274 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 2, 2005)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Runyon v. State, 936 So. 2d 207, 2006 La. LEXIS 2442 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)
Writ denied by State v. Runyon, 942 So. 2d 526, 2006 La. LEXIS 3237 (La., Nov. 17, 2006)
Appeal after remand at State v. Runyon, 944 So. 2d 820, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2734 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CATAHOULA, NOS. 03-736 and 03-817. HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants one and two appealed their convictions and sentences in the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Catahoula (Louisiana). Defendant one was convicted of manslaughter and attempted second degree murder. Defendant two was convicted of second degree murder and attempted second degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were fishing with friends, and an altercation occurred when another party arrived, resulting in the death of one victim and the serious injury of another victim. Defendant one testified that he struck the victim in the back of the head with a piece of wood because the victim, who was intoxicated, was beating up a friend. It was defendant two that had the knife. The court affirmed in part and held that a rational trier could have determined that defendant one's hitting the victim satisfied the requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31(A)(1). As to attempted second degree murder, the court found that it was unlikely that defendant one inflicted any of the injured victim's wounds and further, the evidence established that defendant one's attempts to stab that victim were in response to the victim hitting him. Therefore, the lesser included offense of aggravated battery was appropriate. The court held that considering the location, number, and severity of the wounds, the jury could have inferred that defendant two had the specific intent to kill both victims. There was a lack of physical evidence that one of the victim's tried to drown defendant two.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant one's conviction for manslaughter and reversed his conviction for attempted second degree murder. Both sentences were vacated, and the case was remanded. The court affirmed both of defendant two's convictions, but the sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for re-sentencing.

State v. Day


05-287


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-287 (La. App. 3 Cir. 11/02/05); 915 So. 2d 950; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2324



November 2, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR-217-04. HONORABLE STUART S. KAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of possession of methamphetamine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. He was sentenced by the 36th Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana) to pay a $ 1,000 fine and serve 60 months at hard labor, with 12 months suspended. Defendant was further sentenced to five years of supervised probation after his prison term to be served consecutively to a previous sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that his sentence was excessive. The court considered the "ample consideration" that defendant received in his plea agreement with the State. Defendant received a great benefit through his plea agreement, which reduced his total sentencing exposure from 20 years to 5 years. The district court noted that defendant was a second felony offender. The court's review of the record indicated that defendant previously pled guilty to six counts of distribution of marijuana and one count of possession of marijuana pursuant to a plea agreement in which the State dismissed charges on three counts of possession of a firearm while in possession of marijuana. Maximum sentences should be reserved for the most egregious and blameworthy of offenders. Defendant fell within that category. Defendant alleged that the district court erred in ordering that his sentence should run consecutively to the seven-year sentence he received in 1999. As the district judge clearly designated that the sentences be served consecutively, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 883, the imposition of consecutive sentences by the district court was not an abuse of its sentencing discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed. However, regarding the conditions of defendant's probation following his prison term, the matter was remanded, and the district court was instructed to specify a payment schedule for the fees ordered as conditions of defendant's probation.

State v. Shumaker


No. 40,275-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,275 (La. App. 2 Cir. 10/28/05); 914 So. 2d 1156; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2272



October 28, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Shumaker, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2815 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 236,795. Honorable Michael R. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of an attempt to create or operate a clandestine laboratory for the unlawful manufacture of a Schedule II controlled dangerous substance (CDS) under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:983. The First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) denied defendant's post-trial motions for new trial, post-verdict judgment of acquittal, and arrest of judgment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that § 40:983 was unconstitutional. The most limiting factor of the defined crime was its requirement for proof of the unlawful manufacture of a CDS. Regardless of the fact that many common household items might be possessed by a person accused of the instant crime, the process of manufacturing, which the state's expert witness described in elaborate detail, entailed a complicated course of conduct. Such conduct demonstrated the intent to manufacture the CDS was much more than possession of common household items. Thus, the illegal activity proscribed by the statute was narrow and gave adequate notice to those who would engage in such manufacturing activities that the conduct was proscribed. The finding that defendant did not conspire to manufacture methamphetamine did not conflict with the finding that he attempted to create or operate a clandestine laboratory with the intent to manufacture methamphetamine. Inter alia, the appellate court also held that because the search of the house appeared to have been primarily limited to common areas, the babysitter had authority or at least apparent authority to give consent to search those areas.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Sims


No. 40,300-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,300 (La. App. 2 Cir. 10/26/05); 914 So. 2d 594; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2235



October 26, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 124,647. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress, but his motion was denied. Defendant entered a plea, before the 26th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, to possession of over 28 grams of cocaine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The guilty plea was entered with the reservation that defendant would be allowed to appeal the denial of the pre-trial motion to suppress. Nevertheless, the grounds raised in the memorandum to support the motion to suppress never included the assertion that the initial stop was illegal. Instead, the basis for the motion to suppress was that the detention after the traffic stop ended was prolonged, and, under the circumstances, the consent was not voluntary. Therefore, the issue was not properly before the appellate court. Nevertheless, the appellate court continued to analyze defendant's argument, and it concluded that a trooper's belief that defendant was in violation of a window tinting statute was sufficient to justify the traffic stop. Further, a video made of the stop indicated that there was no coercion that preceded defendant's consent to search under the totality of the circumstances. As to defendant's sentence, the suspension of a fine was part of the plea bargain, and the trial court specifically found defendant to be indigent; therefore, it was a viable option to decline to impose a fine.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Bd. of Dirs. v. All Taxpayers


2005 CA 1935


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1935 (La. App. 1 Cir. 10/07/05);  929 So. 2d 743; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2199



October 7, 2005, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
 
Writ granted by Bd. of Dirs. v. All Taxpayers, 922 So. 2d 525, 2006 La. LEXIS 265 (La., Jan. 27, 2006)
Affirmed by Bd. of Dirs. of the Indus. Dev. Bd. v. All Taxpayers, 2006 La. LEXIS 2312 (La., Sept. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd Judicial District Court. Parish of Ascension, Louisiana. Docket No. 81281, Division "E". Honorable Alvin Turner, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Board of Directors of the Industrial Development Board of the City of Gonzales, Louisiana, filed a petition for a motion for judgment under the Louisiana Bond Validation Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:5121-:5130. The 23rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Ascension, Louisiana issued a bond validation judgment. Appellant residents challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The residents owned sporting goods stores; they contended that the use of public funds to finance a competing retail sporting goods store was unconstitutional. The residents further urged that the Tax Increment Financing Act (TIF Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:9038.1-.10, did not provide the authority for the project. The appellate court declined to read the TIF Act as limiting governmental assistance to only those aspects of an economic development project falling within the ambit of public works and infrastructure. The TIF Act specifically authorized public assistance to economic development projects involving the private retail industry. As to whether the funding scheme amounted to a donation of public funds prohibited by La. Const. art. VII, § 14(A), in this instance the funding was not strictly gratuitous. The residents did not meet their burden of showing that the constitution prohibited legislation that would allow local governments to promote economic development. The residents also made an equal protection challenge, but the TIF Act was rationally related to the legitimate governmental purposes of economic development and enhancement of future revenues.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1282 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. Easter


NO. 2005 CW 0441


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0441 (La. App. 1 Cir. 09/23/05); 914 So. 2d 586; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2080



September 23, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Warren v. Easter, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2529 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 18th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 58,808. Honorable J. Robin Free, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a state prison inmate, filed an application for supervisory review of a judgment from the 18th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), which rejected the inmate's constitutional challenge to a stay of proceedings in a medical malpractice action brought against defendant state employees.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted a defense motion to stay the matter pursuant to Louisiana's Prison Litigation Reform Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186B(2) (as amended by 2002 La. Acts 1st Ex. Sess. No. 89, § 2), until the inmate paid all court costs accrued after the effective date of the statute's amendment. The inmate argued that the automatic stay provision violated his right of access to the courts as guaranteed by La. Const. art. I, § 22 and was contrary to the equal protection guaranteed in La. Const. art. I, § 3. The court found no merit in the inmate's arguments, observing that the automatic stay provision did not affect any suspect class or involve any fundamental right and was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of lessening the burdens presented by nuisance prisoner suits. Thus, the provision neither violated equal protection guarantees nor unconstitutionally impaired a prisoner's right of access to the courts. Moreover, enforcing a stay of litigation as to those costs incurred after the effective date of 2002 La. Acts 1st Ex. Sess. No. 89, § 2 was appropriate and did not constitute an unconstitutional retroactive application of the law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's application for supervisory review.

 

1283 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kirby v. Field


NO. 2004 CA 1898


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1898 (La. App. 1 Cir. 9/23/05);  923 So. 2d 131; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2092



September 23, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Kirby v. Field, 2006 La. LEXIS 1076 (La., Mar. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 516,150. The Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In January 22, 2004, appellant patient brought a medical malpractice action seeking damages against appellee doctor for treatment rendered in the fall of 1997. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) sustained the doctor's dilatory exception of prematurity and the peremptory exceptions, and dismissed the patient's cause of action with prejudice. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: Review of the factual allegations of the petition revealed significant deficiency in factual particularity, particularly as to allegations of facts constituting fraud. Inter alia, the patient failed to allege that the doctor had knowledge of his failure to remove the entire length of the catheter before stating that the procedure was "successful," when and how the doctor acquired that knowledge, that the misrepresentation was deliberate, and when and how the misrepresentation was made. The relevant circumstances of how the doctor managed to conceal his purported knowledge and to prevent the patient from discovering the alleged malpractice were not alleged with any particularity. Thus, even if those allegations were technically uncontroverted they could not be accepted as true for purposes of determining the issue of prescription. Even if the appellate court generously accepted the date of the alleged malpractice as the last day of fall, the complaint was still instituted almost six years after the date of the alleged malpractice, well beyond both the one-year prescriptive period and the statutory three-year period of repose generally applicable to all claims of medical malpractice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court sustaining the peremptory exception as to the objection of prescription and dismissing the petition of the patient was affirmed, but the judgment was amended in part to vacate that portion of the judgment sustaining the dilatory exception of prematurity and the peremptory exception as to the objection of no cause of action as moot. All costs of the appeal were assessed to the patient.

 

1284 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hite v. Larpenter


2004 CA 1821


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1821 (La. App. 1 Cir. 9/23/05);  923 So. 2d 140; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2096



September 23, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Hite v. Larpenter, 925 So. 2d 511, 2006 La. LEXIS 857 (La., Mar. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne, State of Louisiana. No. 134,627. The Honorable Randall L. Bethancourt, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a program under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:708, a prisoner in the custody of appellee sheriff was washing the floor of a police station. Appellant police department dispatcher slipped on the wet floor and sued the sheriff and appellee, the sheriff's department's insurer. The 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana) granted summary judgment to the sheriff, dismissing the dispatcher's claims. The dispatcher appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the dispatcher argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:708, which authorized parish sheriffs to allow prisoners to voluntarily perform manual labor in public buildings, was inapplicable. She argued that since the sheriff did not retain custody of the prisoner, the statute did not apply because he should somehow have been in control of the prisoner at all times. Particularly, she argued that the statute was never intended to apply to situations where prisoners performed manual labor or otherwise walked around without supervision by the sheriff's department. The appellate court disagreed and concluded that § 15:708 was applicable. The language of § 15:708(A)(1)(a) clearly allowed the sheriff to put prisoners to work performing manual labor in public buildings. Nothing in the language of the statute made the statute inapplicable should the sheriff delegate control of the prisoner to trained officers of a fellow law enforcement agency or to any other person or agency. Applying the plain language of § 15:708, the statute governed authorized labor by prisoners held by a Louisiana sheriff's department.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs were assessed to the dispatcher.

 

1285 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Randell


NO. 40,014-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


40,014 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/21/05); 911 So. 2d 393; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2060



September 21, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Randell, 2006 La. LEXIS 2404 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 221261. Honorable Charles R. Scott, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of purse-snatching in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. He was adjudicated a third felony offender and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. He appealed, asserting that although his sentence was statutorily mandated under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, that same was unduly harsh and unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the habitual offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, under which defendant was sentenced, had been held constitutional on numerous occasions. Further, to merit a deviation below the mandatory minimum sentence, a defendant had to clearly and convincingly show that he was "exceptional" as downward departures were to occur only in rare instances. In the instant case, defendant did not argue that he was exceptional. Rather, his only contention was that his offenses had not been very violent. However, he had been convicted of simple robbery on two prior occasions, and in the instant matter, he was convicted of purse snatching. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13) specifically enumerated both "purse snatching" and "simple robbery" as "crimes of violence" for purposes of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. In addition, his lengthy criminal history included a variety of felonies. Thus, defendant failed to show that his case was exceptional or extraordinary in any way, or that he deserved a lenient sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1286 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garrison


No. 39,820-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,820 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/08/05); 911 So. 2d 346; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2031



September 8, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Garrison, 913 So. 2d 888, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2227 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 20, 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Garrison, 2006 La. LEXIS 1242 (La., Apr. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 50776. Honorable Jay Bowen McCallum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress evidence was denied, he pled guilty to driving while intoxicated, third offense. The Third Judicial District Court for Lincoln Parish, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to three years at hard labor, with all but 30 days suspended, and placed him on three years supervised probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence, arguing that the university police officer had no jurisdiction off campus, and even if he did, he did not have a reasonable basis to stop defendant. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the one and a half blocks off campus on route to an off-site campus parking lot qualified as being contiguous to the perimeter of the parking lot as well as the main campus, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1805(A)(3). In considering the reasonableness of the stop at issue in this case, the appellate court noted that this was not a checkpoint stop. Rather, at 11:00 p.m., the officer heard a disturbance of public concern. The officer observed one vehicle leaving the area and stopped that vehicle to ask the occupant and driver what he may have seen or heard. The officer had no intent to arrest or even ticket defendant. There was a public concern, and the intrusion was minimal. As such, there was no discriminatory action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n


NO. 2005 CA 1142, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1143, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1144, CONSOLIDATED WITH 2005 CA 1145, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1146, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1147, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1148, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1149, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1150, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1151, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1152, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1153, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1154, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1155, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1156, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1157, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1158, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1159, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1160, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1161, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1162, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1163, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1164, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1165, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1166, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1167, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1168, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2005 CA 1169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005-1142 (La. App. 1 Cir. 9/7/05); 923 So. 2d 81; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2030



September 7, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. 925 So. 2d 547, 2006 La. LEXIS 979 (La., Mar. 17, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 549 U.S. 822, 127 S. Ct. 157, 166 L. Ed. 2d 38, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5863 (2006)
Writ denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 957 So. 2d 160, 2007 La. LEXIS 1405 (La., 2007)
Remanded by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 997 So. 2d 92, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1329 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)
Related proceeding at Odom v. Southern Natural Gas Co., 72 So. 3d 437, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 978 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 868 So. 2d 950, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 347 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED. DAMAGES FOR FRIVOLOUS APPEAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pipeline companies appealed a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which determined that defendant Louisiana Tax Commission had administered the ad valorem tax scheme in a manner that violated the uniformity requirement of the Louisiana Constitution. The appeal concerned the appropriate remedy.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs owned interstate natural gas transmission pipelines in Louisiana that were classified and taxed as public service properties under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851(K) and (M). The pipelines of public service companies were assessed by local assessors at 15 percent of fair market value while the public service properties of plaintiffs were assessed at 25 percent of fair market value. The court held that the trial court correctly remanded the matter to the Commission and that on remand, it was within the province of the Commission to correct errors in the appraisal and/or assessment of public service properties under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1837. Plaintiffs filed protests with the Commission and filed the instant suit seeking refund of taxes paid under protest, and the court held that plaintiffs could not now argue that the doctrines of res judicata and collateral estoppel precluded reassessment of the properties. Reassessment did not violate plaintiffs' due process rights because they would have ample opportunity to object, if necessary, to the local assessors' valuations. Therefore, the remedy ordered by the trial court was both just and equitable.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment to provide that the Commission would issue to plaintiffs a full refund of the taxes paid under protest. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment.

 

1288 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers


2005 CA 1684


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1684 (La. App. 1 Cir. 8/25/05);  927 So. 2d 328; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2018



August 25, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ granted by Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 2006 La. LEXIS 1284 (La., Apr. 17, 2006)
Affirmed by Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 2006 La. LEXIS 2881 (La., Oct. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of Livingston State of Louisiana. Docket No. 108121. Honorable Zorraine M. Waguespack, Judge Presiding.
Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 894 So. 2d 325, 2005 La. LEXIS 327 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AND AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee economic development district sought judicial validation of bonds and the means of securing and paying them. Appellant taxpayers appealed the judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana) in favor of the economic development district, holding that the individual taxpayers' challenge to a resolution proposing the bond issuance, and related proceedings, was untimely.


OVERVIEW: The motion to strike essentially claimed that the 30-day time limit, provided in La. Const. art. VI, § 35(B) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.4L for a challenge to the validity of the bond resolutions and related proceedings, was a peremptive period that had already run before the individual tax payers filed their answer. Thus, their right to challenge was extinguished. The taxpayers conceded that the trial court ruled not on the merits, but on the issue of peremption raised by the motion to strike. Thus, the motion to strike was more akin to a peremptory exception raising the objection of no cause of action or of prescription. Essentially, a hearing on the claim of peremption was held, and the trial court ruled that the challenge was not timely. The appellate court found no violation of due process rights. However, to the extent that the trial court held that a challenge to the legality of the election or elections at issue was perempted, it erred. Such a challenge was timely if brought within 60 days after promulgation of the result of the election pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 35(A) because the election occurred more than 30 days after the publication of the resolution.


OUTCOME: Any holding by the trial court that a challenge to the legality of the election was perempted was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed. The costs of the appeal were assessed to the taxpayers.

 

1289 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 39,969-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,969 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/17/05); 909 So. 2d 672; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1970



August 17, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Lee, 936 So. 2d 195, 2006 La. LEXIS 2399 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lee v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 122274 (W.D. La., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 117,553. Honorable Bruce Martin Bolin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a trial for the crime of aggravated burglary, a jury, before the 26th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, convicted defendant of the responsive verdict of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: One of the victims returned home to find defendant in her house without permission. As she tried to escape, defendant grabbed her. Defendant attempted to argue on appeal that the evidence was insufficient; however, the State proved that defendant made an unauthorized entry into the victims' home with the intent to commit a felony or any theft. While in the victims' home, defendant committed a battery upon one of the victims. Although the defendant claimed that he was not the person who committed the crime, the State negated any reasonable probability of misidentification, and established the defendant's identity as the burglar by testimony and physical evidence, including fingerprint identification. The jury obviously rejected defendant's explanation of how his fingerprints were found inside the victims' home. Defendant failed to rebut the presumption that his mandatory minimum sentence was constitutional. Finally, a review of the record did not show that trial counsel's representation fell below the standard of reasonableness and competency as required by prevailing professional standards demanded for attorneys in criminal cases.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1290 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. Brian Harris Autoplex


2004 CA 1316


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1316 (La. App. 1 Cir. 08/03/05) 923 So. 2d 17; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1906



August 3, 2005, Date of Judgment


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM DISTRICT 6. OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. (NUMBER 02-08224), STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ELIZABETH A. WARREN, OWC JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (OWC), District 6, (Louisiana) dismissed appellant employee's claim for benefits and granted relief to appellee employer, ordering forfeiture of the employee's right to compensation benefits as a result of his willful misrepresentation of his prior medical history. The employee was also ordered to pay restitution totaling $ 11,130. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that because he was consistent and credible in his testimony about his hemorrhoid problems, the OWC erred in finding he had violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208. The employee fell at work and although he immediately sought treatment for his rectal bleeding, he did not seek treatment for lower back, buttock, and left leg pain until two months later on July 23, 2002. He testified that prior to July 23, 2002, he had never had a problem with or received treatment for hemorrhoids. But the employer submitted medical records showing that beginning in June 1990, he had received medical attention for hemorrhoids. The medical records provided a reasonable factual basis to support the finding that the employee's statement was false and that the misrepresentation was willful and that the employee misrepresented his hemorrhoid history for the purpose of obtaining benefits. His claim for additional benefits associated with his lower back, buttock, and left leg pain exposed him to the risk that if he revealed the history of hemorrhoids, his employer would have denied him medical and indemnity benefits for that claim and sought a refund of what had already been paid.


OUTCOME: The denial of the employee's declinatory exception raising the objection of subject matter jurisdiction, the dismissal of his claim for benefits, and the order of forfeiture of workers' compensation benefits were affirmed. That portion of the judgment, awarding the employer restitution was amended to reduce the award. That portion of the judgment awarding the employer $ 500 in attorney fees was reversed. Appeal costs were assessed equally.

 

1291 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Couvillion


NO. 05-KA-5


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


05-5 (La. App. 5 Cir. 07/26/05); 910 So. 2d 991; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1862



July 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 27, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-0103, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE ROBERT A. CHAISSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with second degree murder. The jury in the 29th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Division "E" (Louisiana) returned a responsive verdict of guilty of manslaughter, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31. After denying defendant's motion for a new trial and for a post-verdict judgment of acquittal, the trial judge sentenced him to imprisonment at hard labor for 25 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion for new trial or for judgment of acquittal and erred in imposing an excessive sentence. The jury was instructed as to both theories of manslaughter as set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31(A). Defendant conceded that § 14:31(A)(2)(a) applied with the intentional misdemeanor being simple battery, when defendant punched the victim in the face while he was being brutally strangled. The doctor who performed the autopsy, testified that the cause of the victim's death was ligature strangulation and denied that he had died as a result of later being dropped from an overpass. The jury could have found the testimony of the doctor who conducted the autopsy more credible than that of defendant's expert. Also, the record reflected that the victim appeared to have been dead prior to his body being thrown over the overpass, as stated in a co-defendant's testimony and recorded statement. Likewise, according to defendant's statement, another co-defendant checked the victim and concluded he was dead before his body was thrown from the overpass. There was sufficient evidence to support the manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1292 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


NO. 2005-KA-0375


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0375 (La. App. 4 Cir. 07/20/05); 913 So. 2d 836; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1879



July 20, 2005, Judgment Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 2005.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 2008 La. LEXIS 132 (La., Jan. 11, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 450-898, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant was convicted of possession of crack cocaine, simple escape, and aggravated battery, in the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana. Pursuant to the State's bill of information, defendant was later adjudicated a quadruple offender. Defendant appealed, asserting the trial court erred in adjudicating him as quadruple multiple offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the due process requirements of the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, specifically La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, were not complied with. However, the appellate court found that he had filed a motion to quash the multiple bill and a full hearing was held. Thus, the requirements for an arraignment, an opportunity to file objections, and a hearing were met. Secondly, under Apprendi v. New Jersey, a defendant's prior convictions were not required to be submitted to a jury. In addition, all the issues raised by defendant concerning the predicate offenses were properly determined by reviewing the documents submitted in support of the multiple bill. Third, defendant asserted the State failed to prove the sufficiency and validity of his prior guilty pleas. However, the appellate court held that the State met its burden of proving same, his identity thereon (in part through his fingerprint record), and the fact that less than 10 years had elapsed between convictions with respect to § 15:529.1. Finally, defendant failed to preserve the issue of whether his sentence was excessive because he had failed to object and he failed to file a motion to reconsider sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence as a multiple offender were affirmed.

 

1293 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Helmers v. Fernandez Nursing Home, Inc.


NO. 2004-CA-0201


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-0201 (La. App. 4 Cir. 7/06/05); 914 So. 2d 556; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1919



July 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 2005.
Writ denied by Helmers v. Fernandez Nursing Home, Inc., 2006 La. LEXIS 611 (La., Feb. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM ST. BERNARD 34TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 93-194, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE JACQUES A. SANBORN, JUDGE.
Helmers v. Fernandez Nursing Home, Inc., 882 So. 2d 35, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2074 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 11, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the family members of a deceased patient, brought a survival and wrongful death action against appellee nursing home, claiming the patient sustained a decubitus ulcer and other serious injuries leading to his death as a result of the nursing home's negligence. The 34th Judicial District Court of St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana, granted the nursing home's exception of prescription. The family appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the family asserted that the trial court erred when it failed to apply the appropriate prescriptive period. In opposition, the nursing home submitted that the family's attempt to classify the claim under Louisiana's Nursing Home Residents' Bill of Rights, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2010.6 et seq., as contractual was incorrect because there had been no showing that a contract between the nursing home and the patient and/or his family ever existed. The appellate court agreed with the nursing home that the family failed to establish their contract claim as there was no evidence that a written contract existed with the patient. Further, because the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2010.9(C) did not shorten the one-year prescriptive period provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628, there was no disturbance of vested rights in the retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2010.9(C). The family was aware of the patient's claim on January 8, 1999 when he was removed from the nursing home. Applying either statute, the family's cause of action against the nursing home prescribed in January of 2000. The petition for damages filed in May of 2001 was, therefore, untimely.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1294 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Plainview Area Ass'n v. State


CA 04-1221


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1221 (La. App. 3 Cir. 06/30/05); 907 So. 2d 923; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1759



June 29, 2005, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF SABINE, NO. 48,239. HONORABLE ROBERT EDWARD BURGESS, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Plainview Area Ass'n v. State, 900 So. 2d 837, 2005 La. LEXIS 1257 (La., Apr. 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed a judgment of the Eleventh Judicial District Court, Parish Of Sabin (Louisiana) requiring it to maintain a road. The matter was remanded. The trial court again found in favor of plaintiffs, a citizens association. The State filed a suspensive appeal. The court transferred the matter to the supreme court, which vacated the judgment and remanded the case for a ruling on the merits of the appeal from the original judgment.


OVERVIEW: The State argued, in part, that it was no longer responsible for the road's maintenance because La. Const. art. 4, § 27 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:757 prohibited the expenditure of state funds on roads that were not part of the state highway system. The association claimed that the State was responsible for the road according to an agreement entered into just before its construction and that La. Const. art. 7, § 27, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:757 unconstitutionally impaired those obligations. On appeal, the court agreed that the trial court erred in finding that the road was part of the state highway system. The court noted that the road had never been assigned a state highway number nor was it referenced by the statute establishing the system. Furthermore, the association conceded at oral argument that the road was not part of the system. The court's finding that the road was not part of the state highway system made the constitutionality issue determinative of the matter. Because the court could not address the constitutionality issue on its own, it remanded the case to the trial court so that the association could specifically plead the issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court so that the association could specifically plead the constitutionality issue.

 

1295 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alexander


NO. 04-KA-1209


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-1209 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/31/05); 904 So. 2d 855; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1435



May 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-3286, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION, FINDING AS A SECOND FELONY OFFENDER AND ENHANCED SENTENCE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for possession of Diazepam (Valium), by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana. The State filed a habitual offender bill of information charging him as a second felony offender. The trial court then vacated his initial five-year sentence, and re-sentenced him to an enhanced sentence of 10 years imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant's motion to reconsider was denied and he then appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty as to heroin charges. The facts showed that officers conducted surveillance on defendant. They observed what appeared to be a narcotics sale in a parking lot. They stopped the other driver, she had heroin and Valium, and she implicated defendant. Hours later, defendant's residence was searched. Defendant was not home and only Valium was recovered, but there was evidence of other drug related activity. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that counsel's failure to file notice of his alibi defense, that he was out of town at the time of the alleged crime, was ineffective assistance. That was because defendant was not in the residence at the time of the search. Further, he was not convicted based on conduct related to the parking lot transaction. In any event, he was equivocally identified by the narcotics agents. Thus, he suffered no prejudice. Finally, defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive of grossly disproportionate. His sentence was a maximum, but the trial court was able to consider the heroin charges even though he was acquitted in that respect. The same was true to a past drug arrest where the case was refused.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. However, the case was remanded for the trial court to advise defendant, by written notice, of the prescriptive period for filing an application for post-conviction relief. The trial court was directed to then to file written proof in the record that defendant received said notice.

 

1296 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Johnson Controls, Inc.


NO. 05-CA-27


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


05-27 (La. App. 5 Cir. 05/31/05); 905 So. 2d 444; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1440



May 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 591-340, DIVISION ''D''. HONORABLE ROBERT M. MURPHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AMENDED AND AS AMENDED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff, the Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA), denying company's summary judgment motion, and ordering the company to pay LIGA $ 25,457 for reimbursement for benefits.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the Louisiana Legislature intended for LIGA to be able to seek recovery from an insured for any claim it paid on behalf of the insured whose net worth exceeded 25 million dollars on December thirty-first of the year immediately preceding the date of the determination of the insolvency of the insurer. To have held otherwise would have rendered La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1382(D) meaningless and would have thwarted the purpose of the statute, to avoid financial loss to a claimant because of the insolvency of an insurer. Moreover, 2004 La. Acts 109, amending La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1382(D), correcting a typographical error by replacing the last letter of the word insured with an "r" thereby changing the word to "insurer," as was clearly intended, and deleting the word "covered" in reference to what claims LIGA can seek reimbursement, the amendment was interpretive or curative. Finally, the appellate court rejected the company's argument that § 22:1382(D) was unconstitutional because it discriminated as to wealth.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed but amended to delete an award of attorney fees for LIGA.

 

1297 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Rhone v. Ward


No. 39,701-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,701 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/11/05); 902 So. 2d 1258; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1234



May 11, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by, Remanded by Rhone v. Ward, 920 So. 2d 217, 2006 La. LEXIS 157 (La., Jan. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35642. Honorable Jenifer W. Clason, Judge.
Rhone v. Ward, 818 So. 2d 26, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2659 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 9, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, whose appeal in an action against appellee warden had been stayed because he had not paid his court costs, sought to have to have the automatic stay provision in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(B)(2) of the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA) declared unconstitutional. The Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, denied relief, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had sued the warden for money damages alleging he sustained medical problems due to exposure to contaminated water. The trial court dismissed the inmate's claim, and the inmate sought review. The trial court granted the warden's motion to enforce the automatic stay in § 15:1186(B)(2) pending payment of the court costs by the inmate. The inmate claimed § 15:1186(B)(2) was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of § 15:1186(B)(2) as it furthered a legitimate state interest in reducing court congestion by reducing the number of frivolous lawsuits filed by inmates. The appellate court also held that § 15:1186(B)(2) did not violate La. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 22 as the inmates did not have a fundamental constitutional right to sue for civil damages, and their access to the courts could be restricted if there was a rational basis for the restriction. Finally, the court approved the retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(B)(2) as § 15:1186(B)(2) was procedural as it prescribed a method for operation of the in forma pauperis proceedings by prisoners under the PLRA, and thus, could be applied both retroactively and prospectively.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court declaring that the automatic stay provision was not unconstitutional.

 

1298 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Christus Schumpert Med. Ctr.


No. 39,593-WCA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,593 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/11/05); 902 So. 2d 1180; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1259



May 11, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 1W. Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 03-01839. Honorable Larry Steven Butler, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee filed a claim when her workers' compensation benefits were reduced to reflect the receipt of her old age benefits as per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1225(C)(1), a section that was later declared unconstitutional. The Office of Workers' Compensation of District 1W, Caddo Parish, Louisiana, found that appellee employer was only obligated to reinstate benefits retroactive to the date of judicial demand. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee challenged the trial court's finding as to when the date of reimbursement should have been. The appellate court found that the employer's assertion that full benefits should only have been restored to the date of judicial demand was untenable considering that it was possible for the employer to receive a credit for benefits paid prior to seeking judicial enforcement of an offset under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1225(C)(1). Further, retroactive application to the date of the commencement of the offset would not have promoted inequity as reimbursing the employee for the benefits that she would have received absent the offset simply allowed her to receive the full benefits to which she was entitled. As such, the trial court erred in denying the employee a reimbursement of the offset benefits retroactive to the date the offset commenced. However, the employee was not entitled to penalties and attorney fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201 because, at the very least, the employer reasonably controverted the employee's demand for complete reimbursement, and the legal dispute was not frivolous as the jurisprudence was not dispositive of the issues.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment denying the employee's claim for reimbursement of all benefits offset retroactive to the date the offset was commenced was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

1299 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr.


NO. 38,148-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,148 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/11/05); 902 So. 2d 1228; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1262



May 11, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 2006 La. LEXIS 463 (La., Feb. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court. Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95383. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Judge.
Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 894 So. 2d 1096, 2005 La. LEXIS 459 (La., Feb. 25, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This medical malpractice claim was before the court upon remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court for an en banc hearing. Plaintiffs, patient and spouse (patient), had filed an action against defendant medical center after being diagnosed with Hepatitis C and the district court granted the medical center's exception of prescription pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.


OVERVIEW: The case was again before the court upon remand from the supreme court. The patient appealed a judgment in favor of the medical center after the district court granted the medical center's exception of prescription, finding that the three-year prescriptive period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was constitutional and that the spouse's claim for damages resulting from a blood transfusion had prescribed. The court affirmed, stating that the application of § 9:5628 did not violate the patient's due process rights pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 2, or equal protection rights pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 3. In regard to the equal protection claim, the patient failed to meet her burden of proving that the statute did not further an appropriate state interest. In regard to the due process claim, the court stated that the application of the statute to person who, like the patient, had diseases with latency periods exceeding three years constitutional. In addition, the prescriptive period of § 9:5628 applied equally to actions for damages arising out of patient care against both state and private hospitals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1300 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Batiste


NO. 2004-KA-1200


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1200 (La.App. 4 Cir. 5/11/05); 904 So. 2d 766; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1578



May 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 7, 2005.
Writ granted by State v. Baptiste, 922 So. 2d 1155, 2006 La. LEXIS 402 (La., Feb. 3, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Batiste, 2006 La. LEXIS 2876 (La., Oct. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 447-514, SECTION "K". HONORABLE ARTHUR HUNTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On November 12, 2002, the State filed a bill of information charging defendant with video voyeurism, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:283. On March 23rd, the day set for trial, the State entered a nolle prosequi. The case was reinstated on April 16th and defendant pleaded not guilty. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "K" (Louisiana) granted defendant's motion to quash on June 23, 2004. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State cited La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 691 and 576 for the propositions that the district attorney had the power to dismiss a bill of information and reinstitute a new prosecution based on the same facts unless the dismissal was made to avoid the time limitations for commencement of trial established by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 578. The motion to quash was granted on June 23, 2004, more than 4 months before the statutory 2-year time limit elapsed. Thus, it did not appear that the State entered a nolle prosequi to avoid statutory time limitations. Twenty months elapsed between the filing of the original bill of information and the granting of defendant's motion to quash. That period of delay was "presumptively prejudicial" under the first factor of Barker, necessitating further analysis. Under the Wingo factors: (1) the length of the delay was presumed prejudicial; (2) the State bore more of the responsibility for the delay; (3) defendant did not object to the delay or file a motion for a speedy trial; and (4) he was inconvenienced by having to travel for court appearances. There was not "palpable abuse" on the part of the trial court in granting the motion to quash.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1301 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 39,681-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,681 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/11/05); 903 So. 2d 580; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1256



May 11, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 213,605. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of possession of cocaine. He was found to be a third-felony habitual offender and was sentenced to serve five years in prison without credit for time served. The sentence also provided for a jail term in the even of default of the payment of court costs. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially stopped for reckless driving. A pat-down of defendant revealed cocaine. Defendant was convicted as charged and the court affirmed on appeal. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 703. The pat-down of defendant pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 215.1 was justified because defendant appeared to be on drugs and the officer was concerned for his safety. Defendant's oral consent, given twice, to the search of his pocket was freely given, which justified the search. Because of defendant's outstanding warrants, the cocaine would have been discovered without reference to any alleged police error or misconduct, and therefore, even if revealed during an illegal search, the evidence was have been admissible under the inevitable discovery rule. The trial court erred in ordering defendant to serve 10 days in jail if he defaulted on the payment of court costs because defendant was indigent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court amended defendant's sentence to delete the portion that provided for a jail term in the event of default of the payment of court costs. As amended, the court affirmed defendant's sentence.

 

1302 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Farm Fresh Food Supplier, Inc. v. Davis


NO. 2004 CA 0856


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 0856 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/6/05); 915 So. 2d 887; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1199



May 6, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 507,442. Honorable Wilson E. Fields, Judge.
Davis v. Farm Fresh Food Supplier, 879 So. 2d 215, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1263 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 14, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation case, a penalty of $ 5,000.00 was assessed against appellant employer pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(D). The employer made willful misrepresentations in an attempt to defeat the employee's claim. In a civil proceeding, the Nineteenth Judicial District, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, upheld the constitutionality of the statute and found the employer liable for the civil penalties. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained a job-related injury during the course of his employment with a grocery store. His employer denied the accident and responsibility for the claim. The workers' compensation court awarded the employee benefits. An additional civil penalty of $ 5,000.00 was assessed against the employer, because the operator and sole stockholder of the grocery store made intentional misrepresentations in his court testimony, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(A). In a civil appeal, the employer argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 was unconstitutional in that it improperly authorized the judge to exercise criminal jurisdiction in a workers' compensation proceeding. The appellate court disagreed. The penalty provided by § 23:1208(D) was civil, not criminal. Therefore, § 23:1208 was not unconstitutional. The court's assessment of civil penalties under § 23:1208(D) was related to the judicious administration of workers' compensation claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court upholding the constitutionality of the statute was affirmed.

Hitchcock v. State


NUMBER 04-1597


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1597 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/27/05); 901 So. 2d 613; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1083



April 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Remanded by Hitchcock v. Heritage Manor Nursing Home, 922 So. 2d 764, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 178 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF VERMILION, NO. 76183. HONORABLE PATRICK L. MICHOT, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Hitchcock v. Heritage Manor Nursing Home, 773 So. 2d 148, 2000 La. LEXIS 3068 (La., Nov. 3, 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of an order from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vermilion (Louisiana), which dismissed as premature her action to have La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(E) declared unconstitutional and to have the court issue an injunction preventing defendant State of Louisiana from enforcing the statute in her workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits. However, before her claim was litigated, the employee filed suit in the trial court, seeking to have § 23:1208(E) declared unconstitutional and to have the trial court issue an injunction preventing the State from enforcing the statute. The trial judge dismissed the employee's suit as premature. On appeal, the court determined that because the employee's workers' compensation claim had not yet been litigated, she had not been adversely impacted by the statute that she sought to have declared unconstitutional. There was a possibility that if the court waited, the whole constitutional problem might be eliminated by later developments. If the workers' compensation judge was to determine that the employee had not violated the statute, the issue of the constitutionality of the statute would be moot. Accordingly, the issue raised by the employee was not ripe for determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Morris v. State/AG


05-518


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-518 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/27/05); 909 So. 2d 3; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1156



April 27, 2005, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Morris v. State, 901 So. 2d 1077, 2005 La. LEXIS 1531 (La., May 2, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Morris v. Louisiana, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5647 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2005-1954. HONORABLE ROBERT L. WYATT, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Morris v. State/AG, 909 So. 2d 1, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1049 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city council candidate brought suit against defendants, the State via the attorney general and a parish court clerk, challenging an election. The attorney general and the clerk filed peremptory exceptions of no cause of action, prescription, and peremption. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court of Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana, granted the exceptions of prescription and dismissed the candidate's suit. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the candidate contended that the time limitation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(B) was unconstitutional and, therefore, should not have been applied to bar her action. The appellate court disagreed, finding that this provision had previously been upheld as constitutional. Furthermore, there was no conflict between the time delays for the promulgation of election returns as forth in § 18:1405 and the time delays for challenging elections pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:574. Nor was La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405 ambiguous as to the date on which the delay for filing the action began to run as the statute clearly stated that the nine-day delay commenced to run on the day following the conducting of the election. Notwithstanding the candidate's contention that the language of the Election Code was confusing, the appellate court found that the wording of § 1405(B) was clear and free of any ambiguity or vagueness. As the time period set forth in § 1405(B) was peremptive, the trial court correctly dismissed the candidate's suit with prejudice as her claim ceased to exist prior to the filing of her petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of New Orleans' Dep't of Fin. v. Touro Infirmary


NO. 2004-CA-0835, CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2004-CA-0951, CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2004-CA-1204


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-0835 (La. App. 4 Cir. 4/27/05); 905 So. 2d 314; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1319



April 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by City of New Orleans' Dep't of Fin. v. Touro Infirmary, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1549 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 31, 2005)
Writ denied by City of New Orleans' Dep't of Fin. v. Touro Infirmary, 924 So. 2d 997, 2006 La. LEXIS 678 (La., Feb. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS [**2] PARISH. NO. 2004-2424, DIVISION "M-7". HONORABLE SHERYL HOWARD, JUDGE PRO TEMPORE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals in a summary tax proceeding, appellant city challenged judgments of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) that granted respondent hospital's reconventional demand for a refund of overpaid sales and use taxes; denied the city's claim for taxes on immovable property; and that denied the city's claim for penalties on the unpaid taxes under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1602. The hospital also appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city challenged the grant of the hospital's reconventional demand for a refund of overpaid taxes. The hospital challenged the grant of the city's claim for audit costs pursuant to New Orleans, La., City Code 150-707 and for attorney fees. It also challenged the calculation of sales taxes assessed on the service and repair contracts for immovable property, which consisted of computerized tomography equipment and a radiation therapy simulator. The court held that reconventional demands were not permitted in tax collections cases because of the sui generis nature of the summary proceedings and because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:337.61, which required that all defenses be filed prior to the time fixed for the hearing, would preclude a tax collector from filing an answer or defenses to the demand. The city was authorized to impose a penalty on delinquent taxes and that the limiting language in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1602 did not mean that no penalty could be imposed. The court held that New Orleans, La., City Code § 150-441 expressly deemed "tangible personal property" to include certain immovables for the purpose of the imposition of sales taxes on the sale of services.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment granting the hospital's reconventional demand for a refund of taxes and dismissed the demand. The court reversed the denial of the city's claims for penalties on the unpaid taxes and the city's claim for taxes on immovable property and remanded the case for a determination of the exact amount of the judgment against the hospital. The court affirmed the grant of the city's request for audit costs and attorney fees.

La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. Connick


NO. 04-CA-1468


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-1468 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/26/05); 902 So. 2d 1090; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1065



April 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 2005.
Writ denied by 2005 La. LEXIS 2677 (La., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 491-403, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE ROBERT M. MURPHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.
La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. State, 833 So. 2d 1016, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3689 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 20, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-profit organization filed a suit to declare unconstitutional and enjoin enforcement of laws regarding crime against nature, sexual offenders, and "homosexual organizations." Inter alia, the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "D" (Louisiana) found La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89(A)(1) unconstitutional and struck the offending portions without nullifying the statute in its entirety. The organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organization argued that the trial court erred by failing to declare § 14:89(A)(1) unconstitutional in its entirety and in refusing to declare La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12:1041 unconstitutional. It argued that the trial court erred in attempting to sever the phrases in § 14:89(A)(1) and rewriting the statute so that the only part of paragraph (A)(1) that remained was the portion prohibiting "unnatural carnal copulation" with an animal. The organization argued that the human/animal clause was not severable from the human/human clause and that the entire § 14:89(A)(1) should have been struck down. The Louisiana Supreme Court's discussion of that conduct in Thomas contrasted compensated versus uncompensated conduct because Thomas involved persons charged with performing human-on-human acts for compensation. The court's language did not prohibit severance of the prohibition of human-on-human conduct from that of human-on-animal conduct within § 14:89(A)(1). The appellate court concluded that the two types of behavior were severable, because the prohibition against the human/human portion could be removed without affecting the validity or intent of the human/animal prohibition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of appeal were assessed against the organization.
