State v. Young


NO. 04-KA-1318


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-1318 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/26/05); 902 So. 2d 461; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1087



April 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 2005.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Young, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 539 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-353, DIVISION ''C''. HONORABLE J. STERLING SNOWDY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fortieth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana) of two counts of distribution of cocaine in a drug free zone, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(A) and 40:981.3, and one count of distribution of cocaine, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A). Defendant was sentenced to consecutive terms on the three counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine to an undercover officer on three occasions. On appeal, the court found that the jury, within its right, apparently chose to believe a detective's uncontradicted testimony in estimating that two of the transactions occurred between 150 to 200 feet from a Catholic school. The jury could have reasonably inferred that a parking lot at issue was the school parking lot and, thus, used for school purposes. The fact that the parking lot might also have been used by a church did not negate its use for school purposes. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request to add co-counsel on the second day of the trial after the completion of voir dire and the testimony of witnesses. Additionally, it appeared that the request for co-counsel may have been for abusive delay. Finally, the trial court sentenced defendant on the same day it denied his second or third motion for a new trial. Thus, the trial court failed to observe the mandatory 24-hour time delay pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873. Because defendant challenged his non-mandatory sentences as excessive, defendant had to be re-sentenced.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for re-sentencing.

State v. Sellers


NO. 2004-KA-1922, NO. 2004-KA-1923


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004 1922 (La. App. 4 Cir. 04/20/05); 902 So. 2d 418; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1306



April 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 14, 2005.
Writ denied by State v. Sellers, 2006 La. LEXIS 346 (La., Jan. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM 25TH JDC, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES NO.S 03-2512, C/W 03-2513, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE WILLIAM A. ROE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ATTEMPTED ARMED ROBBERY CONVICTION REVERSED, SENTENCE FOR ATTEMPTED ARMED ROBBERY CONVICTION VACATED, ALL OTHER CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the 25th Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines (Louisiana) to two counts of carjacking, one count of attempted armed robbery, two counts of aggravated battery, and two counts of armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:64.2, 14:27, 14:64, 14:34. Defendant was sentenced to 30 years for the armed robbery counts and to lesser sentences for the other crimes. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that his counsel was ineffective because his counsel failed to move to withdraw the guilty pleas prior to sentencing. The court reversed defendant's conviction for attempted armed robbery and vacated this sentence, but otherwise affirmed. Because the indictment did not specify that defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon, it was an error patent to convict him for the crime of attempted armed robbery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:64 when the crime described in the bill of information was that of simple robbery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65. The error was not harmless because defendant pleaded guilty to a more serious offense than that alleged in the indictment. The court addressed defendant's claim of error related to ineffective assistance of counsel even though the court was not required to do so. Defendant's contention that his counsel was ineffective for failing to move to withdraw guilty pleas that, according to defendant, did not exist, was without merit. The trial court did not abuse its discretion under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 559.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's attempted armed robbery conviction and vacated defendant's related sentence. All other convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1309 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Poullard v. Pittman


NO. 39,549-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,549 (La. App. 2 Cir. 04/13/05); 900 So. 2d 310; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 948



April 13, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Poullard v. Pittman, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1289 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 5, 2005)
Writ denied by Poullard v. Pittman, 920 So. 2d 237, 2006 La. LEXIS 226 (La., Jan. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 040796. Honorable Hamilton S. Winters, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate brought a medical malpractice action against appellee state university hospital and a doctor. They filed an exception of improper venue asserting that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1184, exclusive venue for a tort action by an inmate was the parish where the inmate was incarcerated when the cause of action arose. The Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) granted the exception. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed the court erroneously granted appellees' exception. When read in isolation, § 15:1184F supported the trial court's grant of the exception of improper venue. But, the provision could not be read in isolation, it had to be read in the context of the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1181-1191. The title of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1184 was "suits by prisoners," indicating that it addressed only those lawsuits that fit the definition of a "prisoner suit" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1181(2). Reading La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1184(F) in context lead to the conclusion that the exclusive venue provision for delictual actions for injury or damages was intended only to address those delictual actions concerning conditions of confinement or the effects of actions by governmental officials on the lives of inmates. Thus, an ordinary malpractice action fell outside the scope of the exclusive venue provision. Neither the hospital nor the doctor were governmental officials whose actions affected the lives of inmate's, and a malpractice action for treatment received at the hospital was not an action with respect to the conditions of confinement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1310 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Alexandria Civ. Serv. Comm'n v. Randolph


04-1620


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1620 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/06/05); 899 So. 2d 857; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 871



April 6, 2005, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 213,980, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 214,680. HONORABLE HARRY F. RANDOW, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Alexandria Civ. Serv. Comm'n v. Randolph, 899 So. 2d 865, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 876 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 6, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Alexandria Civil Service Commission appealed a judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) that was entered in favor of appellees, Mayor and City of Alexandria, which found 2001 La. Acts No. 390 (Act 390) and Alexandria, La., City Ordinance No. 247-2003 (Ordinance) to be constitutional. The Commission argued that the provisions violated La. Const. art. VI, §§ 5 and 6.


OVERVIEW: In accordance with Act 390 and the Alexandria, La., Home Rule Charter §§ 4-01 and 4-11, the Mayor proposed the Ordinance, which created two departments within the Division of Personnel and Civil Service. The Commission objected to the Ordinance and issued an order directing the Mayor to present his proposed plan to amend the Charter to the majority of the electors. The Mayor filed suit and obtained a restraining order against the Commission. The Commission filed suit against the Mayor, claiming that Act 390 and the Ordinance were unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment for the Mayor. The Commission appealed. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that the Commission failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that Act 390 and the Ordinance were unconstitutional. The court found that Act 390 and the Ordinance were not in violation of La. Const. art. VI nor were they contrary to the Charter. The court found that under the Ordinance, the Division of Personnel and Civil Service was still headed by a Director of Personnel as required the Charter and that it was within the Mayor's authority to create departments within the divisions of his administration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1311 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. E.P.


NO. 2004-CA-1822


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1822 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/06/05); 900 So. 2d 1068; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1004



April 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 2, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2004-145-02-DQF, SECTION "F". Honorable Mark Doherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the Orleans Parish Juvenile Court (Louisiana), which denied his motion to suppress identification evidence and adjudicated him delinquent as a result of having committed the crime of purse snatching.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent as a result of having committed the crime of purse snatching. On appeal, the court found that the record did not support the juvenile's contention that the adjudication hearing was not completed. However, the court found that the trial court erred in denying the juvenile's motion to suppress identification evidence because it was unconstitutionally seized. La. Child. Code Ann. art. 818B could not constitutionally be applied to allow the juvenile to be picked up and taken to be photographed and fingerprinted. At best, it could be said that a detective had a suspicion that the juvenile had committed the crime of purse snatching. Yet, the juvenile, who was not in custody and who merely was suspected to have committed a crime, was taken from his home, fingerprinted, and photographed. Clearly, the juvenile was entitled to at least as much protection as an adult. The procedure followed in obtaining the juvenile's photograph and fingerprints could not pass constitutional muster. Accordingly, the identification evidence should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1312 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


NO. 2005-K-0035


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0035 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/06/05); 900 So. 2d 1072; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1012



April 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 2, 2005.
Writ denied by State v. Washington, 904 So. 2d 722, 2005 La. LEXIS 2237 (La., June 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 288-737, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.
Washington v. Cain, 2000 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9469 (E.D. La., June 26, 2000)



DISPOSITION: WRIT APPLICATION GRANTED; POST CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From his life sentence for his armed robbery and aggravated rape convictions, defendant filed a number of writ applications. His motions for postconviction relief and reconsideration were denied. A federal district court dismissed his application for writ of habeas corpus as being time barred. Defendant filed another application for postconviction relief, which the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish (Louisiana) denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant raised eight claims challenging the denial of his motion for postconviction relief, including: challenges to the indictment because of the exclusion of African-Americans on the grand jury; ineffective assistance of counsel for failing to file a motion to quash the indictment; and the use of an erroneous reasonable doubt jury instruction. The appellate court held that defendant's failure to file a motion to quash due to the alleged discriminatory selection of the grand jury barred relief. Further, defendant failed to present any evidence showing that he would not have been indicted by a properly-constituted grand jury. If counsel had filed the pretrial motion to quash, the indictment would have been quashed, but defendant would have been reindicted and convicted at trial. Thus, defendant failed to show prejudice, and his ineffective assistance of counsel claim had no merit. Finally, the appellate court reaffirmed that a so-called Cage instruction did not require reversal of defendant's conviction on grounds that it diluted the State's burden of proving the accused's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt in violation of due process guarantees.


OUTCOME: Defendant's writ application was granted, but he was denied any relief.

Stay denied by Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Grefer, 547 U.S. 1125, 126 S. Ct. 2056, 164 L. Ed. 2d 777, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3927 (2006)
Vacated by, Remanded by Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Grefer, 549 U.S. 1249, 127 S. Ct. 1371, 167 L. Ed. 2d 156, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2656 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 97-15004, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.
Grefer v. Alpha Tech., 744 So. 2d 1284, 1999 La. LEXIS 2935 (La., Oct. 15, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an oil company and an oil pipe company, and plaintiff property owners appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which, upon a jury verdict, awarded compensatory damages and one billion dollars in punitive damages to the property owners as a result of the contamination of immovable property with radioactive material. The oil company also appealed the denial of its exception of prescription.


OVERVIEW: The pipe company leased property from the property owners, where it cleaned pipe for the oil company and others. After the leases were terminated, the property owners learned that their property was contaminated with radium. The property owners filed an action seeking damages. A judgment was entered in favor of the property owners, awarding compensatory damages and one billion dollars in punitive damages. All parties appealed, and the court amended the judgment to reduce the punitive damage award to twice the general damage amount in order to comply with the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed, including the denial of the oil company's exception of prescription. The trial court was not clearly wrong in determining that the property owner acted reasonably in relying on assurances that the property did not contain unacceptable levels of radioactive waste. The trial court did not err in correcting the record pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2132. The court found that for purposes of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.3, the cause of action accrued when the pipe company ceased cleaning pipes on the property owners' land.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment by reducing the amount of punitive damages awarded to the property owners and affirmed the judgment as amended.

Delahoussaye v. Bd. of Supervisors of Cmty. & Tech. Colleges


NO. 2004 CA 0515


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 0515 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/24/05);  906 So. 2d 646; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 653



March 24, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 501,519. The Honorable Jewel E. Welch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; amended and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff instructor brought a declaratory judgment and mandamus action against defendant Louisiana Board of Supervisors of Community and Technical Colleges, seeking to restore his salary and benefits retroactive to the date of his suspension. The 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, entered summary judgment for the instructor. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instructor was placed on administrative leave without pay pending investigation of allegations of sexual harassment. A removal hearing was scheduled, but it was delayed. The appellate court noted that the trial court erred in concluding that the removal policy section was the one under which the Board acted. On that basis alone, the trial court's ruling that the "without pay" provision of the removal policy section was unconstitutional had to be reversed. Nevertheless, the appellate court's de novo review of the record supported the factual finding of the trial court that the leave policy section of the general personnel policy was improperly applied to the instructor. The instructor's suspension violated the safeguards of due process. In his sole assignment of error, the instructor challenged the trial court's ruling that he was not entitled to conduct pre-removal discovery under the provisions of the Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure. Nevertheless, the appellate court did not read the language at issue in the Board's policy as incorporating by reference the discovery devices and procedures of the Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment regarding the "without pay" provision. The trial court's judgment was amended regarding the instructor's suspension without due process. The trial court's decision regarding discovery was affirmed.

Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Dorsey v. State, 973 So. 2d 738, 2008 La. LEXIS 14 (La., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Dorsey v. State, 49 So. 3d 880, 2010 La. LEXIS 2639 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Dorsey v. State, 108 So. 3d 764, 2013 La. LEXIS 348 (La., 2013)
Writ denied by State v. Dorsey, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2734 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 8, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Dorsey v. State, 123 So. 3d 1221, 2013 La. LEXIS 2267 (La., 2013)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Dorsey, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 209 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 10, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 348109. Hon. Martin E. Coady, Judge Presiding.
State v. Dorsey, 864 So. 2d 906, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3761 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 31, 2003)



DISPOSITION: HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AND SENTENCE ON COUNT I AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of attempted molestation of a juvenile by influence of control or supervision and attempted obstruction of justice. The Twenty-Second Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, adjudged defendant a fourth felony habitual offender and sentenced him to 20 years at hard labor to be served without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the habitual offender bill of information, the State alleged that on November 12, 1999, defendant pled guilty to two counts of simple escape and two counts of issuing worthless checks. Defendant argued the November 1999 predicate offenses could not be used to adjudicate him a fourth felony offender as they were entered on the same date. The appellate court disagreed and affirmed defendant's status as a fourth felony offender because under the habitual offender statute, multiple convictions obtained on the same date based on unrelated conduct could be counted separately for sentence enhancement. As the convictions occurred on different dates and were not based on related conduct, defendant's status as a fourth felony offender was affirmed. The appellate court affirmed the sentence imposed as the statutory minimum sentence for the molestation of a juvenile was no less than 20 years. As defendant had not specified any unusual circumstances indicating that he was a victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences that were meaningfully tailored to the culpability of the offender, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the case, the 20-year sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's habitual offender adjudication and the sentence imposed.

State v. Kenner

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 327-373, SECTION "E". Honorable Calvin Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL CONVERTED TO A SUPERVISORY WRIT APPLICATION; WRIT DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted defendant's application for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to simple rape and simple kidnapping. Several years later, he filed a motion for a valid sentence. The trial court interpreted the motion as an application for postconviction relief. The trial court granted defendant's application. On appeal, the court explained that the State's remedy was to file a writ of review invoking the court's supervisory jurisdiction. Therefore, under the court's supervisory jurisdiction, it converted the appeal to a writ application. The court further found that because evidence existed that might have shown that defendant was not the perpetrator of the crimes, his claim that his Alford plea was not intelligently entered had merit. The State withheld evidence that defendant was entitled to have. Experts would have been required at trial to explain to the jury whether defendant's classification as a Group "O" secretor would have included or excluded him as a possible suspect in the crimes. The jury would have been given the opportunity to weigh the evidence along with other evidence that the State may have produced to determine defendant's culpability. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court converted the State's appeal to a writ application. The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Sykes


NO. 2004-KA-1199, C/W 2004-K-0947


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1199 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/09/05); 900 So. 2d 156; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1022



March 9, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 5, 2005.
Writ denied by State v. Sykes, 2006 La. LEXIS 2785 (La., Oct. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 437-305, SECTION "D". Honorable Frank A. Marullo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, possession with the intent to distribute heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966A, and possession with the intent to distribute cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A. Pursuant to a motion to reconsider sentence, the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "D" (Louisiana) vacated the 25 year sentence and imposed a 13 year sentence. The State and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence and that the drugs he abandoned as a result of the stop had to be suppressed because the officers had no reasonable suspicion to stop him. He argued that the officers did not have reasonable suspicion to stop him as a confidential informant's tip was neither detailed nor predictive and the officers did not corroborate the tip. The appellate court held that the officers' actions did not constitute either an actual or an imminent actual stop, and so defendant abandoned the bag prior to any unlawful intrusion into his right to be free from governmental interference. The officers lawfully seized the bag containing the drugs and, once the drugs were found, the officers had probable cause to arrest defendant, and incident to arrest, they could lawfully search him and seize the money from his pocket. Because there was no actual or imminent actual stop, it was immaterial whether the officers had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant, but, even if their action constituted an imminent actual stop, the informant's tip, corroborated by police surveillance, was sufficient to support an investigatory stop.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions, his sentences on his cocaine and marijuana convictions, and his adjudication as a second offender as to the heroin count were affirmed. Because the appellate court could not determine whether the trial court erred by imposing a sentence below the mandatory minimum on defendant's heroin conviction, the matter was remanded to the trial court for a determination on that issue.

State v. Major


03-249


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-0249 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/02/05); 898 So. 2d 548; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 522



March 2, 2005, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 14, 2005.
Rehearing denied by State v. Major, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1177 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 27, 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Major, 2006 La. LEXIS 585 (La., Feb. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. MARTIN. NO. 97-180297. HONORABLE JOHN E. CONERY, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Major, 888 So. 2d 798, 2004 La. LEXIS 3600 (La., Dec. 1, 2004)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of possession of cocaine in excess of 400 grams, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(c). Defendant made oral motions for a post-verdict judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, which the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana) denied. On appeal, the conviction was overturned. The Louisiana Supreme Court reinstated the conviction and remanded the matter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and three passengers were stopped by a state trooper for a traffic violation. Defendant consented to a search which uncovered more than a pound of cocaine under the dashboard. The appellate court held that the trial court had not imposed a fine although one was mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(c). Therefore, the sentence appeared to have been illegally lenient. The trial court, even in light of its determination that defendant was indigent, should have imposed the mandatory fine but without imposing default time under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 884. Defendant's 40-year sentence was not excessive because the sentence imposed fell in the lower-middle range of possible sentences. Applying the Barker analysis, the appellate court held that defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated because even though the delay until trial was slightly more than two and one-half years, the delay could not be entirely attributed to the State; at least some of the delay was attributable to defendant. Also, defendant had not asserted his constitutional right to a speedy trial while before the trial court or clearly alleged any prejudice to his case due to the delay.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. However, the sentence was vacated for failure to impose the mandatory fine. The case was remanded for resentencing. The trial court was instructed that, if it found defendant was indigent, it was to impose the mandatory fine without default time.

State v. Richardson


No. 39,456-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,456 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/02/05); 896 So. 2d 257; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 528



March 2, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Richardson, 916 So. 2d 165, 2005 La. LEXIS 2555 (La., Nov. 29, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Richardson v. La., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3814 (U.S., May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 225,544. Honorable Jeanette Giddens Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated battery, determined that he was a third felony habitual offender, and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat a victim with a crowbar, causing serious head injuries. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of aggravated battery. He appealed after a life sentence was imposed due to the fact that he was a third felony habitual offender. In affirming, the court determined that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. Self-defense was not a viable claim because defendant armed himself during a verbal exchange, followed the victim as he tried to leave the residence, and hit the victim from behind. The court did not have the authority to re-weigh the credibility of the witnesses. Moreover, the record showed that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to a jury trial under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 780. The trial court advised defendant about his right to a jury trial under La. Const. art. I, § 17 (1974), defendant entered a waived by an oral statement in open court, and defendant was represented by counsel at all times. Next, the State proved all elements of the habitual offender bill under La. Rev. Stat. § 15:529.1, and Apprendi did not apply to prior convictions. Finally, the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Hamilton v. Royal Int'l Petroleum Corp.


NO. 2003 CA 2660


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 2660 (La. App. 1 Cir. 3/2/05); 906 So. 2d 627; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 542



March 2, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ granted by Hamilton v. Royal Int'l Petroleum Corp., 2005 La. LEXIS 1856 (La., June 3, 2005)
Reversed by Hamilton v. Royal Int'l Petroleum Corp., 2006 La. LEXIS 644 (La., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. Suit Number 465,644-I. Honorable MICHAEL CALDWELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax debtor sought review of a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which rendered judgment in favor of defendants, a buyer and a city tax collector. The debtor had filed an action to annul the tax sale of his property, which had been conducted pursuant to the orders of the tax collector and had resulted in the property being purchased by the buyer.


OVERVIEW: The debtor's property was sold by the tax collector because of unpaid city and parish taxes in June 1995. The buyer purchased the property and a conditional tax deed was recorded. The debtor filed an action to annul the tax proceeding alleging, in part, that he did not receive post-sale notice as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180A(1)(b), which was not enacted until after the sale had occurred, but did go into effect before the expiration of the three-year redemption period on the property. The trial court rejected the debtor's assertion that the notice was required to be given to the debtor, and entered judgment in favor of defendants. Reversing the judgment of the trial court, the court held that the notice provision of § 47:2180A(1)(b), which went into effect on August 15, 1997, required the tax collector to give the debtor notice of his post-sale rights while the three-year redemption period was still in effect, even though the provision did not go into effect until after the sale. Providing the notice did not impact concerns about inappropriate retrospective application of the provision. Because the required notice was not given, the tax sale needed to be annulled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and rendered judgment in favor of the tax debtor.

 

1322 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Nichols v. Williams


NO. 2004-CA-1025


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1025 (La. App. 4 Cir. 3/2/05); 898 So. 2d 581; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 892



March 2, 2005, Judgment Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 28, 2005.
Writ denied by Nichols v. Williams, 902 So. 2d 1030, 2005 La. LEXIS 1745 (La., May 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2003-15223, DIVISION "J". Honorable Nadine M. Ramsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner filed a petition for declaratory judgment when defendant city tax assessor denied the homeowner's application for a homestead exemption, maintaining that he was the sole occupant of the purchased dwelling and that the dwelling was his residence. The Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, agreed with the homeowner and granted his motion for summary judgment. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the city contended that La. Civ. Code Ann. art 477(B) did not constitutionally allow bond-for-deed purchasers to be eligible for a homestead exemption. The appellate court found that the property in question was owned and occupied in accordance with La. Const. art. VII, § 20(A)(1); thus, the homeowner was exempt from taxes. Further, in accordance with La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 477, the homeowner was considered the "owner" of the subject property via a bond-for-deed contract for the purpose of obtaining a homestead exemption. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the city's argument that art. 477 was unconstitutional was without merit. Neither the record, nor the briefs, indicated that the homeowner and the previous owner both sought to benefit from the homestead exemption status. If anything, the laws were extended to protect the tax assessor from instances whereby people sought to "double dip" in their homestead exemption. The homeowner sought what was rightfully owed to him as a property owner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1323 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. State


No. 39,323-CW


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,323 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/17/05); 901 So. 2d 1109; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 279



February 17, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by McCoy v. State, 2006 La. LEXIS 422 (La., Feb. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 02-2439. Honorable Wilson Rambo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Ouachita, State of Louisiana revoked appellant inmate's pauper status for having three qualifying strikes under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1187. The inmate requested a writ application.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that the inmate's underlying causes of action clearly fell within the definitional confines of the Prison Litigation Reform Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1181(2) et seq.; therefore, the causes of action were subject to the sanctions found in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1187. The inmate claimed that he was entitled to proceed in forma pauperis pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 5181(B). After embarking on a close examination of the inmate's claims, the appellate court concluded that the trial court was correct in its ruling that the inmate's action was related to the conditions of his confinement, or the effects of actions by government officials on his life as a person confined in prison. Turning next to the question of whether the inmate's rights were infringed by the three qualifying strikes rule under § 15:1187, the appellate court noted that the rule did not prohibit the inmate from pursuing his lawsuit, but merely required him to pay full filing fees. The inmate's right to sue for civil damages was not based on a fundamental right to file a civil suit cost-free. There was a rational basis for restricting the inmate's access to courts.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1324 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Gaylord Container Corp.


2003 CA 0692


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 0692 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/16/05); 897 So. 2d 1; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 268



February 16, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Cox v. Gaylord Container Corp., 901 So. 2d 1102, 2005 La. LEXIS 1606 (La., May 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of Washington, State of Louisiana. Docket Number 79,593, Division A. Honorable Raymond Childress, Judge Presiding.
Cox v. Gaylord Container Corp., 897 So. 2d 1, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 344 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part, amended in part, and affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, individually and on behalf of her minor child, sued defendant employer alleging that the child's neurological damage was a result of an accident that occurred at work while the mother was pregnant with the child. The 22nd Judicial District Court of Washington Parish, Louisiana, ruled that the employer was not vicariously liable for the mother's negligence and that the child had no theory of recovery. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the mother contended the trial court erred: in concluding that the child had no theory of recovery against her mother for her negligently inflicted prenatal injuries; and in finding that the employer was not vicariously liable for the negligent acts of the mother that caused damage to her unborn child. The appellate court found that it was possible that when the child became of age or was emancipated, she could bring a claim against her mother, and whether the child could at some point in her life sue her mother for negligently injuring her before birth was not before the trial court in the employer's motion for summary judgment; thus, dismissal of the child's claim against her mother was error. However, the employer had no choice but to keep the mother working while she was pregnant under The Pregnancy Discrimination Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e(k): the mother did not request light duty or ask to be moved to another assignment, and there was no evidence of prior negligence acts on the mother's part. Thus, the employer could not be held vicariously liable for the child's injuries.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated insofar as it dismissed the child's claim against her mother. The judgment was affirmed insofar as it dismissed the mother's claims against the employer.

Monistere v. Engelhardt


No. 04-CA-1126, C/W 04-CA-1127


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-1126 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/15/05); 896 So. 2d 1105; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 261



February 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.
Writ denied by Monistere v. Engelhardt, 916 So. 2d 141, 2005 La. LEXIS 2778 (La., Nov. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 574-040 C/W 566-092, DIVISION ''M''. HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, wife and children, filed a medical malpractice action against defendant doctor for medical malpractice. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, entered judgment for plaintiffs. The Patient Compensation Fund (PCF) intervened and the trial court granted its summary judgment motion holding that the medical malpractice caps were not unconstitutional. Plaintiffs and the PCF appealed.


OVERVIEW: The award to the plaintiffs included $ 175,000 for the decedent's survival action, and $ 1,100,000 to the decedent's wife and daughters for their wrongful death claims. The trial judge reduced this award to $ 500,000 in accordance with the medical malpractice recovery limits set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42B(1). The trial judge also awarded $ 146,830 to the plaintiffs for future medical care and related benefits. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the caps in § 40:1299.42(B)(1) were not unconstitutional, as the state supreme court had previously upheld the caps. The appellate court reversed and vacated the award for related funeral expenses, as they were outside the scope of "future medical care and related benefits" as defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43B(1). Further, the award for future medical care and related benefits was vacated and remanded to the trial court to determine what bills were related to services provided to the decedent after the malpractice occurred.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment that the statutory caps were not unconstitutional. The appellate court reversed and vacated the award of funeral, cemetery, and burial expenses. Further, the appellate court reversed the trial court's award of future medical expenses and related benefits to be awarded to plaintiffs.

State v. Thompkins


NO. 04-KA-1062


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-1062 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/15/05); 896 So. 2d 1165; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 944



February 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-5630, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE JOAN S. BENGE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of attempted forcible rape, sexual battery, and simple kidnapping, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27, 14:42.1, 14:43.1, and 14:45. His motion for a new trial was denied. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "A" (Louisiana) sentenced defendant to serve, inter alia, 15 years imprisonment at hard labor for the attempted forcible rape and 4 years for simple kidnapping. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was also sentenced to seven years for sexual battery, with the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant contended that his 15 year sentence was excessive because he was only 19 years old at the time of the offense and because he was a first offender. Defendant did not file or make a motion to reconsider sentence that alleged any particular grounds. He objected to the sentence as excessive after it was imposed. Thus, defendant was limited to a review for constitutional excessiveness. The appellate court held that in the instant case, nothing in the record reflected that the trial judge abused her broad discretion when imposing the 15 year sentence for attempted forcible rape. Defendant grabbed the victim by her hair and neck and dragged her to a canal bank. After forcing her into the backseat of his car that he had previously parked there, he repeatedly struck the victim while attempting to have sexual intercourse with her. It was only the victim's evasive maneuvers that prevented defendant from completing the act of rape. Further, the Louisiana Supreme Court held that a sentence of 17 1/2 years at hard labor was not excessive for an 18 year-old with no prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed. The case was remanded with an order to the trial judge to advise defendant of the two year prescriptive period for filing post-conviction relief and its time of commencement. In addition, the trial judge was ordered to advise defendant of the registration requirements within 10 days after rendition of the appellate opinion and to file written proof in the record that defendant received such notice.

Sanders v. Silverthorn


NUMBER 2003 CA 2726


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 2726 (La.App. 1 Cir. 2/11/05); 906 So. 2d 518; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 239



February 11, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Sanders v. Silverthorn, 901 So. 2d 1076, 2005 La. LEXIS 1490 (La., Apr. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Ascension State of Louisiana. Docket No. 2002-13115. Honorable William J. Knight, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Ascension (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellee, the natural father, and ordered that the name of the parties' child be changed to that of the father.


OVERVIEW: The mother of the child, not born of a marriage to the father, appealed a judgment ordering that the surname of the minor child be changed to that of the natural father. The court affirmed, however, stating that, according to the general prevailing meaning of the terms used and considering that the documents in question expressly outlined the construction to be given the father's signature thereon, the court could not say that the trial court clearly erred in finding that he did not intend to consent to the child's surname being the mother's when he signed the affidavit of paternity and the certificate of live birth. The parol evidence introduced at trial further supported that finding by the trial court. Also, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:34(B)(1)(a)(iv) substantially furthered an important governmental interest. Due to the large number of children born outside of marriage in Louisiana and the cost incurred by the State in establishing paternity and collecting child support, the State had an important interest in increasing the number of fathers who acknowledged and supported their children, thus reducing the costs borne by the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1328 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


04-1442 consolidated with 04-1470


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1442 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/02/05); 894 So. 2d 564; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 117



February 2, 2005, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR-487-2003. HONORABLE HERMAN I. STEWART JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: 04-1442 WRIT DENIED. 04-1470 WRIT DENIED IN PART; GRANTED IN PART; AND MADE PEREMPTORY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a writ application contending that the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana), erred in prohibiting introduction of evidence regarding a prior sexual assault against the victim, a minor child. The State filed a writ application contending that the trial court erred in ruling that evidence about a prior sexual assault would be admissible and that it waived the right to object to such evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of raping the victim. The evidence showed that the victim had previously been sexually abused by her grandfather. The appellate court found that the introduction of testimony concerning the causes of any alleged pre-existing conditions of the victim would be irrelevant; unnecessary to establish the facts sought by the defense; and unfairly prejudicial, confusing, and misleading. Also, evidence of prior incidents of sexual assault against the victim was prohibited by Louisiana's rape shield law. Thus, the trial court properly permitted general testimony regarding the potentially pre-existing physical condition of the victim, while excluding irrelevant and prohibited evidence concerning the alleged prior sexual abuse. However, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in ruling that the waiver by the State of its right to assert the rape shield statute could not be withdrawn prior to trial where the State apparently acquiesced to an erroneous ruling by the trial court and where the State had not even seen the documents from the Beaumont hospital. Thus, the State was not estopped from raising its objection based on the rape shield law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied defendant's writ. The appellate court granted in part the State's writ, permitting it to re-urge its objection to the Beaumont hospital records based on the rape shield law. The appellate court denied the remainder of the State's writ.

State v. Insley


04-1006


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-1006 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/02/05); 893 So. 2d 209; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 142



February 2, 2005, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF VERNON, NO. 65179. HONORABLE VERNON B. CLARK, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to attempted cultivation of marijuana and was sentenced by the Thirtieth Judicial District Court Parish of Vernon, Louisiana, to serve four years at hard labor and to pay a fine of $ 1,500 plus court costs. Defendant appealed and alleged his sentence was unconstitutionally excessive, and not particularized to him, and that the trial court erred in refusing his request for post-conviction bail.


OVERVIEW: The police went to defendant's house to arrest the individual who was living with him for a probation violation. While there, the police saw five marijuana plants growing in plain view behind the house; defendant admitted they were his. Defendant pled guilty to attempted cultivation of marijuana for the dismissal of the possession of marijuana and possession of drug paraphernalia charges. After the sentence was imposed, defendant filed a motion to reconsider his sentence, which was denied. The appellate court affirmed defendant's sentence and held that the sentence imposed was not unconstitutionally excessive, as the sentencing range for attempted cultivation of marijuana was five to thirty years and could not exceed one-half of the longest term of imprisonment prescribed for the offense attempted. Thus, defendant's four year sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. Further, as the court considered defendant's personal history including his age, family ties, marital status, health, employment record, prior criminal record, and the likelihood of recidivism or rehabilitation, the sentence was particularized to him as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence and the denial of his request for post-conviction bail were affirmed.

 

1330 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers


No. 2005-CA-0048


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


05-0048 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/01/05); 894 So. 2d 1185; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 296



February 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 2005.
Affirmed by World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 908 So. 2d 623, 2005 La. LEXIS 2092 (La., June 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2004-2404, DIVISION "E-7". Honorable Madeleine Landrieu, Judge.
World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 883 So. 2d 459, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2256 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 1, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxing district filed a motion for judgment in the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Louisiana. Following a hearing, a judgment was rendered as prayed for, and appellant taxpayers appealed. Subsequently, the matter was remanded for a full new trial on the merits. Following the new trial, the district court rendered judgment for the taxing district. Intervenor hotel association and intervenor individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxing district urged that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.21 operated as a suspension of law pursuant to La. Const. art. III, § 20. The appellate court disagreed. The appellate court found the law to be a special law, but found no reasonable basis for the distinction. The statute violated La. Const. art. III, § 12(A)(7) because the law exempted a facility to be operated as a hotel from paying already existing sales taxes imposed by statutes and ordinances, and it granted a private entity (the developer) a special privilege to use taxes imposed by the statute for private purposes. The appellate court noted that a classification of certain parties would not render a law special if it was based on a substantial difference between the class created and the subjects excluded, and there existed a reasonable basis for the distinction. Section 33:9038.21 was a special law, but the appellate court found no reasonable basis for the distinction it created. Section 33:9038.21 created an open-ended exemption from the present hotel occupancy taxes, and it was not uniform; it further violated La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D) by creating a special taxing district and political subdivision.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Peters v. GMC


No. 39,279-WCA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,279 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/26/05); 892 So. 2d 717; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 38



January 26, 2005, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 1W Parish of Caddo, Louisiana Docket No. 02-03307. Sam L. Lowery, Workers' Compensation Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee claimant developed carpal tunnel syndrome and, despite surgery on his right wrist in 2001, became disabled from work. Appellant employer paid benefits but stopped paying them after the employee took regular retirement. The employer's motion under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.8 to modify the prior judgment was denied but the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 1W, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana). The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that the claimant had been receiving supplemental earnings benefits (SEB) and that the applicable statute regarding his entitlement to those benefits was La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3). With the employer seeking to terminate a prior award of SEB, the issue was whether the workers' compensation judge (WCJ) erred in finding that the employer had failed to prove the availability of a job that satisfied the criteria set forth in § 23:1221(3)(c)(i). The claimant admitted that he had not looked for employment since retiring but stated that he intended to continue working in some capacity when his hands/medical condition allowed him to do so. The evidence showed he had not sought treatment for his carpal tunnel condition for some time and that he had likely reached maximum medical improvement regarding that condition. The WCJ had the opportunity to observe the claimant testify and found him to be a credible witness. The WCJ carried over that observation to its reading of the claimant's deposition testimony on the issue of his intent to retire/continue to work. The court was unable to say that the WCJ's choice between the alternative conclusions was clearly wrong.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the WCJ was affirmed. Costs were assessed to the employer.

Hudson v. City of Bossier City


No. 39,182-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,182 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/06/05); 892 So. 2d 143; 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1



January 6, 2005, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Hudson v. City of Bossier City, 899 So. 2d 574, 2005 La. LEXIS 1272 (La., Apr. 22, 2005)
Writ granted by Hudson v. City of Bossier City, 899 So. 2d 574, 2005 La. LEXIS 1273 (La., Apr. 22, 2005)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by Hudson v. City of Bossier City, 2006 La. LEXIS 1421 (La., Apr. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98,781. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.
Hudson v. City of Bossier, 823 So. 2d 1085, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2587 (La.App. 2 Cir., Aug. 14, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed, rendered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sued defendants, City, river boat companies, and parish school board, education fund, youth shelter, and a police jury, and alleged that defendants entered into contracts that directly contravened how monies generated by admission fees on the river boats were to be distributed. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, entered judgment for defendants, and the citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature authorized the local governing authorities, where riverboats were berthed to levy an admission fee of up to $ 2.50 for each boarder. In 1993, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:552 (now La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:93) was amended to specifically direct how the proceeds collected would be distributed. The parties designated to receive the funds from the two river boat companies in this action were: 80 percent to the City; 15 percent to the parish school board, and 5 percent to a youth shelter. 1995, the legislation was again amended to add another $ .50 to the boarding fee, with this additional amount to go to the police jury for widening a road and thereafter to be placed in its road fund. Defendants entered into contracts with the river boat companies that placed limits on the amounts all parties were to receive, except for the City. The appellate court reversed the judgment entered in favor of defendants and held that the legislature specifically delineated its intent as to how collected casino revenues were to be distributed. The subsequent amendment did not give defendants the authority to deviate from that method of distribution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court and rendered judgment in favor of the citizens and remanded for the trial court to redistribute the monies collected in accordance with the instructions herein.

State v. Girod


No. 04-KA-854


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-854 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/28/04); 892 So. 2d 646; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3166



December 28, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 16, 2005
Writ denied by State v. Girod, 903 So. 2d 455, 2005 La. LEXIS 1912 (La., June 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95-436, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN V. GRANT, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Girod, 867 So. 2d 672, 2004 La. LEXIS 496 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to reconsider after the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), imposed a 35-year enhanced sentence on his conviction for illegal possession of stolen things valued at over $ 500, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:69. The court had previously vacated defendant's sentence and had remanded for resentencing in defendant's first appeal, and the state supreme court denied writs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his enhanced sentence was unconstitutional because he was entitled to a jury trial of the facts found by the trial court in his habitual offender proceeding. Defendant was found to be a fourth felony offender with predicate convictions of simple robbery, possession of PCP, and possession of cocaine. The court noted that defendant had demonstrated himself to be a career criminal. His prior arrests comprised numerous felony and misdemeanor offenses. Thus, the record supported the sentence imposed. In addition, longer sentences had been held to be constitutional for similarly situated offenders. Defendant's sentence was only 15 years above the minimum 20-year sentence. The court failed to find that defendant's assignment challenging his habitual offender finding should be considered because it was challenged for the first time on appeal. In any event, his argument had no merit. Defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the three years and three month delay between his conviction and sentence. As a fourth felony offender, the sentencing range he faced was 20 years to life. Thus, he could not reasonably have expected any sentence less than 20 years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence, but remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to correct the habitual offender commitment for accuracy.

State v. Bonner


No. 39,187-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


39,187 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/22/04); 895 So. 2d 1; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3187



December 22, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Bonner v. State, 2007 La. LEXIS 589 (La., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 97-2935. Honorable D. Milton Moore, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court of Morehouse Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of second-degree murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment without benefits. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the State failed to meet its burden of proving his identity, the trial court erred in failing to admonish the jury following prejudicial statements, and his sentence was excessive. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the jury heard codefendant's testimony and chose to convict defendant mostly on the sole evidence of codefendant's testimony, which was well within the province of the trier of fact. While the prosecutor walked a fine line when he referred to defendant's failure to "come forward," the appellate court found that the statement followed his reference to defendant's own action of coming forward to police during the crime's investigation years later. The prosecutor was contrasting the pretrial actions of the two accomplices and their behavior, not defendant's failure to testify. Thus, denial of defendant's motion for mistrial was not an abuse of discretion. Considering that defendant committed the planned robbery of the victim, choked and brutally beat him to death with a tire iron, and then left his body to decompose in a cotton field, the imposed sentence was neither grossly disproportionate nor shocking to the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Winn

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of simple robbery after a bench trial in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. State v. Bertrand


No. 2004-KA-1496


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1496 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/15/04); 891 So. 2d 752; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3241



December 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 437-673, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.
State v. Bertrand, 874 So. 2d 905, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1129 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana) resentencing him to three years at hard labor after he was convicted of attempted sexual battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:43.1 and La. Rev. Stat. § 14:27.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually abused a minor child. As a result, defendant was convicted of attempted sexual battery and received nine months in jail and probation. Defendant appealed, and the conviction was affirmed but the sentence was remanded for reconsideration. The trial court imposed a new sentence of three years at hard labor. Defendant challenged the conviction contending that the resentence was excessive, was contrary to sentencing guidelines, and that his counsel was ineffective. The court noted that La. Const. art. I, § 20 expressly prohibited excessive sentence. The court concluded that defendant's sentence was not excessive, even though it imposed a longer term, because it contributed to acceptable goals of punishment, was not imposed to inflict pain and suffering, and was not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime. Furthermore, defendant failed to satisfy the two-prong test to show ineffectiveness of counsel. Defendant failed to show that counsel's performance was defective, and that he was prejudiced. Finally, the court held that the sentence imposed was fully within the sentencing range for attempted sexual battery. Therefore, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court resentencing defendant was affirmed.

 

1337 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spencer


04-857


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-857 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/08/04); 888 So. 2d 1128; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2991



December 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 03-187. HONORABLE ANN SIMON, DISTRICT JUDGE. HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), convicted defendant of two counts of armed robbery as well as attempted armed robbery and theft in excess of $ 500. He was sentenced to serve 20 years for each of his convictions for armed robbery, 15 years for his attempted armed robbery conviction, and five years for his conviction for theft. All of the sentences were ordered to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence contained in the record demonstrated that defendant intended to plead guilty to count two, alleging a second count of armed robbery, even if not captured by the transcript because (1) the minute entry for his guilty plea hearing stated that he was pleading guilty to two counts of armed robbery; (2) he was clearly made aware of the nature of the charges and the number of counts against him several times during his guilty plea hearing; and (3) he signed a certificate outlining the plea agreement, which stated that he agreed to plead guilty to two counts of armed robbery. Additionally, the appellate court found that defendant's sentences were not excessive because (1) there was no indication that the sentences imposed were a purposeless imposition of pain and suffering or that they were grossly disproportionate to the crimes; and (2) defendant substantially benefitted through the plea agreement as his sentencing exposure was reduced significantly. Finally, the record did not support a finding that there was an agreement between defendant and the State or the trial judge which would set defendant's sentence at one-half the length of his co-defendants' sentences.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for the two counts of armed robbery, attempted armed robbery, and theft in excess of $ 500. However, the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court with an order to amend the minutes of sentencing to reflect that the sentences for the two counts of armed robbery were to be served concurrently with each other and to the other two sentences.

 

1338 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Belle of Orleans, L.L.C.


No. 2003-CA-1203


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1203 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/01/04); 890 So. 2d 670; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3216



December 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 14, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Williams v. Belle of Orleans, L.L.C., 2005 La. App. LEXIS 99 (La.App. 4 Cir., Jan. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2002-14055, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an assessor for a municipal district, filed a petition for review of a decision of the Louisiana Tax Commission that reduced the valuation of a riverboat gambling casino vessel that was owned and operated by defendant taxpayer. The assessor appealed from a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) granting the taxpayer's peremptory exception of no right of action.


OVERVIEW: After the assessor valued the casino vessel for ad valorem tax purposes, the assessor's valuation was affirmed by the local board of assessors. On the appeal that the taxpayer took to the Tax Commission, the Tax Commission reduced the valuation. In the action that the assessor brought for judicial review of the Tax Commission's decision, the trial court determined that the assessor had no right of action either in his official capacity or in his capacity as the bona fide representative of an affected tax-recipient body. On appeal, the court ruled that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:1989 and 47:1998(C), the assessor, in his official capacity, had the right to bring suit on behalf of the state to protect the state's interest in ad valorem taxes. The assessor also had the right under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1998(A)(1)(a) to institute suit as the bona fide representative of the board of assessors, the affected tax-recipient body. The court concluded that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1998, which provided for judicial review of Tax Commission decisions, did not violate the due process rights that were guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the judgment granting the taxpayer's peremptory exception of no right of action. The court affirmed the part of the judgment finding that the statutory procedure for seeking judicial review of Tax Commission decisions was constitutional. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Brooks


No. 04-KA-779


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-779 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/30/04); 889 So. 2d 1064; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2903



November 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-2509, DIVISION ''P''. HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Brooks, 873 So. 2d 815, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1036 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 27, 2004)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, found defendant to be a third felony offender and sentenced him to life in prison without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The trial court later denied defendant's motion to reconsider sentence. Defendant appealed, asserting that the mandatory minimum sentence of life imprisonment was constitutionally excessive based on the facts of his case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 was unconstitutional, as the trial judge utilized facts not found by the jury at his underlying trial to enhance his sentence to life imprisonment in violation of Apprendi v. New Jersey. However, habitual offender proceedings did not charge a separate crime, but merely constituted ancillary sentencing proceedings such that the punishment for a new conviction was enhanced. As defendant's sentence was enhanced based on prior convictions, wherein he obtained procedural due process protections, and not any other fact, he was not entitled to a jury trial under Apprendi. However, defendant's case had been remanded from an earlier appeal. In reviewing the record, the appellate court found the trial court imposed a life imprisonment sentence under the mistaken impression that the appellate court instructed it to do so. Defendant was in fact "subject" to a life sentence as a third felony offender. But, because of the trial court's erroneous belief, and because the trial court failed to consider whether a life sentence in light of defendant's unusual circumstances was constitutionally excessive, remand was required.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence as a third felony offender was set aside, and the case was remanded to the trial court for a hearing and resentencing in accordance with law.
