State v. Divers


No. 38,524-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,524 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/23/04); 889 So. 2d 335; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2811



November 23, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Divers, 899 So. 2d 2, 2005 La. LEXIS 1102 (La., Apr. 8, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Divers v. Louisiana, 546 U.S. 939, 126 S. Ct. 431, 163 L. Ed. 2d 327, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7378 (2005)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Divers v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 114312 (W.D. La., Aug. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 46968. Honorable John Larry Lolley, Judge.
State v. Divers, 793 So. 2d 308, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1626 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 22, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, which convicted him of two counts of second-degree murder and sentenced him to two consecutive life sentences. Defendant's first-degree murder conviction was reversed due to the trial court's failure to excuse jurors for cause, and, on remand, his motion to quash the indictment was granted based on systemic discrimination in grand juror selection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, raising numerous points of error, including the restrictions on his right to cross-examine a cell mate and his accomplice and the admission of his plea discussions. The evidence showed that defendant and his accomplice murdered two victims after tying them up, taking them to a lake, and shooting them in the head. Defendant's tennis shoes matched impressions recovered at the crime scene, his fingerprints were found in one of the victim's homes, and the victim's car, watch, and jacket were found at defendant's apartment. The court rejected defendant's claim that the trial court violated his right to confrontation by refusing to allow him to cross-examine his cell mate or the accomplice, as defendant sought to question them on collateral matters and their testimony did not exculpate defendant or contradict their prior statements. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in allowing the State to introduce evidence regarding his plea discussions, because it was used to corroborate the cell mate's testimony about little known facts that could only have been revealed in a private conversation with defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted defendant of second-degree murder and sentenced him to two life sentences.

 

1341 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


First Commerce Title Co. v. Martin


No. 38,903-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,903 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/17/04); 887 So. 2d 716; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2754



November 17, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by First Commerce Title Co. v. Martin, 896 So. 2d 66, 2005 La. LEXIS 652 (La., Mar. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 37-135. Honorable Glenn Fallin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant title company challenged a decision from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of appellee clerk by determining that hand-held scanners were not allowed in the clerk's office.


OVERVIEW: An employee of the title company used a hand-held scanner inside the clerk's office to copy a map and other public documents while conducting a title search. The title company filed an action against the clerk when he objected to such use. The trial court determined that the scanners were not permitted, and the title company sought review. In reversing, the court determined that there was a constitutional right to the free access of records under La. Const. art. 12, § 3. This was codified in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:31. However, there were two exceptions for clerk's offices under La. Rev. Stat. § 44:32(C)(1)(c) and La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 251A. The court analyzed the plain language of the latter statutes to determine if the use of a hand-held scanner constituted the "placement" or "installation" of prohibited equipment within the office of the clerk. The court noted that both terms meant assigning or locating in a particular spot. A hand-held scanner did not fit within this definition. The court noted that the legislative history also supported this interpretation. Finally, the title company was awarded costs and fees under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:35(D).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The clerk was ordered to permit the use of the hand-held scanners. The court awarded reasonable costs and attorney fees to the title company.

 

1342 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Simmons v. Turner


NUMBER 04-374


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-374 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/17/04); 888 So. 2d 357; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2755



November 17, 2004, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 21, 2004.
Writ denied by Simmons v. Turner, 893 So. 2d 884, 2005 La. LEXIS 1172 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 33rd Judicial District Court [No. 2003-528], for the Parish of Allen, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Patricia C. Cole, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff children filed suit seeking damages related to their father's death while he was in the custody of defendant sheriff. The 33rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen (Louisiana), granted the motion to strike filed by defendants, the sheriff, the sheriff's department, and several deputies, because a jury trial was unavailable pursuant to the Louisiana Governmental Claims Act. The children filed an application for supervisory writs.


OVERVIEW: The children alleged that their father was denied medical assistance while confined in the parish jail and that the denial of treatment led to his death while in the sheriff's custody. In their application for a supervisory writ, the children contended that, even to the extent that the Act might operate to preclude a jury trial against the sheriff and the department, the Act could not be viewed as prohibiting a jury trial against the deputies. However, reading La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:5101(B) and 5102(B) within the context of the Act, use of "political subdivision" in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105 included officers or employees of that political subdivision, which included the deputies. Also, the children were not entitled to a jury trial in their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action, as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105 expressly indicated that they did not have that right, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not provide an independent basis on which a right to jury trial was conferred, and the Seventh Amendment's guarantee to a jury trial was not made applicable to the states. Thus, the children were not entitled to a jury trial on any of their claims against the sheriff, the department, or the deputies.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied the children's writ application.

State v. Howard


04-499 consolidated with 04-500


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-499 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/17/04); 888 So. 2d 375; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2753



November 17, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 21, 2004.
Companion case at State v. Howard, 888 So. 2d 385, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2775 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 17, 2004)
Writ denied by State v. Howard, 899 So. 2d 13, 2005 La. LEXIS 1106 (La., Apr. 8, 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Howard, 34 So. 3d 277, 2010 La. LEXIS 1048 (La., 2010)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Howard v. State, 131 So. 3d 858, 2014 La. LEXIS 286 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Howard v. Warden, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 79486 (W.D. La., Apr. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF LASALLE, NUMBER 67,007. HONORABLE JOHN PHILIP MAUFFRAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Twenty-Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lasalle (Louisiana), which convicted him of conspiracy to distribute a controlled dangerous substance. He also challenged the life sentence imposed under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant approached defendant about purchasing some drugs. Later, defendant convicted of one count of conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance. After sentencing on the drug charge, defendant was found guilty under a habitual offender bill. He was then sentenced to life in prison under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Thereafter, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that a statement made by one of the undercover agents was admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801(D)(4), even though the agent did not hear the conversation between the informant and defendant. In addition, defendant failed to object to the same testimony when offered by the informant. The officer's recitation of an accomplice's statement was admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801(D)(3)(b) because the course of events, coupled with the statements made by the accomplice, were sufficient to establish a prima facie showing of conspiracy. An ineffective assistance of counsel claim was meritless because the failure to object to two statements did not most likely result in the conviction. Finally, the life sentence imposed was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Green


No. 04-KA-357


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-357 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/16/04); 890 So. 2d 6; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2769



November 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-1245, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Amended, and as amended, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "G" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of two counts of distribution of marijuana. The trial court sentenced defendant to imprisonment at hard labor for 15 years on each count to run concurrently, with the first five years of the sentences to be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold an informant one-half pound of marijuana on one occasion and two pounds of marijuana on another occasion. Defendant argued that his 15-year sentences were excessive for a 26-year-old convicted of non-violent offenses. The appellate court found that defendant distributed a large amount of marijuana on two occasions. Additionally, the appellate court found that had the trial court given defendant the maximum sentence on each count and ordered them to run consecutively, he would be serving a 60-year sentence; thus, defendant received a benefit from the concurrent 15-year sentences imposed. Also, sentences in prior cases supported defendant's sentences. Thus, the sentences imposed by the trial court were not constitutionally excessive. However, because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(3) did not require that the first five years of defendant's sentence be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, that portion of the sentence was illegally excessive. Finally, defense counsel's affirmative response to a question by the trial judge as to whether defendant was ready for sentencing constituted a waiver of the required 24-hour delay in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court amended defendant's sentence to delete that portion requiring that the first five years of his sentence be served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. As amended, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Future Trends, LLC v. Rabito


No. 04-CA-525


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-525 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/16/04); 890 So. 2d 13; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2767



November 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2005.
Writ denied by Future Trends, L.L.C. v. Rabito, 896 So. 2d 40, 2005 La. LEXIS 439 (La., Feb. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 577-384, DIVISION ''N''. HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee company purchased a home at a tax sale and moved for summary judgment to confirm the tax sale against appellant couple. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "N" (Louisiana) granted the motion for summary judgment as to the husband because he had received notice but denied the motion as to the wife because she had not received the required notices of the delinquent taxes or the tax sale. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife argued that notice had to be sent to each record owner of the property and due process required that she receive notice of the tax sale, as a record owner. The company argued that either spouse was a proper party to receive notice of a tax sale of community property, so notice to either spouse was sufficient. The company contended it sent notice to the husband, so notice to the community was perfected. The appellate court noted that no statute clearly stated whether or not both spouses in a community had to receive notice on delinquent taxes due on community property. The wife was not listed in the caption of the act of sale; however, she did sign the act of sale as an owner. Further, the property was community property, so the couple each owned an undivided one half interest. Accordingly, the wife had an interest in the property and had to receive notice of the delinquent taxes due and notice of the tax sale. The wife had not received that required notice, and thus, the trial court correctly denied the company's petition to confirm the tax title. The failure to provide notice of the tax sale to the wife was a violation of her due process rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying the company's petition for confirmation of tax title in favor of the wife was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the company.

State v. Everett


04-808


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-0808 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/10/04); 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2672



November 10, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE FOURTEEN DAY REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Everett, 887 So. 2d 157, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3009 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR984-02. HONORABLE HERMAN I. STEWART, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of a firearm by a convicted felon in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, and with possessing a firearm while attempting to commit a crime of violence in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E). Defendant was convicted, before the 36th Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard, Louisiana, of the lesser included charge of attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a previously convicted felon, became involved in a dispute between his mother and three of her tenants concerning return of a rental deposit. Defendant allegedly threatened the tenants with a pistol, and he fired one or two shots into the air, or in the general direction of the tenants. On appeal, defendant asserted that the trial court erred in imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence. Trial counsel did not file a motion to reconsider the sentence as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann.art. 881.1. Counsel did, however, make an oral statement. This statement, as well as other statements made by the trial court at the sentencing hearing, revealed that the trial court, while aware of mitigating factors which would tend to favor a lighter sentence, was under the mistaken impression its sentencing discretion was quite limited and that the minimum sentence defendant could receive was five years. Because he was convicted of attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, there was no minimum sentence. Had the trial court realized that no minimum sentence applied, the trial court might have chosen to impose a shorter sentence.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded for sentencing after consideration of the proper sentencing range.

 

1347 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vollm


04-837


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-837 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/10/04); 887 So. 2d 664; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2676



November 10, 2004, Opinion Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF GRANT, NO. 03-324. HONORABLE ALLEN A. KRAKE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, AMENDED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to charges of obstruction of justice, aggravated burglary and theft in excess of $500, and two charges of attempted first degree murder. The Thirty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Grant, Louisiana, sentenced him to consecutive 32 years for each of the attempted first degree murder charges. He was also sentenced to five years for obstruction of justice and 15 years for aggravated burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers stopped the truck defendant was driving after receiving a complaint that it was suspicious. During the course of the stop, defendant began shooting at the officers; both officers were shot. Defendant later broke into a home where he was found by the police. Defendant's sole basis of appeal was that the sentences imposed were excessive. Before addressing the excessiveness claim, the appellate court reviewed the record for errors patent and remanded the matter for sentencing to be imposed on the theft charge, and amended the sentences for aggravated battery and obstruction of justice to be served at hard labor. With regard to the excessiveness claim, defendant did not raise any specific grounds; thus, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(E), the only issue was whether it was unconstitutionally excessive. Given that defendant shot two police, and the sentencing range for attempted first-degree murder was 20 to 50 years, the sentences of 32 years were not excessive. The court also held that consecutive sentences were not improper, as the judge stated the reason for the consecutive sentences was that defendant came very close to murdering two police officers.


OUTCOME: The sentences for attempted first degree murder were affirmed, but were remanded to reflect that they were imposed without the benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence and without good time eligibility. The conviction of defendant on the theft charge was remanded for sentencing. Finally, the sentences for obstruction of justice and aggravated battery were affirmed, but were amended to reflect that they be served at hard labor.

 

1348 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Myers


No. 2004-K-1219


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1219 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/03/04); 888 So. 2d 1002; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2865



November 3, 2004, Judgment Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 30, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Myers, 893 So. 2d 86, 2005 La. LEXIS 1167 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Myers, 893 So. 2d 85, 2005 La. LEXIS 1241 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 384-892, SECTION "A". Honorable Charles L. Elloie, Judge.
State v. Myers, 773 So. 2d 884, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 3003 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 6, 2000)



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellate court originally reversed petitioner inmate's manslaughter convictions; however, on remand, the appellate court affirmed his convictions. Subsequently, the inmate filed an application for post-conviction relief. At the hearing on the merits, the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "A" (Louisiana), denied the inmate's application. The inmate appealed the trial courts denial of his application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that trial counsel manifested his apparent lack of knowledge of criminal law and procedure, rules of evidence, and trial techniques. He listed 22 examples of trial counsel's ineffectiveness. However, the appellate court found that the inmate was either unable to show that counsel erred or that he was prejudiced by counsel's errors. Thus, the inmate's ineffective assistance of counsel claims failed. Additionally, the appellate court found that the inmate did not carry his burden of proof under Brady and its progeny since he did not show that exculpatory evidence material to his guilt was withheld, and that the suppression of the evidence undermined confidence in the outcome of the trial. Also, the inmate's argument that the felony-murder doctrine did not apply was essentially an insufficiency of the evidence claim, which had already been raised on appeal. Thus, the trial court did not err in not considering that argument. In addition, the appellate court found that sentencing claims were not cognizable in post-conviction proceedings; thus, the trial court did not err in not considering the inmate's claims that his sentence was excessive, and cruel and unusual.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the inmate's writ, but denied his petition for post-conviction relief.

McPherson v. Foster


NUMBER 2003 CA 2696


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003-2696 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/29/2004); 889 So. 2d 282; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2559



October 29, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by McPherson v. Foster, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3016 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Docket Number 499,088, Honorable William Morvant, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded; motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff senator alleged that the agreements donating property to the state were unconstitutional. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) granted the exceptions of no right of action filed by defendants, the governor, a state official, a company, and a non-profit corporation, and dismissed the senator's and intervenor wildlife organization's claims for declaratory judgment. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The senator alleged that to the extent the documents at issue could be interpreted as granting the company the mineral rights on state-owned land and water bottoms, the effect of the agreements would be an unconstitutional donation of public property. Moreover, the senator alleged that to the extent the agreements diverted to the company state income in the form of royalties on state-owned land, such diversion constituted an unconstitutional expenditure of state funds without an appropriation. Those allegations, if proven, would clearly have a detrimental effect upon the public fisc. Additionally, the senator also established his standing to bring the declaratory judgment action as a legislator because he averred that, through the execution of the agreements, executive branch officials had usurped the legislative duty of appropriating and budgeting the expenditures of the state. Accordingly, the senator's right to bring an action challenging the validity of those agreements was firmly established in the jurisprudence, and the trial court erred in denying him that right. However, the individuals members of the wildlife organization did not have standing to bring an action.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction filed in the appellate court was denied. Trial court's judgment maintaining defendants' exceptions of no right of action as to the senator's petitions and dismissing his demands with prejudice was reversed. Defendants' exceptions of no right of action as to the wildlife organization's petition of intervention was affirmed, but the dismissal of its petition with prejudice was reversed.

State v. Gordon


2004 KA 0633


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 0633 (La. App. 1 Cir. 10/29/04);  896 So. 2d 1053; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2563



October 29, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by State v. Gordon, 897 So. 2d 600, 2005 La. LEXIS 994 (La., Apr. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twentieth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Feliciana, State of Louisiana. Trial Court Number W-03-3-145. Honorable George H. Ware, Jr., Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twentieth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of West Feliciana (Louisiana) convicted defendant, pursuant to his plea of nolo contendere, of the amended charge of introduction of contraband into a state correctional institution, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:402(A). Defendant was sentenced to four years imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer was contacted by officials of a state penitentiary concerning two packages containing marijuana that were sent to an inmate. The packages were labeled as "legal mail." Defendant admitted to mailing purported "legal mail" to the inmate. Upon his admission, defendant's parole officer placed him under arrest for having contact with the inmate, a violation of his parole. The appellate court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions to suppress evidence because (1) there was probable cause to arrest defendant, and (2) no evidence was obtained as a result of his arrest. Also, the appellate court found that the trial court properly denied his motion to quash because the bill of information clearly charged a valid offense. Further, defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated. In addition, defendant was not entitled to a motion for change of venue as he failed to establish any reason why a fair and impartial trial could not be obtained in the parish where the prosecution was pending. Finally, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to recuse the trial judge since he failed to show or even allege any acts of bias or prejudice.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Taylor v. LSU Med. Ctr.


No.04-38944-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,944 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/14/04); 892 So. 2d 581; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2420



October 14, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by Taylor v. LSU Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3251 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 9, 2004)
Different results reached on rehearing at Taylor v. LSU Med. Ctr., 892 So. 2d 581, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 56 (La.App. 2 Cir., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 460,572. Honorable Charles Rex Scott II, Judge.
Taylor v. LSU Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2423 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 14, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed suit against defendant employer for wrongful termination. The First District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, rendered judgment sustaining the employer's exceptions of insufficiency of citation and service of process, and granted its motion to dismiss. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee challenged the dismissal of her case. The appellate court found that the employee failed to request service upon the proper agent within 90 days of the filing of her original petition as the proper agent was not served. Despite receiving a letter explaining that the employee had served the wrong agent, the employee did not act with haste to serve the proper defendant or agent. Instead, she amended her petition and requested service on the proper defendant eight months after the filing of her original petition. The employee's apparent later service on the proper agent through the amended petition did not change the result in this matter, as it did not cure the earlier defective service. As such, dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1353 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Savage v. Prator


No. 38,955-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,955 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/06/04); 886 So. 2d 523; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2370



October 6, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Savage v. Prator, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3403 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 29, 2004)
Writ granted by Savage v. Prator, 896 So. 2d 13, 2005 La. LEXIS 346 (La., Feb. 18, 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Savage v. Prator, 2006 La. LEXIS 145 (La., Jan. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 481,892. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two game clubs, sought a declaratory judgment and permanent injunction against defendants, a parish and the parish sheriff's office, after being informed that an existing parish ordinance against cockfighting would be enforced. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, granted a preliminary injunction but deferred a decision on declaratory relief and a permanent injunction. The parish appealed.


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:102.1 was the state statute prohibiting cruelty to animals and it explicitly stated that fowl were not defined as animals. However, the parish ordinance prohibiting cruelty to animals included fowl, and therefore, allowing cockfighting was punishable as a misdemeanor under said ordinance. The appellate court noted that since the parish had adopted a home rule charter, it was therefore governed by La. Const. Art. VI, § 5(E), and it could pass ordinances consistent with the 1974 Louisiana constitution unless denied by general law. Further, La. Const. art. VI, § 9 recognized the state's vital interest to define and provide for the punishment of felonies but failed to make such a provision concerning misdemeanors. However, the appellate court noted that implicitly, state law misdemeanors could be duplicated by local governments, but a local government ordinance could not contravene a state statute. The appellate court held the trial court correctly found that the parish ordinance abridged the police power of the state because the threatened prosecution under an unconstitutional ordinance presumed irreparable injury and impaired an existing property right.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty, before the Ninth Judicial District Court, Louisiana, to manslaughter and aggravated robbery charges. Defendant appealed.

State v. Adams


04-77


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-0077 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/29/04); 884 So. 2d 694; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2294



September 29, 2004, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Adams, 894 So. 2d 1131, 2005 La. LEXIS 537 (La., Feb. 25, 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Adams, 894 So. 2d 1132, 2005 La. LEXIS 540 (La., Feb. 25, 2005)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Batiste v. Cain, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 100703 (W.D. La., Oct. 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 93424, HONORABLE PATRICK MICHOT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, three brothers, appealed from a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which convicted them of second-degree murder after granting the State's motion to rescind the plea agreements on the ground that they did not testify truthfully at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were originally charged with second-degree murder, but pled guilty pursuant to plea agreements to the reduced charge of second-degree battery. The trial court granted the State's motion to rescind the plea agreements on the ground that defendants did not testify truthfully at trial. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court decision as to two defendants. The court held that the transcript of the plea hearing established that the factual basis was an integral part of the plea agreements and that defendants acknowledged that they understood their plea agreements were based on truthful cooperation and testimony. The court found that defendants failed to meet their burden to establish that they complied with the plea agreements, and the record showed they were evasive and untruthful. The court reversed the trial court rescission of one defendant's plea agreement, as his responses to the prosecutor's questions showed that the other defendant held and swung the knife and was the only one stabbing the victim. The court rejected one defendant's other claims of excessive punishment, ineffective assistance of counsel, double jeopardy, defective indictments, and misjoinder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed two defendants' murder convictions and sentences. The court reversed the trial court's rescission of the third defendant's guilty plea, vacated his conviction and sentence for murder, and ordered that his guilty plea and sentence for second-degree battery be reinstated.

State v. Lawson


No. 04-KA-334


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-334 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/28/04); 885 So. 2d 618; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2277



September 28, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 2004.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lawson v. State, 2005 La. LEXIS 2633 (La., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-2526, DIVISION ''E''. HONORABLE GREG G. GUIDRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of battery upon three different correctional facility employees while detained in jail, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.5, and was found guilty. Defendant was sentenced, but after a multiple offender hearing was found to be a second felony offender, and the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "E" (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to six years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The multiple offender bill alleged defendant was a fourth offender. However, he was sentenced as a second felony offender, as the court thought that a sentence as a fourth felony offender might have been unconstitutionally excessive. As a second felony offender, defendant faced a sentencing range of two and one-half to 10 years of imprisonment. Defendant argued that the trial judge had no basis for imposing the sentence. The pre-sentence investigation report (PSI) classified defendant as a third offender. At the time of the commission of the underlying offense, he was 51 years old. Prior to that time, he had been arrested for several felonies, in particular, attempted murder and attempted armed robbery in 1969. However, the PSI indicated the district attorney's office was not able to associate the 1969 charges with the arrest, and defendant pled guilty to a lesser charge and was given six months in parish prison. The trial judge imposed a mid-range sentence of six years. Under all of the circumstances, in particular, defendant's past criminal history, the appellate court found no abuse of the trial judge's sentencing discretion in imposing the enhanced six-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for the limited purpose of informing the defendant of the time period for seeking post-conviction relief and correcting the commitment to conform with the transcript.

Succession of Halligan


2003 CA 1168


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 1168 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/17/04); 887 So. 2d 109; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2133



September 17, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Succession of Halligan, 888 So. 2d 875, 2004 La. LEXIS 3882 (La., Dec. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 74,191, Division "N". Honorable Jewel E. Welch, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant beneficiary challenged a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of appellee Louisiana Department of Revenue by determining that the purchase price plus the earnings of a decedent's annuity was subject to an inheritance tax.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary filed a petition for possession in an intestate succession. The detailed descriptive list did not include an annuity. He later filed a rule to determine if there was any inheritance tax due on the annuity. After the district court determined that the annuity was taxable under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:2401, 2404, the beneficiary sought review. In affirming, the court determined that an annuity contract under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:647(B)(2) was not entitled to the same legal status as an insurance contract. Life insurance proceeds were excluded from taxation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2404(C). The annuity in question did not fall under the exclusion in § 47:2404(C) because it was not qualified under the Internal Revenue Code. The fact that an exemption for creditors for both annuities and life insurance existed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:647 did not mean that the two types of contracts enjoyed the same legal status for all purposes. Further, the Department did not act as a creditor in the context of imposing an inheritance tax on an estate. Finally, the court declined to address the beneficiary's argument concerning constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Thomas v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., Mun. Officers' Supp. Pay Bd. of Rev.


NUMBER 2003 CA 2271


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 2271 (La. App. 1 Cir. 09/17/04); 887 So. 2d 509; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2123



September 17, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. Docket Number 481,681, Division N(27). Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections, Municipal Officers' Supplemental Pay Board of Review (board) and members, sought review of the decision of the Nineteenth District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiffs', employees, and reversed the denial of the employees' applications for supplemental pay.


OVERVIEW: The employees were full-time radio dispatchers, and the board denied their requests for supplemental pay on the basis that they were not Peace Officer Standards and Training (POST) certified. The trial court reversed the denial of the employees' applications, and the court affirmed. The issue on appeal was whether the board erred in its interpretation and application of the eligibility requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2218.2(A)(1). The court affirmed, concluding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2405(C) clearly had no application to the stipulated factual situation herein. Rather, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2218.2(A)(l) was the applicable statute, and its application clearly provided that the employees were entitled to state supplemental pay. Because the employees were employed as police officers prior to March 31, 1986, they were not required to obtain POST certification as a requisite for state supplemental pay eligibility. Accordingly, the court found no error in the judgment of the district court, which reversed the board's denial of the employee's applications for state supplemental pay on the basis that the employees were not POST certified.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers


No. 2004-CA-1365


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1365 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/01/04); 883 So. 2d 459; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2256



September 1, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 2004.
Writ denied by World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 885 So. 2d 599, 2004 La. LEXIS 3265 (La., Oct. 29, 2004)
Appeal after remand at World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 296 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2004-2404, DIVISION "M-7". Honorable Paula A. Brown, Judge Pro Tempore.
World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 875 So. 2d 850, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1501 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 19, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor hotel association appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division "M-7" (Louisiana) denying in part its motions for new trial. The trial court allowed the association to address, in brief only, the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.21, and refused to hear any new evidence, but allowed the association to proffer evidence pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1636. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that the trial court violated its due process rights in granting a new trial without allowing the introduction of any additional evidence or the cross-examination of prior testimony. Specifically, the association argued that because it did not receive actual notice of the hearing, it was entitled to a full and complete new trial. The appellate court agreed that the trial court clearly recognized that a substantial injustice would result if a new trial had not been allowed. The only possible basis for the trial court's decision was that it believed the association had not received adequate notice of the hearing. Despite that conclusion and the trial court's statement that it desired "to place all parties on equal footing," it had refused to give the association a full new trial. Rather, it limited the new trial to argument (in brief form) on constitutional challenges only. That ruling was an abuse of the trial court's discretion, particularly in light of the statement in the trial court's corrected reasons for judgment that it found that the association had failed to clearly and convincingly show that § 33:9038.21 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court abused its discretion in granting only a limited new trial, and the matter was remanded.

Forum for Equal. PAC v. City of New Orleans


No. 2004-CA-1521


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-1521 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/30/04); 881 So. 2d 777; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2179



August 30, 2004, Judgment Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 10, 2004.
Writ denied by Forum for Equal. PAC v. City of New Orleans, 882 So. 2d 587, 2004 La. LEXIS 2572 (La., Sept. 2, 2004)
Related proceeding at Forum for Equal. PAC v. McKeithen, 886 So. 2d 1172, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2407 (La.App. 1 Cir., Oct. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2004-11325, DIVISION "C-6". Honorable Christopher J. Bruno, Judge Pro Tempore.
Forum for Equal. PAC v. City of New Orleans, 882 So. 2d 1172, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2093 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 24, 2004)



DISPOSITION: MOTION DENIED; AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Secretary of State (secretary), sought review of the decision of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiffs, committee and electors, and granted a writ of permanent injunction enjoining him from placing Act 926 on the September 18, 2004 election ballot. Plaintiff's further filed a motion to transfer the case.


OVERVIEW: The secretary appealed a judgment granting a writ of permanent injunction enjoining him from placing on the September 18, 2004 election ballot a proposed constitutional amendment, Act 926. Act 926 involved the proposal to the constitution that defined marriage as a union of one man and one woman. The court stated that the trial court erred as a matter of law in addressing the issue of whether the proposed new article confined itself to a single object. In light of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(C), the merits of the issue could only be attacked when and if the electors adopted the proposed amendment. Further, the legislature, by adopting Act 926, did not violate either the laws or the constitution of Louisiana when it set the election for the proposed amendment on September 18, 2004. Thus, the trial court erred in granting the injunction on that ground. Because the proposed constitutional amendment had no force of law, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3601, the record failed to disclose grounds for issuance of an injunction. There was also no evidence in the record of the legislature exceeding its authority in amending the joint resolution as originally filed.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' motion to transfer the case and affirmed the overruling of the secretary's peremptory exceptions of no right and no cause of action. The court further reversed the writ of permanent injunction.

State v. Brewer


No. 38,515-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,515 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/20/04); 880 So. 2d 1005; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2015



August 20, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Brewer, 896 So. 2d 27, 2005 La. LEXIS 400 (La., Feb. 18, 2005)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Brewer v. State, 896 So. 2d 28, 2005 La. LEXIS 401 (La., Feb. 18, 2005)
Related proceeding at State v. Grady, 954 So. 2d 183, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 343 (La.App. 2 Cir., Feb. 28, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Brewer, 964 So. 2d 383, 2007 La. LEXIS 2216 (La., 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Brewer v. Warden, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 158565 (W.D. La., Oct. 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 217,718. Honorable John Mosely, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of manslaughter. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. A witness testified that both she and defendant needed money. They discussed robbing the victim. She drove defendant to the victim's trailer and under the pretext of using the telephone. She witnessed defendant stabbing the victim. Although the witness gave five different accounts to the police of the events of the crime, in each of her accounts she implicated defendant as the actual murderer. Her false statements mainly centered around her involvement in the crime. Defendant's cousin testified that defendant came to her home on the night of the homicide to request her brother's assistance in changing a flat tire. Defendant offered her $ 20 to call her brother. The brother testified that defendant was in the possession of "a lot of money" when he came to her home. Blood found on the inside of the passenger's door of the car belonged to the victim, and defendant's DNA was recovered from the console of the car, the T-shirt, and the currency used to purchase money orders. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ellis


No. 38,740-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,740 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/18/04); 880 So. 2d 214; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1967

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which convicted him of two counts of molestation of a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2 and two counts of indecent behavior with a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences, but the court affirmed, stating that the evidence sufficiently supported all convictions. Defendant engaged in inappropriate sexual behavior with his seven-year-old daughter and the evidence was clear that the child was visiting with defendant and that he exercised control and supervision. Thus, molestation conviction was appropriate. Further, the indecent behavior convictions were proper because he permitted his daughter to view sexually explicit movies coupled with inappropriate touching and nudity. Defendant's behavior showed a pattern of exposing children, including his son, to erotic or semi-pornographic movies as a conduit for more specific sexual contact. A jury could reasonably have found under those circumstances that this wanton conduct was lewd and lascivious. His sentence was not excessive and the evidence of other crimes involving defendant's stepdaughter and her friend, who were six or seven years old, established identity, proved intent, guilty knowledge, motive, system, scheme, opportunity, and/or acts tending to show his "lustful disposition" in accordance with La. Code Evid. Ann. arts. 404(B) and 412.2.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Sweet


04-85


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


04-85 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/23/04); 880 So. 2d 43; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1851



July 21, 2004, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 94,410. HONORABLE KRISTIAN EARLES, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant got into his car, which he had left unlocked and running, and pointed a gun at him when he tried to stop defendant from taking the car. An unidentified person who saw the crime told the victim defendant's name and then walked away, saying that he did not want to get involved. The victim identified defendant in a photographic lineup and in open court. Although defendant argued that the victim was not occupying the car when it was taken, the court held that the victim's presence in the vicinity of the car was sufficient to establish that the car was in his immediate control; hence, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of armed robbery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, rather than carjacking under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.2. The identification was not overly suggestive, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it chose to believe the victim's identification testimony over that of defendant's alibi witnesses. Defendant's sentence of 30 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, given that defendant was a second felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

TSC, Inc. v. Bossier Parish Police Jury


No. 38,717-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,717 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/14/04); 878 So. 2d 880; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1827



July 14, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 109620. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a summary judgment from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana), which, in reviewing a zoning decision, ruled in favor of defendant, the parish police jury, and dismissed the owners' claims with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought rezoning of land on the edge of a heavy industry district for the purpose of residential and commercial development. Businesses operating in the surrounding heavy industrial districts opposed rezoning on the ground that residential and commercial development would not be compatible with the existing heavy industry. Following the denial of rezoning, the owners sought review, arguing that the police jury lacked authority to regulate zoning of the land. The court found no merit in that claim, concluding that Bossier Parish, La., Ord. 783 was not inconsistent with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:106.1 and that an amendment to § 33:106.1 allowed the parish police jury to regulate all land within five miles of city limits pursuant to the ordinance. Moreover, the owner did not show that the actions of the police jury in denying his request for rezoning were arbitrary and capricious. The record established that the decision to deny the request for rezoning was debatable and that considerations of public health, safety, and general welfare could have, and did, justify the denial. The zoning decision appeared to have been based on appropriate and well-founded concerns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment dismissing the action.

 

1367 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Newman


No. 2003-KA-1721


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1721 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/07/04); 879 So. 2d 870; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1858



July 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 2, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Newman, 2005 La. LEXIS 58 (La., Jan. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 380-770, SECTION "A". HONORABLE CHARLES L. ELLOIE, JUDGE.
State v. Newman, 840 So. 2d 536, 2003 La. LEXIS 775 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, (Louisiana) of first degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because the State did not prove the requisite intent. The court of appeal disagreed. There were a number of circumstances from which a rational trier of fact could have concluded that defendant had the specific intent to kill or to inflict great bodily harm upon the victim. First, there was evidence that defendant shot one victim in the head at very close range and that the same gun that was used to shoot that victim was used to shoot the other victim numerous times. The victim was shot with that gun in the torso, both from the front and the back, in the head, and in other areas of his body. Clearly, shooting the victim in the torso and in the head evidenced a specific intent on the part of defendant at least to commit great bodily harm. Further, defendant did not deny that he was participating in a drug transaction when the victim was shot. Therefore, even if the fatal wound were inflicted by someone other than defendant, defendant was a principal to the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Mitchell


No. 04-KA-136

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, convicting and sentencing him on a charge of possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Two men were walking across the street. Defendant dropped something to the ground "very discreetly." A police officer walked over and retrieved the object. Once police officers determined that the substance tested positive for cocaine, the officers had probable cause to arrest defendant. Defendant was not entitled to suppress the cocaine. The record reflected that defendant was not actually stopped until after he abandoned the cocaine. Since defendant discarded the cocaine prior to any unlawful intrusion by the police, the cocaine was lawfully seized. Upon his plea to possession of cocaine, the trial court sentenced him to imprisonment at hard labor for five years to run concurrent with his parole violation. However, the trial judge failed to state that this sentence was to be served without benefits of probation or suspension of sentence. This error patent did not require any action by the appellate court, because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:301.1(C) imposed these restrictions by operation of law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence was affirmed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for correction of the commitment as instructed in the opinion.

Ferrington v. La. Bd. of Parole


NUMBER 2003 CA 2093


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 2093 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/25/04); 886 So. 2d 455; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1623



June 25, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Ferrington v. 2005 La. LEXIS 2171 (La., June 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket Number 495,806. Honorable R. Michael CaIdwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment amended; petitioner's claims dismissed with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), dismissing his petition for writ of habeas corpus on the basis of his failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The inmate alleged the unconstitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.5, contending its application by appellee department of public safety resulted in a deprivation of his constitutional rights. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed, inter alia, that his claim was a habeas corpus application challenging the department of public safety's legal authority to place him on supervised release and to revoke his release, a claim not subject to administrative remedies. The appellate court agreed with the inmate that his claim was not governed by the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure (CARP), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq. The appellate court concluded that, while not a claim governed by CARP, the inmate's claim was also not one that could have been raised through post-conviction habeas corpus under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 362(2), in that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.5 had been upheld on numerous occasions and, thus, there was no application of a statute declared unconstitutional to trigger a true habeas corpus claim. Rather, such a claim involving a liberty interest or asserting deprivation of a constitutionally protected right was a civil matter over which the trial court retained original jurisdiction. However, even accepting the allegations of the pleadings as true, the inmate failed to state a cause of action, in that he was not legally entitled to the relief sought.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was amended to reflect that the inmate's claims were dismissed with prejudice on the basis that he failed to state a cause of action. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the inmate.

Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc.


2001 CA 2414


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2414 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/25/04); 885 So. 2d 1193; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1622



June 25, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 887 So. 2d 479, 2004 La. LEXIS 3555 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Writ of certiorari denied Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 887 So. 2d 478, 2004 La. LEXIS 3553 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Writ denied by Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 887 So. 2d 479, 2004 La. LEXIS 3554 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Subsequent appeal at Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1131 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 18th Judicial District Court Parish of Iberville. State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 52,211, Division "A". Honorable James J. Best, Judge Presiding.
Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1088 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 9, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate opinion reinstated. Trial court opinion reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a rehearing to review its previous ruling relating to a tort action. Ruling that a decedent's children were parties needed, the court remanded to the18th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana). On remand, the trial court overruled appellant corporation's peremptory exception raising the objection that appellee testamentary executor had no right of action. The action was then returned for review on rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The decedent brought a tort action against the corporation. The trial court had rendered judgment in favor of the decedent. An appeal was taken before the decedent died. The executor was substituted as a party. On original hearing, the court ruled that the trial court abused its discretion when it denied the corporation's motion to amend its answer to assert the statutory employer affirmative defense. During the oral argument on rehearing, the court noted that it was arguable that the decedent's surviving children, and not the executor, were the proper parties. The court remanded to the trial court, which overruled the corporation's peremptory exception raising the objection of no right of action. The court reversed the trial court's ruling. The court stated that the legal effect of construing La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.1, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 801, and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1519 together was that the decedent's death caused her legacy of the tort cause and right of action to lapse pursuant to the provisions of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1589(2). When the decedent died during the pendency of the case, the executor lost his legal capacity to receive the legacy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment overruling the corporation's peremptory exception raising the objection of no right of action and rendered judgment in favor of the corporation and against the executor. The court reinstated its judgment on original hearing and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The trial court was instructed to cause the substitution of the deceased's children as parties in the action.

State v. Moore


No. 38,444-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,444 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/23/04); 877 So. 2d 1027; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1560



June 23, 2004, Judgment Rendered

Writ denied by State v. Moore, 2005 La. LEXIS 1233 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 99-3554F. Honorable Wilson Rambo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana, which convicted him of second-degree murder and which sentenced him to life imprisonment without parole. The charge against defendant arose from a liquor store robbery in which the store owner was killed. A co-offender agreed to testify against defendant in exchange for being allowed to plead guilty to the reduced charge of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the jury adversely considered his decision not to testify when it requested copies of any statements by him and the co-offender. In affirming, the court held that there was no rational basis by which to conclude that the innocuous jury request indicated an improper consideration of defendant's right to remain silent. Furthermore, the jury instructions as to second-degree murder and manslaughter were not so incomplete as to preclude the jury's ability to properly consider manslaughter as a responsive verdict. The judge and attorneys had merely simplified the charge for the jury, to aid them in reaching a just verdict. Defendant failed to show that his trial counsel erred in approving the instructions or that the jury reached an unreliable verdict. Defendant made no showing that the State committed any constitutional error by obtaining a search warrant for a DNA sample without a hearing, nor by harvesting defendant's DNA at a time when his counsel was not present. Finally, the court found meritless defendant's claim that the State had asked leading questions to his co-offender, which prevented him from receiving a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Holley v. Plum Creek Timber Co.


No. 38,716-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,716 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/23/04); 877 So. 2d 284; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1571



June 23, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 2001-929. Honorable Sharon Marchman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parish police jury challenged a decision from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, several owners and two tax officials, in a dispute involving the tax exempt status of land designated as a wildlife management area (WMA).


OVERVIEW: One of the owners entered into a lease agreement with the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (DWF). The property was used for a WMA, which allowed for a tax exemption under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:24. A resident filed a declaratory action challenging the classification of the property. Later, the parish joined the action. After a motion for summary judgment was granted, the parish sought review. On appeal, the court determined that § 56:24 was not unconstitutional. La. Const. art. 7, § 21 stated that public lands were exempt from taxation. The court determined that the lease agreement demonstrated that the land was used by the DWF for a public purpose, which was the establishment of a WMA. As such, the property fell with in the public land exemption in § 21. However, it was unclear if the lease met the 25-year requirement of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:24. The agreement provided for a 25-year term, but it allowed a termination in 30 days by either party. The court found that this created an ambiguity as to the intent of the parties. As such, summary judgment was precluded on the issue. The case was remanded to determine the intent of the parties in executing the lease.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the judgment finding that a tax exemption statute was constitutional. The court reversed the portion of the judgment that determined that the lease complied with the 25-year requirement. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, Property Owners & Citizens of the Denham Springs Economic Dev. Dist.


2004 CA 1013


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2004 1013 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/04/04); 885 So. 2d 1153; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1467



June 4, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1549 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 21, 2004)
Writ granted by Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 882 So. 2d 1129, 2004 La. LEXIS 2789 (La., Sept. 24, 2004)
Reversed by Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 894 So. 2d 325, 2005 La. LEXIS 327 (La., Feb. 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Parish of Livingston, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 103,565, Division "C". Honorable Robert H. Morrison, III, Judge Presiding.
City of Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 872 So. 2d 469, 2004 La. LEXIS 1454 (La., Apr. 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Livingston, Division "C" (Louisiana), validated a bond issuance by appellee economic development district created pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.2 to fund an economic development project in the parish that would have facilitated the location of a retail outlet in the parish. Appellant opponent taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the taxpayer argued that the application of the tax increment financing statute (TIF law), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.1-9038.10, to the particular project under consideration violated certain constitutional and statutory provisions and that the alternative plan was not approved by all participating entities. The appellate court held that the fact that the project benefited private entities, either by disbursement of revenue bond funds to procure facilities for the use of private businesses or by the subsequent transfer of property so procured to a private entity for a nominal price upon retirement of the revenue bonds, did not render the project violative of La. Const. art. VII, § 14. Testimony at the hearing held in the instant case revealed the extent to which the project would economically benefit the parish. The district was comprised of undeveloped property that generated no sales tax revenue. Without the incentive plan offered by the state and local government entities to the shops to locate in the parish, the company might have decided against opening a retail center in the parish, and the district would have continued to have generated no sales tax revenue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. All costs of the appeal were assessed to the taxpayer.

 

1375 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Oestringer v. City of New Orleans


No. 2003-CA-2213


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-2213 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/02/04); 876 So. 2d 240; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1503



June 2, 2004, Judgement Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Reported at Oestringer v. City of New Orleans, 874 So. 2d 439, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1551 (La.App. 4 Cir., June 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION NO. 01-7222, DISTRICT "EIGHT". Honorable Sean A. Jackson, Workers' Compensation Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee was injured while working for appellee city as a firefighter. He obtained workers' compensation benefits, but shortly after the accident, he obtained his retirement pension benefits. The city then terminated his workers' compensation benefits. Pursuant to the employee's disputed claim, the Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC) approved the termination of his supplemental earnings benefits (SEB). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who had began his employment with the city in 1966, did not attempt to engage in any employment. The employee argued that the OWC judge erred in finding that he had retired from the work force and in denying him the maximum 520 weeks of supplemental earnings benefits (SEB) as allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(ii). The Louisiana Supreme Court had found the portion of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) that terminated benefits upon a claimant's receipt of social security old age benefits unconstitutional. However, the supreme court had expressly declined to consider the constitutionality of that portion of the statute terminating benefits when a claimant retired. The appellate court noted that an employee who expressed his intention to both retire or stop working and not look for other employment, and who made no effort to find another job, retired within the meaning of § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii). In such case, whether an employee "retired" was determined on a case by case basis. In reviewing the record, the appellate court concluded the employee did in fact retire. Thus, the OWC properly held the city was entitled to terminate SEB benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

 

1376 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


No. 2003-KA-1234


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1234 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/02/04); 876 So. 2d 912; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1522



June 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Lewis, 888 So. 2d 229, 2004 La. LEXIS 3662 (La., Nov. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 433-074, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of one count of attempted armed robbery, one count of armed robbery and two counts of attempted second-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred by permitting the State to try the charges against him in connection with two separate criminal incidents in a single trial and the sentence he received was excessive. The appellate court found that the joined offenses were triable by the same mode of trial. Further, the Williams criteria were met, and defendant suffered no prejudice from having the charges against him joined at trial; the facts of each offense were simple and each of the criminal incidents was a completely separate event with its own set of witnesses such that the jury would not have been confused by the various counts and would have been able to segregate the charges and the evidence. Defendant's sentence of imprisonment at hard labor for 203 years without the possibility of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence was not excessive, considering the crimes he perpetrated were abhorrent, he was among the worst offenders for whom the maximum sentences were reserved, he showed no remorse for his crimes, and one of his victims was going to suffer from permanent physical problems as a result of his injuries.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1377 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pickett


03-1492


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1492 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/26/04); 878 So. 2d 722; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1361



May 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Pickett, 2004 La. LEXIS 3550 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. LANDRY, NO. 02-K0437C. HONORABLE ALONZO HARRIS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.30.1, following a jury trial. The 27th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his shoes that he claimed were unconstitutionally seized without probable cause or reasonable suspicion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three detectives testified that defendant was cooperating with the investigation and that he consented to give up his shoes. The issue of consent turned on the credibility of those testifying and the weight of the evidence. The trial court had not abused its discretion in denying the motion to suppress. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in allowing expert witness testimony that reached conclusions that were solely within the province of the jury. The expert gave a summarizing opinion of the evidence before the jury and concluded that the State's theory of the case was the only reasonable explanation. Thus, the expert's opinion invaded the province of the jury and was in violation of La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 704. But, at trial, the physical evidence tying defendant to the crime scene was uncontroverted. Inter alia, his DNA was found in a blood smear on the panel of the door that was kicked in at the victim's house and his shoe contained a blood droplet with the victim's DNA and glass similar to the glass found in the broken window of the house. A reasonable jury could have concluded that defendant was at the crime scene. Thus, the expert's opinion was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Sarrio


No. 04-KA-89


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


04-89 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/26/04); 875 So. 2d 898; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1374



May 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 13, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Sarrio, 2004 La. LEXIS 3539 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-3301, DIVISION ''C''. HONORABLE ALAN J. GREEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Sarrio, 803 So. 2d 212, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2939 (La.App. 5 Cir., Nov. 27, 2001)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCES AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court of Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of one count of racketeering and two counts of possession with intent to distribute marijuana. On appeal, defendant's sentences were vacated and remanded for re-sentencing. On remand, defendant was re-sentenced to 30 years at hard labor on each conviction, to be served concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended his sentences were excessive and the trial court erred in denying his motion to reconsider sentence. The appellate court held that the fact that defendant's co-defendant received a more lenient sentence did not necessarily indicate that the penalty imposed on defendant was excessive. Further, the record established that defendant's involvement in the narcotics business was more substantial than his co-defendant's. Contrary to defendant's complaint, the appellate court did not find that the sentences imposed were vindictive; defendant neither alleged nor demonstrated that he was not free to accept any plea offers made by the State. Based on evidence showing that defendant ran a large-scale narcotics-distribution operation in which he moved significant quantities of marijuana on a regular basis, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing concurrent 30-year sentences or in denying defendant's motion to reconsider sentence. The trial court's advisal to defendant of the provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8 was incomplete.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed but remanded with instructions that the trial court inform defendant of the prescriptive period at the time of sentencing and to amend the commitment to reflect the trial transcript.
