Williams v. Webre


No. 2004-CA-0032


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-0032 (La.App. 4 Cir. 5/26/04); 876 So. 2d 858; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1507



May 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 26, 2004.
Writ denied by Williams v. Webre, 2005 La. LEXIS 397 (La., Feb. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 2003-1439, DIVISION "G", HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.
Williams v. Holiday Inn Worldwide, 816 So. 2d 998, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1761 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 15, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sued defendants, lawyer and law firm (law firm), for legal malpractice after her complaint for personal injuries was dismissed. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted the law firm's exceptions of peremption and no cause of action. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client hired the law firm to represent her in a personal injury suit for injuries she sustained while working as a security guard at a hotel and tripped over a decorative flower planter. The claim against the hotel was filed on September 19, 1997 and was dismissed on June 20, 2001, as it was immune, and the complaint against the other parties were dismissed shortly thereafter on the basis that the client's claim was barred by an exception of prescription. The client filed a malpractice action against the law firm on January 20, 2003. The appellate court affirmed the exception of peremption filed by the law firm and found the client's claims were perempted by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605. As the complaint against the law firm alleged that the law firm's negligence was its failure to timely add the other parties to the law suit, the malpractice claim would have had to have been filed by September 19, 2000. The appellate court also held that as the client failed to prove how she was denied due process of law, the right of access to the courts, or the right to petition for a redress of grievances, her claim that § 9:5605 was unconstitutional failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Greater New Orleans Expressway Comm'n v. Olivier

PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 575-033, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE KERNAN A. HAND, JUDGE PRESIDING.

DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, denied plaintiff commission's petition for mandamus against defendant judges. The commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge denied the commission's petition for writ of mandamus, finding that the judges had sufficient interest to question the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:57(G) (standing) and determined that the statute was unconstitutional on the grounds asserted by the judges. The supreme court found that the case was not properly before it and transferred the case to the court of appeals. The appellate court determined that, although it had appellate jurisdiction, because the trial court judgment did not declare the statute unconstitutional, like the supreme court, it could not rule on whether the trial judge erred in finding the statute unconstitutional. The appellate court concluded that the claim was still pending and the procedurally correct resolution was to remand the case to the trial court for a determination of the unconstitutionality issue and to issue a modified judgment to include his decision into the judgment denying the writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The commission's appeal was dismissed and remanded to the trial court for a determination of the unconstitutionality issue and to issue a modified judgment.

New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans


No. 2003-CA-1281


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1281 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/26/04); 876 So. 2d 211; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1520



May 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 26, 2004.
Writ denied by New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 887 So. 2d 475, 2004 La. LEXIS 3542 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Writ denied by New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 887 So. 2d 475, 2004 La. LEXIS 3543 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Writ denied by New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 887 So. 2d 476, 2004 La. LEXIS 3544 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
Appeal after remand at New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 980 So. 2d 760, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 332 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2008)
Related proceeding at Needom v. Robein, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 358 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 81-11108, DIVISION "C". Honorable Roland L. Belsome, Judge.
New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 788 So. 2d 1166, 2001 La. LEXIS 1237 (La., May 25, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-appeals were taken from a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which, in a labor dispute, awarded plaintiff firefighters' union a sum of damages, annual leave days, legal interest, additional pension contributions, and an adjustment to base pay to include all longevity raises that defendant employer should have paid.


OVERVIEW: The employer, a home rule city, argued that minimum wage statutes for firefighters violated La. Const. art. VI, § 6. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:1992(B), 33:1996 represented a valid exercise of the state's police power and were constitutional as applied pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 9(B). An amendment seeking longevity pay was prejudicial and did not relate back under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1153; hence, the three-year prescriptive period of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3494 ran from the filing of the amended petition. The trial court did not err in allowing a credit for periodic longevity raises. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1992(B) required longevity raises for 20 years of service after the initial three years. Supplemental pay was included in base pay for the computation of longevity raises. New Orleans, La., Civ. Serv. Comm. R. VIII, § 1.2, which limited the period of time for earned vacation days to be used, did not violate La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1996. Injured firefighters who lost scheduled annual leave were entitled to compensation. Pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 14, as amended, vacation and sick leave benefits were included in the calculation.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment with respect to the calculation of longevity pay. The court affirmed the determination of constitutionality, the credit for periodic longevity raises, and the validity of the vacation day limitation. The court reversed with respect to the calculation of vacation benefits forfeited by injured firefighters, and the court remanded for recalculation.

 

1382 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rhea


No. 2004-KA-0091


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-0091 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/19/04); 876 So. 2d 131; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1509



May 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Rhea, 2004 La. LEXIS 2742 (La., Oct. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 394-578, SECTION "E", Honorable Calvin Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to forcible rape, second degree kidnapping, and attempted armed robbery. He later filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, claiming that his attorney pressured him to make the plea. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied his motion. The trial court also denied defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence and to dismiss the indictment underlying the conviction. Defendant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: In the case at bar, the transcript from when the guilty pleas were entered indicated that defendant was represented by an attorney when he entered the pleas. The trial judge fully explained defendant's rights and questioned him as to whether the pleas were knowing and voluntary. The judge explained the maximum sentences that defendant could receive. Defendant said that he understood the rights and that he had no questions. Therefore, defendant's pleas were knowing and voluntary and the Boykin colloquy was adequate. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion to withdraw the guilty plea. Although the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to quash his grand jury indictment, defendant's substantial rights were not affected because he was indicted by a grand jury selected according to local laws. The error did not require reversal of his indictment, convictions, and sentences.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers


No. 2004-C-0572


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2004-0572 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/16/04); 875 So. 2d 850; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1501



May 19, 2004, Judgement Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 2004.
Remanded by World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 883 So. 2d 459, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2256 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 2004-2404, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE SHERYL HOWARD, JUDGE PRO TEMPORE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case arose on an application for writs directed to the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). Relator, taxing district, sought supervisory review of the trial court judgment granting defendants, the hotel and lodging association and the individual (intervenors), permission to intervene in this litigation.


OVERVIEW: In compliance with statutory provisions, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5121, et seq., the taxing district filed a motion for judgment seeking validation of the contemplated agreements, contracts, and transactions. The intervenors filed motions to intervene as defendants, opposing the taxing district's request as unconstitutional, as, among other reasons, it diverted public funds to a private property developer. The taxing district argued the lower court's ruling was erroneous because it permitted intervention after a final judgment was rendered. Yet, given the expedited nature of the validation procedure, the legislatively expressed intent to provide an equitable process with regard for the public fisc and rights of interested parties, plus the procedural exclusivity language in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5122, it appeared that the Louisiana Legislature implemented La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5126 to vest the trial court with discretion as to intervention to safeguard the rights of interested parties. There was no time limitation as to intervention expressed in § 13:5126. Also, there was no case law on point to confirm or negate the foregoing conclusion.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

State v. Allen


No. 2003-KA-2156


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-2156 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/19/04); 876 So. 2d 122; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1499



May 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 15, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Allen, 888 So. 2d 194, 2004 La. LEXIS 3441 (La., Nov. 19, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Allen v. State, 999 So. 2d 773, 2009 La. LEXIS 1855 (La., Feb. 6, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Allen v. Cain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 93045 (E.D. La., May 11, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS, PARISH NO. 442-008, SECTION "A". HONORABLE CHARLES L. ELLOIE, JUDGE.
State v. Allen, 800 So. 2d 378, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2487 (La.App. 4 Cir., Oct. 17, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's original conviction and sentence for second-degree murder was reversed and remanded for a new trial. Upon retrial, the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, again found defendant guilty and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant's motion for reconsideration of sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the evidence was insufficient to sustain the verdict, the trial court erred by allowing the admission of hearsay evidence, and his sentence was excessive. The appellate court found that an eyewitness's testimony describing the getaway car and positive identification of defendant as the person who killed the victim, combined with the fact that defendant hid in the attic when the police came to the house to arrest him, was sufficient to support the verdict. Further, even if information regarding defendant's relationship to his wife and mother-in-law was inadmissible hearsay, the admission was harmless, as any reference to defendant's relationship to his wife and mother-in-law was not a factor in the jury's decision; the jury had ample evidence upon which to convict defendant based on the in-court eyewitness's identification of defendant. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in not ordering a pre-sentence investigation, as it was not requested and the trial judge was required to impose a mandatory sentence. As second-degree murder was one of the gravest offenses one could commit, a mandatory life sentence was warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Brown


03-1747


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1747 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/12/04); 874 So. 2d 318; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1203



May 12, 2004, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Brown, 2004 La. LEXIS 3338 (La., Nov. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 01-389. HONORABLE KEITH R. J. COMEAUX, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES ANNULLED AND SET ASIDE; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted forcible rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42.1 and 14:27, and aggravated burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:60.He was sentenced as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by a bill of information with attempted forcible attempted forcible rape and aggravated burglary and was found guilty as charged. The State filed a habitual offender bill alleging that defendant was a second felony offender and he was subsequently sentenced as such. On appeal the court set aside and annulled the convictions and sentences, stating that since the record established that the trial judge represented the defendant on a 1987 charge of attempted forcible rape which resulted in a conviction, and that the 1987 conviction was admitted as other crimes evidence, the trial judge should have been recused pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 671(A)(3). The failure to recuse was not harmless error inasmuch as the trial judge was required to rule on the admissibility of that 1987 conviction, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 921. The trial court erred when it refused to give the jury limiting instructions regarding the proper purpose and use of the other crimes evidence as requested by defendant. It could not be ruled out that the jury convicted the defendant of the present offense because he had been convicted of committing the same offense in the past.


OUTCOME: The court set aside and annulled defendant's convictions and sentences and remanded the case for a new trial.

Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr.


No. 38,148-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,148 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/12/04); 873 So. 2d 841; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1167



May 12, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1658 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 17, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1659 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 17, 2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 894 So. 2d 1095, 2005 La. LEXIS 1974 (La., Feb. 25, 2005)
Vacated by, Remanded by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 894 So. 2d 1096, 2005 La. LEXIS 459 (La., Feb. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95383. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Judge.
Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 714 So. 2d 895, 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1634 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 24, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a medical review panel issued an adverse decision, plaintiffs, a former patient and her spouse, filed an amended petition against defendants, a medical center, the state attorney general, and a blood center, alleging strict liability for the use of tainted blood on the patient. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, granted the center's exception of prescription. Plaintiffs petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Ten years after receiving blood at the medical center, the patient was diagnosed with Hepatitis C. In a previous appeal, the court held that plaintiffs' strict liability claim was one of medical malpractice, making the three-year prescriptive period in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. ?? 9:5628 applicable. At issue in the instant appeal was plaintiffs' claim that the statute was unconstitutional as applied. The court agreed. Under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. 1, ?? 2, plaintiffs had a vested property right to file a damage suit in tort. A doctor testified that a person contracting Hepatitis C would not experience any symptoms for a period of approximately 10 years from the date of receipt of the contaminated blood. Such was the case for the patient. The court held that to enforce the three-year prescriptive period on such facts would have resulted in a denial of due process rights. Therefore, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. ?? 9:5628 was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings. Costs were assessed to the medical center.

Phillips v. Lowe's Home Ctr., Inc.


No. 2003 CA 0660


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 0660 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/28/04); 879 So. 2d 200; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1078



April 28, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court. Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana. Docket No. 132,729, Division "C". Honorable Timothy C. Ellender, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor filed a petition against appellee store to have the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana, annul a portion of a judgment rendered by a workers' compensation judge (WCJ), in a claim involving the store, wherein the WCJ stated the doctor violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 for performing an unnecessary surgery. The trial court granted the store's exception for lack of jurisdiction. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor treated the store's employee after the employee was injured on the job. The doctor performed a cervical diskectomy and three-level fusion at the C3-4, C4-5, and C5-6 levels despite the contrary opinions of three other specialists, who felt that the surgery was unnecessary. The store's employee sought workers' compensation benefits, and the WCJ found that the cervical diskectomy and three-level fusion performed by the doctor was medically unnecessary and unreasonable. The judgment stated that the doctor had violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208. The doctor filed his petition to have that portion of the workers' compensation judgment nullified. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's grant of the store's exception for lack of jurisdiction. The appellate court held that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(E), the Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation Administration had exclusive jurisdiction over disputes arising out of workers' compensation law. As the allegation that the doctor had violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 arose out of workers' compensation law, the court had no jurisdiction to hear the matter.


OUTCOME: The grant of the exception for lack of jurisdiction was affirmed.

State v. Armour


No. 2003-KA-1882


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003 1882 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/28/04); 874 So. 2d 304; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1127



April 28, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 438-236, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which imposed an additional three-year sentence, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:50.2, after she pled guilty to being a second offender. She had been convicted of purse snatching, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed, asserting as her sole assignment of error the trial court's imposition of an additional three year sentence pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:50.2, which provided for the discretionary imposition of an additional three year sentence when the victim of certain crimes of violence was 65 years old or older. Defendant had snatched the victim's purse. The court affirmed, however, stating that, given the procedural history of this case coupled with the fact the actual sentence imposed on defendant did not exceed the statutory maximum for purse snatching, the court found no due process violation occurred as a result of the trial court's expressly considering the victim's advanced age in setting the sentences. The court also noted two relevant factors. First, the State filed a pretrial motion to invoke the sentencing enhancement provision of § 14:50.2. Second, defendant failed to object in the trial court to her 18-year sentence, in general, and the constitutionality of § 14:50.2, in particular. The court thus found that defendant's argument that her sentence should be vacated unpersuasive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Walton


No. 2003-KA-1968


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 10, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 432-555, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery and attempted indecent behavior with a juvenile. As a third felony offender, he was sentenced to 12 years on count one, with credit for time served, and, on count two, to a consecutive sentence of seven years, with credit for time served. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, resentenced him to three and one-half years on count two, with credit for time served. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The mother and defendant's girlfriend agreed to go to a neighborhood bar. When the mother returned to the house, her daughters told her that defendant had touched them inappropriately while the mother was gone. He was arrested. At trial, the mother testified that defendant exposed himself to her children, raped one, and demanded oral sex from the other. Defendant was not entitled to present evidence of the rape victim's prior sexual contact, because he did not file a pretrial motion in compliance with La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 412. Defendant's sentences of 12 years of imprisonment as a third felony offender for committing sexual battery upon an 11-year-old female and three and one-half years for attempted indecent behavior with a four-year-old were not unreasonable punishment. The trial judge's failure to specify that defendant's sentences were subject to the restrictions listed in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1(C) did not require remand for correction; defendant's sentences had to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Walker


No. 38,254-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,254 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/07/04); 870 So. 2d 442; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 834

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Walker v. State, 45 So. 3d 1089, 2010 La. LEXIS 2173 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Walker v. Burl Cain, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82139 (W.D. La., Apr. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 217,971. Honorable Ramona Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of second degree murder. Defendant also challenged the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice attempted to rob a disabled man. During the altercation, the victim was shot in the head. Defendant fled the scene and attempted to discard evidence. After he was convicted of second degree murder and sentenced to life in prison, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that there was sufficient evidence presented to support the conviction. The jury was free to reject defendant's contention that the victim was the aggressor. Further, the evidence showed that an attempted robbery was consistent with the testimony of the accomplice and other witnesses. The court also noted that defendant gave an inculpatory statement regarding his role in the crime. The fact that the weapon was fired in close range of the victim's head was sufficient to show that defendant had the specific intent to commit the crime under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1(A). Finally, the court determined that the sentence imposed was not unconstitutionally excessive. The trial court was not required to give reasons for the sentence, and defendant did not show any facts that warranted a departure. Based on the facts, the sentence did not shock the court's sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed.

 

1392 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Nichols v. Cain


No. 2003 CA 1169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 1169 (La. App. 1 Cir. 04/02/04); 871 So. 2d 654; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 753



April 2, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Nichols v. Cain, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1353 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 19, 2004)
Writ denied by Nichols v. Cain, 883 So. 2d 1017, 2004 La. LEXIS 3059 (La., Oct. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 486,544. The Honorable Timothy Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate was convicted in a disciplinary board proceeding of being a threat to security and was sentenced to a transfer to maximum custody. He filed a petition for judicial review with respect to defendants, disciplinary board members, asserting their action was unlawful. He sought damages and an injunction. The 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, dismissed the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the relief the inmate sought was not simply reversal of his disciplinary board conviction. Rather, he sought monetary damages for the rights violation he claimed occurred when he was wrongfully convicted. His petition for injunctive relief, filed after his petition for judicial review, arose from an entirely different set of facts. The inmate's action was in fact a delictual action, which did not fall under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177, which governed suits for post-conviction relief or habeas corpus relief. The claims for which the inmate sought injunctive relief were subject to the administrative remedies procedure, and the inmate had to exhaust his administrative remedies prior to filing suit in district court. The inmate's action was governed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186, regarding proceedings in forma pauperis. The appellate court held that, because the inmate's action was not a proceeding for post-conviction relief or habeas corpus challenging the fact or duration of confinement in prison, a stay of the proceedings was appropriate under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1186(2)(b), because the inmate had not paid required court costs and fees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded the proceedings to the trial court with instruction to order a stay of his action until all costs and fees owed the trial court by the inmate were paid. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the inmate.

 

1393 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Odom


2003 KA 1772


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 1772 (La. App. 1 Cir. 04/02/04); 878 So. 2d 582; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 775



April 2, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Odom, 2004 La. LEXIS 3026 (La., Oct. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of Washington, Louisiana. Docket No. 01-CR3-81852, Division "A". Honorable Raymond S. Childress, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with aggravated battery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34. Defendant pled not guilty. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of the responsive offense of second-degree battery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1. The 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Washington (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to five years of imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction of second-degree battery. The appellate court did not agree. To prove a second-degree battery, the State had to prove that defendant: (1) committed a battery upon his wife; (2) without her consent; and (3) intentionally inflicted serious bodily injury. It was undisputed that defendant intentionally committed a battery and his wife did not consent to the battery. Moreover, there was no evidence to suggest that his wife did anything to physically threaten defendant that would have justified him in striking her repeatedly with the handle of a pistol and with his fists and feet. The jurors were charged with the law regarding simple battery, which did not require serious bodily injury. They were advised that they could return that verdict if the evidence did not support conviction for a more serious grade of the offense. For the additional reason that there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of the originally charged offense of aggravated battery, the jury's verdict of guilty of the responsive offense of second-degree battery did not entitle defendant to a reversal of his conviction.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1394 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Pontchartrain Materials Corp. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't


No. 2003-CA-1444


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1444 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/31/04); 871 So. 2d 1171; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 817



March 31, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 26, 2004.
Writ of certiorari denied Pontchartrain Materials Corp. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't, 2004 La. LEXIS 2638 (La., Sept. 3, 2004)
Writ of certiorari denied Pontchartrain Materials Corp. v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't, 2004 La. LEXIS 2640 (La., Sept. 3, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM 25TH JDC, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES. NO. 48-238, DIVISION "A". Honorable Anthony D. Ragusa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee corporation had filed an action against appellant parish for freight charges and lease payments. The parish now sought suspensive appeal of the judgment by the 25th JDC, Parish of Paquemines, Louisiana, that denied its motion for a new trial in favor of the corporation. The corporation cross-appealed the partial motion for summary judgment in favor of the parish that denied its claims for attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988.


OVERVIEW: The corporation sued the parish for the return of sales and use taxes paid under protest and claimed damages and attorney's fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and § 1988 on the grounds that it was deprived of its federally protected property rights. The parish had presented the corporation with a tax assessment for delinquent sales/use taxes, penalties, and interest resulting from the freight charges and leasing of barges used in their deliveries. The corporation paid the tax under protest. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the corporation and ordered the parish to return all taxes, interest, and penalties paid under protest. The appellate court noted that Plaquemines, La., Parish Ordinance No. 98-117, § 14-51 defined "sales price" in the same manner as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(13)(a). As § 47:301 did not provide for the inclusion of transportation and freight charges as part of its taxable base, then neither could the ordinance include freight charges in the sales price for the purpose of calculating sales tax. The corporation was not entitled to its attorney's fees as it was allowed to pay its taxes under protest and receive a refund.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the parish's motion for new trial and its grant of its motion for partial summary judgment.

 

1395 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of Broussard v. Watkins


03-1383


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1383 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/31/04); 869 So. 2d 962; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 703



March 31, 2004, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 98718-I. HONORABLE THOMAS R. DUPLANTIER, DISTRICT JUDGE. BROUSSARD MUNICIPAL COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 2002-157. HONORABLE CAROL SPELL, MAGISTRATE JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the owner of a gentlemen's club, sought review of an order from the 15th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which upheld an order suspending his occupational license for 15 days for violating Broussard, La., Mun. Code § 144. Plaintiff city had issued summonses to the owner for violating § 144.


OVERVIEW: The owner was issued two misdemeanor summonses for violations of Broussard, La., Mun. Code § 144. The trial court upheld the decision of the magistrate court suspending the owner's occupational license for 15 days. On appeal, the court determined that the proceeding was civil rather than criminal. While the purpose of the ordinance was to promote the protection of the citizens and to maintain peace, which was both a civil and a criminal objective, violators suffered no loss of liberty, incarceration, or fine. The court further found that, under either La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:1896 or 33:4788, the owner was entitled to a trial de novo by the trial court. The owner, as a defendant in a civil proceeding, was entitled to a trial de novo. Finally, the court held that, in light of its decision that the case be remanded for a trial de novo, the owner's contention that the city did not prove its case beyond a reasonable doubt was rendered moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for a trial de novo.

 

1396 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


LeRay v. Bartholomew


No. 03-CA-1370


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1370 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/30/04); 871 So. 2d 492; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 685



March 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 18, 2004.
Related proceeding at Leray v. Nissan Motor Corp., 916 So. 2d 260, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1600 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA NO. 557-708, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JR., JUDGE PRO TEMP PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AMENDED AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a treating physician and the Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund (LPCF), appealed from an adverse judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), after a jury trial on a medical malpractice claim brought by plaintiffs, a patient and her parents. Defendants also appealed from a subsequent judgment taxing costs.


OVERVIEW: The patient was rendered a quadriplegic after receiving medical treatment for injuries sustained in a traffic accident. The court found that the award of costs pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 970 was valid. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42B(1) was clear that costs in amounts over the cap were permissible. The trial court erred, however, in taxing costs to the physician. While the limitation of liability for a qualified health care provider was $ 100,000 plus interest, liability of LPCF was limited to $ 500,000 plus interest and cost. Special interrogatories sent to the jury were proper, and the finding that the patient was in need of future medical care and related benefits pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43 was noted correctly in the final judgment. The jury did not abuse its discretion in the award of special damages to the patient's mother for reimbursement of custodial care rendered to her daughter. It was harmless error for the trial court to keep from the jury the factual finding that there was insufficient evidence to meet the burden of proof for a finding of liability for the patient's damages against the driver in the accident or the hospital.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment taxing costs to name only the LPCF. The court affirmed the judgments as amended.

New Orleans Redevelopment Auth. v. Ovide


No. 2003-CA-0476


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0476 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/19/04); 871 So. 2d 396; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 795



March 19, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 19, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2002-10168, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MICHAEL G. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed a judgment by the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, that ordered it to cancel and erase from its rolls all taxes, health liens, housing liens, grass liens or liens of whatever nature or kind to property that was acquired from the taxpayers by appellee redevelopment agency through an expropriation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: A redevelopment agency had filed an expropriation suit against the taxpayers. The city was not a party to the proceeding, but monitored it after being served with a "Notice to Creditor" document. The agency's petition requested that (1) a judgment of expropriation be rendered and that the title to the property pass to agency free and clear of all encumbrances, reserving to the creditors, if any, satisfaction of their claims, to the extent possible, from the amount fixed in the judgment and deposited in the trial court's registry, (2) all liens of whatever nature or kind heretofore assessed and recorded against the property by the city be cancelled and erased within 30 days of rendition of judgment of expropriation, and (3) any such liens that were not recorded when the petition was filed be declared null, void, unenforceable and otherwise without effect, and that no such lien be subsequently assessed, against the property until the agency had disposed of the property. The appellate court reversed the order and held that as the city was not a party to the action, and never served with the judgment, the judgment was null as to the city under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1201.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was reversed.

 

1398 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Succession of Gonzales


No. 2003-CA-0823 CONSOLIDATED WITH: No. 2003-C-0537


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0823 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/10/04); 868 So. 2d 987; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 640



March 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Succession of Gonzales, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 984 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2002-18717, DIVISION "M". Honorable C. Hunter King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, son, moved to be appointed independent administrator of decedent's estate. Respondent, decedent's former wife, filed a petition to have the decedent's will probated and to be confirmed as the testamentary executrix. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division M, Louisiana, appointed an attorney not involved in the litigation as provisional administrator, and the parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The son asserted that the decedent died intestate, and the wife asserted that the decedent died testate. The appellate court determined that the issue was whether La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1608(5) was applicable to a testament executed in 1990. The appellate court found that the application of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1608(5), which was part of the revision law of successions adopted by 1997 La. Acts 1421, effective July 1, 1999, to the decedent's testament would fly in the face of long-standing law and jurisprudence. La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1608(5), concerning revocation of a legacy or other testamentary provision due to divorce, did not apply to the last will and testament of the decedent. The decedent's succession was not opened until after the effective date of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1611(B), and, at the time he executed his will, the legacy to the wife and the appointment of her as executrix was not prohibited under Louisiana law. The will specifically stated that the decedent desired to leave his entire estate to the wife, his then spouse, and that he desired the wife to serve as executrix. There was no evidence that the decedent wished to revoke the legacy and appointment.


OUTCOME: Denial of the wife's petition to be appointed testamentary executrix was reversed, and the case was remanded for the trial court to lift the stay of its order of probate and to proceed according to law with the appointment of the wife as testamentary executrix.

 

1399 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Yarnell Ice Cream Co. v. Allen


No. 38,263-WCA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,263 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/03/04); 867 So. 2d 969; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 425



March 3, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 1E Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98-00962. Honorable Brenza R. Irving, Workers' Compensation Judge.
Allen v. Fireman's Fund Ins. Co., 830 So. 2d 1120, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3345 (La.App. 2 Cir., Nov. 6, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant filed a petition and set forth an action for nullity seeking to nullify two money judgments rendered in favor of appellee employer previously rendered in a prior proceeding appealed. The Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC), District 1E Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, dismissed the claimant's petition. The claimant appealed, and the employer and cross-appellant insurer answered seeking damages for a frivolous appeal.


OVERVIEW: The instant action asserted that the OWC lacked jurisdiction in the first action to award money damages to the employer for restitution. After a contradictory hearing, the worker's compensation judge found the OWC had jurisdiction as a matter of law and dismissed the nullity action. The claimant appealed. His former employer and its insurer answered, seeking damages for a frivolous appeal. The gist of the claimant's argument in this appeal was that the OWC had no jurisdiction to award money damages except in awarding compensation benefits. The appellate court generally held that: the claimant's challenge to the OWC's jurisdiction and to the constitutionality of the statutes enabling the OWC to enter the awards, including his action challenging the subsequent award for damages for investigation and litigation, was barred by operation of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2005; the second action could be read as the court's reaffirmation that the employer's restitution action was within the original and exclusive jurisdiction of the OWC and that, because of art. 2005, the claimant had no cause of action in any forum to nullify the judgments resulting from the first action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the OWC's dismissal of this nullity action and awarded damages for a frivolous appeal.

 

1400 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Reno v. Scafco, L.L.C.


03-1232


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1232 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/03/04); 870 So. 2d 311; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 463



March 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Reno v. Scafco, L.L.C., 2004 La. LEXIS 2898 (La., Sept. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 96-3317, HONORABLE MICHAEL CANADAY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party challenged a decision from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee company in a negligence and strict liability action. The injured party also challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1671.


OVERVIEW: A piece of wood hit the injured party after it fell from a piece of scaffolding owned by the company. The injured party later filed an action against the company, which alleged negligence and strict liability. After its initial motion for summary judgment was denied, the company filed a motion for reconsideration based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1671. The injured party's attorney prepared a memorandum in opposition to the motion, but did not appear in court. The document contained a statement that the application of § 40:1671 was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection. After the motion was granted, the injured party sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the injured party had not preserved the issues regarding summary judgment for appellate review. The only issues before the court concerned the constitutionality of § 40:1671 and the procedures for attacking the constitutionality of a statute. The court found that the injured party did not notify the attorney general at the trial court level. Further, the attack on § 40:1671 was not contained in any pleadings. The memorandum did not constitute a pleading.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.
